https//bitly/2gSttKk, 4 In that city shining with the splendour of gems darkness like poverty could find no place prosperity shone resplendently as with a smile from the joy of dwelling with such surpassingly excellent citizens,ratnaprabhodbhāsini yatra lebhe tamo na dāridryamivāvakāśam |parārdhyapauraiḥ sahavāsatoṣāt kṛtasmitevātirarāja lakṣmīḥ || 14*
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 5 With its festive arbours its arched gateways and pinnacles 06 it was radiant with jewels in every dwelling and unable to find any other rival in the world it could only feel emulation with its own houses,yadvedikātoraṇasiṁhakarṇairatnairdadhānaṁ prativeśama śobhām |jagatyadṛṣṭveva samānamanyatspardhāṁ svagehairmitha eva cakre || 15*
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 6 There the sun even although he had retired was unable to scorn the moon-like faces of its women which put the lotuses to shame and as if from the access of passion hurried towards the western ocean to enter the (cooling) water,rāmāmukheṁdūn paribhūtapadmān yatrāpayāto pyavimanya bhānuḥ |saṁtāpayogādiva vāri veṣṭuṁ paścātsamudrābhimukhaḥ pratasthe || 16*
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 7 Yonder Indra has been utterly annihilated by the people when they saw the glories 07 acquired by the Sakyas’-uttering this scoff the city strove by its banners with gay-fluttering streamers to wipe away every mark of his existence,śakyārjitānāṁ yaśasāṁ janena dṛṣṭvāṁtabhāvaṁ gamito yamindraḥ |iti dhvajaiścārucalatpatākairyanmārṣṭumasyāṁkamivodayacchat || 17*
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 8 After mocking the water-lilies even at night by the moonbeams which rest on its silver pavilions — by day it assumed the brightness of the lotuses through the sunbeams falling on its golden palaces,kṛtvāpi rātrau kumudaprahāsamiṁdoḥ karairyadrajatālayasthaiḥ |sauvarṇaharmyeṣu gatārkapādairdivā sarojadyutimālalaṁbe || 18*
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 9 A king by name Śuddhodana of the kindred of the sun anointed to stand at the head of earths monarchs — ruling over the city adorned it as a bee-inmate a full-blown lotus 08,mahībṛtāṁ mūrdhni kṛtābhiṣekaḥ śuddhodano nāma nṛpo rkabaṁdhuḥ |adhyāśayo vā sphuṭapudarīkaṁ purādhirājaṁ tadalaṁcakāra || 19*
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 10 The very best of kings with his train ever near him 09 — intent on liberality yet devoid of pride 10 a sovereign yet with an ever equal eye thrown on all 11 — of gentle nature and yet with wide-reaching majesty 12,bhūbhṛtparārdhyo pi sapakṣa eva pravṛttadāno pi madānupetaḥ |īśo pi nityaṁ samaḍṛṣṭipātaḥ saumyasvabhāvo pi pṛthupratāpaḥ || 110*
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 11 Falling smitten by his arm in the arena of battle the lordly elephants of his enemies bowed prostrate with their heads pouring forth quantities of pearls as if they were offering handfuls of flowers in homage,bhujena yasyābhihatāḥ pataṁto dviṣaddvipeṁdrāḥ samarāṁgaṇeṣu |udvāṁtamuktāprakaraiḥ śirobhirbhaktyeva puṣpāṁjalibhiḥ praṇemuḥ || 111*
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 12 Having dispersed his enemies by his preeminent majesty as the sun disperses the gloom of an eclipse he illuminated his people on every side showing them the paths which they were to follow,atipratāpādavadhūya śatrūnmahoparāgāniva tigmabhānuḥ |udyotayāmāsa janaṁ samaṁtātpradarśayannāśrayaṇīyamārgān || 112*
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 13 Duty wealth and pleasure under his guidance assumed mutually each other’s object but not the outward dress yet as if they still vied together they shone all the brighter in the glorious career of their triumphant success,dharmārthakāmā viṣayaṁ mitho nyaṁ na veśamācakramurasya nītyā |vispardhamānā iva tūgrasiddheḥ sugocare dīptatarā babhūvuḥ || 113*
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 14 He the monarch of the Śākyas of native pre-eminence but whose actual pre-eminence was brought about by his numberless councillors of exalted wisdom shone forth all the more gloriously like the moon amidst the stars shining with a light like its own 13,udārasaṁkhyaiḥ sacivāirasaṁkhyaiḥ kṛtāgrabhāvaḥ sa udagrabhāvaḥ |śaśī yathā bhairakṛtānyathābhaiḥ śakyeṁdrarājaḥ sutarāṁ rarāja || 114*
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 15 To him there was a queen named Māyā as if free from all deceit (māyā) — an effulgence proceeding from his effulgence like the splendour of the sun when it is free from all the influence of darkness a chief queen in the united assembly of all queens,tasyātiśobhāvisṛtātiśobhā raviprabhevāstatamaḥ prabhāvā |samagradevīnivahāgradevī babhūva māyāpagateva māyā || 115*
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 16 Like a mother to her subjects intent on their welfare — devoted to all worthy of reverence like devotion itself — shining on her lord’s family like the goddess of prosperity — she was the most eminent of goddesses to the whole world,prajāsu māteva hitapravṛttā gurau jane bhaktirivānuvṛttā |lakṣmīrivādhīśakule kṛtābhā jagatyabhūduttamadevatā yā || 116*
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 17 Verily the life of women is always darkness yet when it encountered her it shone brilliantly thus the night does not retain its gloom when it meets with the radiant crescent of the moon,kāmaṁ sadā strīcaritaṁ tamisraṁ tathāpi tāṁ prapya bhṛśaṁ vireje |na hīṁdulekhāmupagamya śubhāṁ naktaṁ tathā saṁtamasatvameti || 117*
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 18 This people being hard to be roused to wonder in their souls cannot be influenced by me if I come to them as beyond their senses’ - so saying Duty abandoned her own subtile nature and made her form visible,atīṁdriyenātmani duṣkuho yaṁ mayā jano yojayituṁ na śakyaḥ |itīva sūkṣmāṁ prakṛtiṁ vihāya dharmeṇa sākṣādvihitā svamūrtiḥ || 118*
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 19 Then falling from the host of beings in the Tuṣita heaven 14 and illumining the three worlds the most excellent of Bodhisattvas suddenly entered at a thought into her womb like the Nāga-king entering the cave of Nandā,cyuto tha kāyāttuṣitāt trilokīmudyotayannuttamabodhisattvaḥ |viveśa tasyāḥ smṛta eva kukṣau naṁdāguhāyāmiva nāgarājaḥ || 119*
https//bitly/2gSttKk, kukṣiṁ viveśa sa jagadvyasanakṣayāya || 120*,dhṛtvā himādridhavalaṁ guru ṣaḍviṣāṇāṁdānādhivāsitamukhaṁ dviradasya rūpam |
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 20 Assuming the form of a huge elephant white like Himālaya armed with six tusks with his face perfumed with flowing ichor he entered the womb of the queen of king Śuddhodana to destroy the evils of the world,śuddhodanasya vasudhādhipatermahiṣyāḥkukṣiṁ viveśa sa jagadvyasanakṣayāya || 120*
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 21 The guardians of the world hastened from heaven to mount watch over the world’s one true ruler thus the moonbeams though they shine everywhere are especially bright on Mount Kailāsa,rakṣāvidhānaṁ prati lokapālā lokaikanāthasya divo bhijagmuḥ |sarvatra bhāṁto pi hi caṁdrapādā bhajaṁti kailāsagirau viśeṣam || 121*
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 22 Māyā also holding him in her womb like a line of clouds holding a lightning-flash relieved the people around her from the sufferings of poverty by raining showers of gifts,mayāpi taṁ kukṣigataṁ dadhānā vidyudvilāsaṁ jaladāvalīva |dānābhivarṣaiḥ parito janānāṁ dāridryatāpaṁ śamayāṁcakāra || 122*
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 23 Then one day by the king’s permission the queen having a great longing in her mind went with the inmates of the gynaeceum into the garden Lumbinī,sātaḥ purajanā devī kadācidatha luṁbinīm |jagāmānumate rājñaḥ saṁbhūtottamadohadā || 123*
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 24 As the queen supported herself by a bough which hung laden with a weight of flowers the Bodhisattva suddenly came forth cleaving open her womb,śākhāmālaṁbamānāyāḥ puṣpabhārāvalaṁbinīm |devyāḥ kukṣiṁ vibhidyāśu bodhisattvo viniryayau || 124*
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 25 15At that time the constellation Puṣya was auspicious and from the side of the queen who was purified by her vow her son was born for the welfare of the world without pain and without illness,tataḥ prasannaśca babhūva puṣyastasyāśca devyā vratasaṁskṛtāyāḥ |pārśvātsuto lokahitāya jajñe nirvedanaṁ caiva nirāmayaṁ ca || 125 (19)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 26 Like the sun bursting from a cloud in the morning — so he too when he was born from his mother’s womb made the world bright like gold bursting forth with his rays which dispelled the darkness,prātaḥ payodādiva tigmabhānuḥ samudbhavanso pi ca mātṛkukṣeḥ |sphuranmayūkhairvihatāṁdhakāraiścakāra lokaṁ kanakāvadātam || 126*
https//bitly/2gSttKk, khānnirmale ca vinipetaturaṁbudhāre || 127*,taṁ jātamātramatha kāṁcanayūpagauraṁprītaḥ sahasranayaṇaḥ śanakairagṛhṇāt
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 27 As soon as he was born the thousand-eyed (Indra) well-pleased took him gently bright like a golden pillar and two pure streams of water fell down from heaven upon his head with piles of Mandāra flowers,maṁdārapuṣpanikaraiḥ saha tasya mūrdhnikhānnirmale ca vinipetaturaṁbudhāre || 127*
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 28 Carried about by the chief suras and delighting them with the rays that streamed from his body he surpassed in beauty the new moon as it rests on a mass of evening clouds,surapradhānaiḥ paridhāryamāṇo dehāṁśujālairanuraṁjayaṁstān |saṁdhyābhrajāloparisaṁniviṣṭaṁ navoḍurājaṁ vijigāya lakṣmyā || 128*
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 29 As was Aurva’s birth from the thigh 16 and Pṛthu’s from the hand 17 and Māndhātṛ’s who was like Indra himself from the forehead 18 and Kakṣīvat’s from the upper end of the arm 19 — thus too was his birth (miraculous),ūroryathaurvasya pṛthośca hastānmāṁdhāturiṁdrapratimasya mūrdhnaḥ |kakṣīvataścaiva bhujāṁsadeśāttathāvidhaṁ tasya babhūva janma || 129 (110)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 30 Having thus in due time issued from the womb he shone as if he had come down from heaven he who had not been born in the natural way — he who was born full of wisdom not foolish as if his mind had been purified by countless aeons of contemplation,krameṇa garbhādabhiniḥsṛtaḥ san babhau gataḥ khādiva yonyajātaḥ |kalpeṣvanekeṣviva bhāvitātmā yaḥ saṁprajānan suṣuve na mūḍhaḥ || 130 (111)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 31 With glory fortitude and beauty he shone like the young sun descended upon the earth when he was gazed at though of such surpassing brightness he attracted all eyes like the moon,dīptyā ca dhairyeṇa śriyā rarāja bālo ravirbhūmimivāvatīrṇaḥ |tathātidīpto pi nirīkṣyamāṇo jahāra cakṣūṁṣi yathā śaśāṁkaḥ || 131 (112)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 32 With the radiant splendour of his limbs he extinguished like the sun the splendour of the lamps with his beautiful hue as of precious gold he illuminated all the quarters of space,sa hi svagātraprabhayojjvalaṁtyā dīpaprabhāṁ bhāskaravanmumoṣa |mahārhajāṁbūnadacāruvarṇo vidyotayāmāsa diśaśca sarvāḥ || 132 (113)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 33 Unflurried with the lotus-sign in high relief 20 far-striding set down with a stamp — seven such firm footsteps did he then take — he who was like the constellation of the seven Ṛṣis,anākulānyabjasamudgatāni niṣpeṣavaṁtyāyatavikramāṇi |tathaiva dhīrāṇi padāni sapta saptarṣitārāsadṛśo jagāma || 133 (114)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 34 I am born for supreme knowledge for the welfare of the world — thus this is my last birth’ thus did he of lion gait gazing at the four quarters utter a voice full of auspicious meaning,bodhāya jāto smi jagaddhitārthamaṁtyā tathotpattiriyaṁ mameti |caturdiśaṁ siṁhagatirvilokya vāṇīṁ ca bhavyārthakarīmuvāca || 134 (115)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 35 Two streams of water bursting from heaven bright as the moon’s rays having the power of heat and cold fell down upon that peerless one’s benign head to give refreshment to his body,khātprasrute caṁdramarīciśubhre dve vāridhāre śiśiroṣṇavīrye |śarīrasaukhyārthamanuttarasya nipetaturmūrdhani tasya saumye || 135 (116)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 36 His body lay on a bed with a royal canopy and a frame shining with gold and supported by feet of lapis lazuli and in his honour the yakṣa-lords stood round guarding him with golden lotuses in their hands,śrīmadvitāne kanakojjvalāṁge vaiḍūryapāde śayane śayānam |yadgauravātkāṁcanapadmahastā yakṣādhipāḥ saṁparivārya tasthuḥ || 136 (117)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 37 The gods in homage to the son of Māyā with their heads bowed at his majesty held up a white umbrella in the sky and muttered the highest blessings on his supreme wisdom,māyātanūjasya divaukasaḥ khe yasya prabhāvātpraṇataiḥ śirobhiḥ |ādhārayan pāṇdaramātapatraṁ bodhāya jepuḥ paramāśiṣaśca || 137 (118)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 38 The great dragons 21 in their great thirst for the Law 22 — they who had had the privilege of waiting on the past Buddhas — gazing with eyes of intent devotion fanned 23 him and strewed Mandāra flowers over him,mahoragā dharmaviśeṣatarṣādbuddheṣvatīteṣu kṛtādhikārāḥ |yamavyajan bhaktiviśiṣṭanetrā maṁdārapuṣpaiḥ samavākiraṁśca || 138 (119)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 39 Gladdened through the influence of the birth of the Tathāgata the gods of pure natures and inhabiting pure abodes 24 were filled with joy though all passion was extinguished for the sake of the world 25 drowned in sorrow,tathāgatotpādaguṇena tuṣṭāḥ śuddhādhivāsāśca viśuddhasattvāḥ |devā nanaṁdurvigate pi rāge magnasya duḥkhe jagato hitāya || 139 (120)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 40 When he was born the earth though fastened down by (Himālaya) the monarch of mountains shook like a ship tossed by the wind and from a cloudless sky there fell a shower full of lotuses and water-lilies and perfumed with sandalwood,yasmin prasūte girirājakīlā vātāhatā nauriva bhūścacāla |sacaṁdanā cotpalapadmagarbhā papāta vṛṣṭirgagaṇādanabhrāt || 140 (121)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 41 Pleasant breezes blew soft to the touch dropping down heavenly garments the very sun though still the same shone with augmented light and fire gleamed unstirred with a gentle lustre,vātā vavuḥ sparśasukhā manojñā divyāni vāsāṁsyavapātayaṁtaḥ |sūryaḥ sa evābhyadhikaṁ cakāśe jajvāla saumyārciranīrito gniḥ || 141 (122)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 42 In the north-eastern part of the dwelling a well of pure water appeared of its own accord wherein the inhabitants of the gynaeceum filled with wonder performed their rites as in a sacred bathing-place,prāguttare cāvasathapradeśe kūpaḥ svayaṁ prādurabhūtsitāṁbuḥ |aṁtaḥ purāṇyāgatavismayāni yasmin kriyāstīrtha iva pracakruḥ || 142 (123)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 43 Through the troops of heavenly visitants who came seeking religious merit the pool itself received strength to behold Buddha and by means of its trees bearing flowers and perfumes it eagerly offered him worship,dharmārthibhirbhūtagaṇaiśca divyaistaddarśanārthaṁ balamāpa pūraḥ |kautūhalenaiva ca pādapaiśca prapūjayāmāsa sagaṁdhapuṣpaiḥ || 143 (124)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 44 The flowering trees at once produced their blossoms while their fragrance was borne aloft in all directions by the wind accompanied by the songs of bewildered female bees while the air was inhaled and absorbed by the many snakes (gathering near) 26,puṣpadumāḥ svaṁ kusumaṁ pukulluḥ sasīraṇodrāmitadiksugaṁdhi |susaṁbhramadnṛgavadhūpagītaṁ bhujaṁgaṁvṛdāpihitāttavātam || 144*
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 45 Sometimes there resounded 27 on both sides songs mingled with musical instruments and tabours and lutes also drums tambourines and the rest from women adorned with dancing bracelets,kvacit kvaṇattūryamṛdaṁgagītairvīṇāmukuṁdāmurajādibhiśca |svīṇāṁ calatkuṁḍalabhūṣitānāṁ virājitaṁ cobhayapārścatastat || 145*
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 46 28That royal law which neither Bhṛgu nor Aṅgiras ever made those two great seers the founders of families their two sons Śukra and Vṛhaspati left revealed at the end,yadrājaśāstraṁ bhṛguraṁgirā vā na cakraturvaṁśakarāvṛṣī tau |tayoḥ sutau tau ca sasarjatustatkālena śukraśca bṛhaspatiśca || 146 (141)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 47 Yea the son of Sarasvatī 29 I proclaimed that lost Veda which they had never seen in former ages — Vyāsa rehearsed that in many forms which Vaśiṣṭha helpless could not compile,sārasvataścāpi jagāda naṣṭaṁ vedaṁ punaryaṁ dadṛśurna pūrvam |vyāsastathainaṁ bahudhā cakāra na yaṁ vaśiṣṭhaḥ kṛtavānaśaktiḥ || 147 (142)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 48 The voice of Vālmīki uttered its poetry which the great seer Cyavana could not compose and that medicine which Atri never invented the wise son of Atri 30 proclaimed after him,vālmīkinādaśca sasarja padyaṁ jagraṁtha yanna cyavano mahārṣiḥ |cikitsitaṁ yacca cakāra nātriḥ paścāttadātreya ṛṣirjagāda || 148 (143)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 49 That Brahmanhood which Kuśika never attained — his son O king found out the means to gain it (so) Sagara made a bound for the ocean which even the Ikṣvākus had not fixed before him,yacca dvijatvaṁ kuśiko na lebhe tadgādhanaḥ sūnuravāpa rājan |velāṁ samudre sagaraśca dadhre nekṣvākavo yāṁ prathamaṁ babaṁdhuḥ || 149 (144)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 50 Janaka attained a power of instructing the twice-born in the rules of Yoga which none other had ever reached 31 and the famed feats of the grandson of Śūra 32 (Kriṣṇa) Śūra and his peers were powerless to accomplish,ācāryakaṁ yogavidhau dvijānāmaprāptamanyairjanako jagāma |khyātāni karmāṇi ca yāni śauraiḥ śūrādayasteṣvabalā babhūvuḥ || 150 (145)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 51 Therefore it is not age nor years which are the criterion different persons win pre-eminence in the world at different places those mighty exploits worthy of kings and sages when left undone by the ancestors have been done by the sons’,tasmātpramāṇaṁ na vayo na kālaḥ kaścitkvacicchraiṣṭhyamupaiti loke |rājñāmṛṣīṇāṁ ca hitāni tāni kṛtāni putrairakṛtāni pūrvaiḥ || 151 (146)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 52 The king being thus consoled and congratulated by those well-trusted Brāhmans dismissed from his mind all unwelcome suspicion and rose to a still higher degree of joy,evaṁ nṛpaḥ pratyayitairdvijaistairāśvāsitaścāpyabhinaṁditaśca |śaṁkāmaniṣṭāṁ vijahau manastaḥ praharṣamevādhikamāruroha || 152 (147)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 53 And well-pleased he gave to those most excellent of the twice-born rich treasures with all due honour — May he become the ruler of the earth according to your words and may he retire to the woods when he attains old age’,prītaśca tebhyo dvijasattamebhyaḥ satkārapūrvaṁ pradadau dhanāni |bhūyādayaṁ bhūmipatiryathokto yāyājjarāmetya vanāni ceti || 153 (148)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 54 Then having learned by signs and through the power of his penances this birth of him who was to destroy all birth the great seer Asita in his thirst for the excellent Law 33 came to the palace of the Śākya king,athau nimittaiśca tapobalācca tajjanma janmāṁtakarasya buddhvā |śākyeśvarasyālayamājagāma saddharmatarṣādasito mahārṣiḥ || 154 (149)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 55 Him shining with the glory of sacred knowledge and ascetic observances the king’s own priest — himself a special student among the students of sacred knowledge — introduced into the royal palace with all due reverence and respect,taṁ brahmavidbrahmavidāṁ jvalaṁtaṁ brāhmyā śriyā caiva tapaḥśriyā ca |rājño gururgauravasatkriyābhyāṁ praveśayāmāsa nareṁdrasadma || 155 (150)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 56 He entered into the precincts of the king’s gynaeceum which was all astir with the joy arisen from the birth of the young prince — grave from his consciousness of power his pre-eminence in asceticism and the weight of old age,sa pārthivāṁtaḥpurasaṁnikarṣaṁ kumārajanmāgataharṣavegam |viveśa dhīro balasaṁjñayaiva tapaḥprakarṣācca jarāśrayācca || 156 (151)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 57 Then the king having duly honoured the sage who was seated in his seat with water for the feet and an arghya offering invited him (to speak) with all ceremonies of respect as did Antideva 34 in olden time to Vaśiṣṭha,tato nṛpastaṁ munimāsanasthaṁ pādyārghyapūrvaṁ pratipūjya samyak |nimaṁtrayāmāsa yathopacāraṁ purā vasiṣṭhaṁ sa ivāṁtidevaḥ || 157 (152)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 58 I am indeed fortunate this my family is the object of high favour that thou shouldst have come to visit me be pleased to command what I should do O benign one I am thy disciple be pleased to show thy confidence in me’,dhanyo smyanugrāhyamidaṁ kulaṁ me yanmāṁ didṛkṣurbhagavānupetaḥ |ājñāpyatāṁ kiṁ karavāṇi saumya śiṣyo smi viśraṁbhitumarhasīti || 158 (153)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 59 The sage being thus invited by the king filled with intense feeling as was due uttered his deep and solemn words having his large eyes opened wide with wonder,evaṁ nṛpeṇopanimaṁtritaḥ sansarveṇa bhāvena muniryathāvat |savismayotphullaviśāladṛṣṭirgaṁbhīradhīrāṇi vacāṁsyuvāca || 159 (154)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 60 This is indeed worthy of thee great-souled as thou art fond of guests liberal and a lover of duty — that thy mind should be thus kind towards me in full accordance with thy nature family wisdom and age,mahātmani tvayyupapannametat priyātithau tyāgini dharmakāme |sattvānvayajñānavayo nurūpā snigdhā yadevaṁ mayi te matiḥ syāt || 160 (155)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 61 This is the true way in which those seer kings of old rejecting through duty all trivial riches 35 have ever flung them away as was right — being poor in outward substance but rich in ascetic endurance,etacca tadyena nṛparṣayaste dharmeṇa sūkṣmāṇi dhanānyapāsya |nityaṁ tyajaṁto vidhivadbabhūvustapobhirāḍhyā vibhavairdaridrāḥ || 161 (156)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 62 But hear now the motive for my coming and rejoice thereat a heavenly voice has been heard by me in the heavenly path that thy son has been born for the sake of supreme knowledge,prayojanaṁ yattu mamopayāne tanme śṛṇu prītimupehi ca tvam |divyā mayā divyapathe śrutā vāgbodhāya jātastanayastaveti || 162 (157)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 63 Having heard that voice and applied my mind thereto and having known its truth by signs I am now come hither with a longing to see the banner of the Śākya race as if it were Indra’s banner being set up’ 36,śrutvā vacastacca manaśca yuktvā jñātvā nimittaiśca tato smyupetaḥ |didṛkṣayā śākyakuladhvajasya śakradhvajasyeva samucchritasya || 163 (158)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 64 Having heard this address of his the king with his steps bewildered with joy took the prince who lay on his nurse’s side and showed him to the holy ascetic,ityetadevaṁ vacanaṁ niśamya praharṣasaṁbhrāṁtagatirnareṁdraḥ |ādāya dhātryaṁkagataṁ kumāraṁ saṁdarśayāmāsa tapodhanāya || 164 (159)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 65 Thus the great seer beheld the king’s son with wonder — his foot marked with a wheel his fingers and toes webbed with a circle of hair between his eyebrows and signs of vigour like an elephant,cakrāṁkapādaṁ sa tathā mahārṣirjālāvanaddhāṁgulipāṇipādam |sorṇabhruvaṁ vāraṇavastikośaṁ savismayaṁ rājasutaṁ dadarśa || 165 (160)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 66 Having beheld him seated on his nurse’s side like the son of Agni (Skanda) seated on Devī’s side he stood with the tears hanging on the ends of his eyelashes 37 and sighing he looked up towards heaven,dhātryaṁkasaṁviṣṭamavekṣya cainaṁ devyaṁkasaṁviṣṭamivāgnisūnum |babhūva pakṣmāṁtarivāṁcitāśrurniśvasya caivaṁ tridivonmukho bhūt || 166 (161)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 67 But seeing Asita with his eyes thus filled with tears the king was agitated through his love for his son and with his hands clasped and his body bowed he thus asked him in a broken voice choked with weeping,dṛṣṭvāsitaṁ tvaśrupariplutākṣaṁ snehāttu putrasya nṛpaścakaṁpe |sagadgadaṁ bāṣpakaṣāyakaṁṭhaḥ papraccha ca prāṁjalirānatāṁgaḥ || 167 (162)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 68 One whose beauty has little to distinguish it from that of a divine sage 38 and whose brilliant birth has been so wonderful and for whom thou hast prophesied a transcendent future — wherefore on seeing him do tears come to thee O reverend one,svalpāṁtaraṁ yasya vapurmuneḥ syādbahvadbhutaṁ yasya ca janma dīptam |yasyottamaṁ bhāvinamāttha cārthaṁ taṁ prekṣya kasmāttava dhīra vāṣpaḥ || 168 (163)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 69 Is the prince O holy man destined to a long life Surely he cannot be born for my sorrow 39 I have with difficulty obtained a handful of water surely it is not death which comes to drink it,api sthirāyurbhagavan kumāraḥ kaccinna śokāya mama prasūtaḥ |labdhaḥ kathaṁcit salilāṁjalirme na khalvimaṁ pātumupaiti kālaḥ || 169 (164)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 70 Tell me is the hoard of my fame free from destruction Is this chief prize of my family secure  Shall I ever depart happily to another life — I who keep one eye ever awake even when my son is asleep 40,apyakṣayaṁ me yaśaso nidhānaṁ kacciddhruvo me kulahastasāraḥ |api prayāsyāmi sukhaṁ paratra supte pi putre nimiṣaikacakṣuḥ || 170 (165)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 71 Surely this young shoot of my family is not born barren destined only to wither Speak quickly my lord I cannot wait thou well knowest the love of near kindred for a son’,kaccinna me jātamaphullameva kulaprabālaṁ pariśoṣabhāgi |kṣipraṁ vibho brūhi na me sti śāṁtiḥ snehaṁ sute vetsi hi bāṁdhavānām || 171 (166)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 72 Knowing the king to be thus agitated through his fear of some impending evil the sage thus addressed him Let not thy mind O monarch be disturbed — all that I have said is certainly true 41,ityāgatāvegamaniṣṭabuddhyā buddhvā nareṁdraṁ sa* munirbabhāṣe |mā bhūnmatiste nṛpa kācidanyā niḥsaṁśayaṁ tadyadavocamasmi || 172 (167)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 73 I have no feeling of fear as to his being subject to change but I am distressed for mine own disappointment It is my time to depart and this child is now born — he who knows that mystery hard to attain the means of destroying birth,nāsyānyathātvaṁ prati vikriyā me svāṁ vaṁcanāṁ tu prati viklavo smi |kālo hi me yātumayaṁ ca jāto jātikṣayasyāsulabhasya boddhā || 173 (168)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 74 Having forsaken his kingdom indifferent to all worldly objects and having attained the highest truth by strenuous efforts he will shine forth as a sun of knowledge to destroy the darkness of illusion in the world,vihāya rājyaṁ viṣayeṣvanāsthastīvraiḥ prayatnairadhigamya tattvam |jagatyayaṁ mohatamo nihaṁtuṁ jvaliṣyati jñānamayo hi sūryaḥ || 174 (169)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 75 He will deliver by the boat of knowledge the distressed world borne helplessly along from the ocean of misery which throws up sickness as its foam tossing with the waves of old age and rushing with the dreadful onflow of death,duḥkhārṇavādvyādhivikīrṇaphenājjarātaraṁgānmaraṇogravegāt |uttārayiṣyatyayamuhyamānamārttaṁ jagajjñānamahāplavena || 175 (170)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 76 The thirsty world of living beings will drink the flowing stream of his Law bursting forth with the water of wisdom enclosed by the banks of strong moral rules delightfully cool with contemplation and filled with religious vows as with ruddy geese,prajñāṁbuvegāṁ sthiraśīlavaprāṁ samādhiśītāṁ vratacakravākām |asyottamāṁ dharmanadīṁ pravṛttāṁ tṛṣṇārditaḥ pāsyati jīvalokaḥ || 176 (171)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 77 He will proclaim the way of deliverance to those afflicted with sorrow entangled in objects of sense and lost in the forest-paths of worldly existence as to travellers who have lost their way,duḥkhārditebhyo viṣayāvṛtebhyaḥ saṁsārakāṁtārapathasthitebhyaḥ |ākhyāsyati hyeṣa vimokṣamārgaṁ mārgapranaṣṭebhya ivādhvagebhyaḥ || 177 (172)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 78 By the rain of the Law he will give gladness to the multitude who are consumed in this world with that fire of desire whose fuel is worldly objects as a great cloud does with its showers at the end of the hot season,vidahyamānāya janāya loke rāgāgnināyaṁ viṣayeṁdhanena |prahlādamādhāsyati dharmavṛṣṭyā vṛṣṭyā mahāmegha ivātapāṁte || 178 (173)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 79 He will break open for the escape of living beings that door whose bolt is desire and whose two leaves are ignorance and delusion — with that excellent blow of the good Law which is so hard to find,tṛṣṇārgalaṁ mohatamaḥkapāṭaṁ dvāraṁ prajānāmapayānahetoḥ |vipāṭayiṣyatyayamuttamena saddharmatāḍena durāsadena || 179 (174)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 80 He the king of the Law when he has attained to supreme knowledge will achieve the deliverance from its bonds of the world now overcome by misery destitute of every refuge and enveloped in its own chains of delusion,svairmohapāśaiḥ pariveṣṭitasya duḥkhābhibhūtasya nirāśrayasya |lokasya saṁbudhya ca dharmarājaḥ kariṣyate baṁdhanamokṣameṣaḥ || 180 (175)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 81 Therefore make no sorrow for him — that belongs rather kind sire to the pitiable world of human beings who through illusion or the pleasures of desire or intoxication refuse to hear his perfect Law,tanmā kṛthāḥ śokamimaṁ prati tvam tatsaumya śocye hi manuṣyaloke |mohena vā kāmasukhairmadādvā yo naiṣṭhikaṁ śroṣyati nāsya dharmam || 181 (176)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 82 Therefore since I have fallen short of that excellence though I have accomplished all the stages of contemplation my life is only a failure since I have not heard his Law I count even dwelling in the highest heaven a misfortune’,bhraṣṭasya tasmācca guṇādato me dhyānāni labdhvāpyakṛtārthataiva |dharmasya tasyāśravaṇādahaṁ hi manye vipattiṁ tridive pi vāsam || 182 (177)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 83 Having heard these words the king with his queen and his friends abandoned sorrow and rejoiced thinking such is this son of mine’ he considered that his excellence was his own,iti śrutārthaḥ sasuhṛtsadārastyaktvā viṣādaṁ mumude nareṁdraḥ |evaṁvidho yaṁ tanayo mameti mene sa hi svāmapi sāramattām || 183 (178)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 84 But he let his heart be influenced by the thought he will travel by the noble path’ — he was not in truth averse to religion yet still he saw alarm at the prospect of losing his child,āryeṇa mārgeṇa tu yāsyatīti ciṁtāvidheyaṁ hṛdayaṁ cakāra |na khalvasau na priyadharmapakṣaḥ saṁtānanāśāttu bhayaṁ dadarśa || 184 (179)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 85 Then the sage Asita having made known the real fate which awaited the prince to the king who was thus disturbed about his son departed by the way of the wind as he had come his figure watched reverentially in his flight,atha munirasito nivedya tattvaṁ sutaniyataṁ sutaviklavāya rājñe |sabahumatamudīkṣyamāṇarūpaḥ pavanapathena yathāgataṁ jagāma || 185 (180)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 86 Having taken his resolution and having seen the son of his younger sister 42 the saint filled with compassion enjoined him earnestly in all kinds of ways as if he were his son to listen to the sage’s words and ponder over them,kṛtamatiranujāsutaṁ ca dṛṣṭvā munivacanaśravaṇe pi tanmatau ca |bahuvidhamanukaṁpayā sa sādhuḥ priyasutavadviniyojayāṁcakāra || 186 (181)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 87 The monarch also being well-pleased at the birth of a son having thrown off all those bonds called worldly objects caused his son to go through the usual birth-ceremonies in a manner worthy of the family,narapatirapi putrajanmatuṣṭo viṣayamatāni vimucya baṁdhanāni |kulasadṛśamacīkaradyathāvatpriyatanayaṁ tanayasya jātakarma || 187 (182)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 88 When ten days were fulfilled after his son’s birth with his thoughts kept under restraint and filled with excessive joy he offered for his son most elaborate sacrifices to the gods with muttered prayers oblations and all kinds of auspicious ceremonies,daśasu pariṇateṣvahaḥsu caivaṁ prayatamanāḥ parayā mudā parītaḥ |akuruta japahomamaṁgalādyāḥ paramatamāḥ sa sutasya devatejyāḥ || 188 (183)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 89 And he himself gave to the Brāhmans for his son’s welfare cows full of milk with no traces of infirmity golden-horned and with strong healthy calves to the full number of a hundred thousand,api ca śatasahasrapūrṇasaṁkhyāḥ sthirabalavattanayāḥ sahemaśṛṁgīḥ |anupagatajarāḥ payasvinīrgāḥ svayamadadātsutavṛddhaye dvijebhyaḥ || 189 (184)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 90 Then he with his soul under strict restraint having performed all kinds of ceremonies which rejoiced his heart on a fortunate day in an auspicious moment gladly determined to enter his city,bahuvidhaviṣayāstato yatātmā svahṛdayatoṣakarīḥ kriyā vidhāya |guṇavati divase śive muhūrte matimakaronmuditaḥ purapraveśe || 190 (185)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 91 Then the queen with her babe having worshipped the gods for good fortune occupied a costly palanquin made of elephants’ tusks filled with all kinds of white flowers and blazing with gems,dviradaradamayīmatho mahārhāṁ sitasitapuṣpabhṛtāṁ maṇipradīpām |abhajata śivikāṁ śivāya devī tanayavatī praṇipatya devatābhyaḥ || 191 (186)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 92 Having made his wife with her child 43 enter first into the city accompanied by the aged attendants the king himself also advanced saluted by the hosts of the citizens as Indra entering heaven saluted by the immortals,puramatha purataḥ praveśya patnīṁ sthavirajanānugatāmapatyanāthām |nṛpatirapi jagāma paurasaṁghairdivamamarairmaghavānivārcyamānaḥ || 192 (187)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 93 The Śākya king having entered his palace like Bhava 44 well-pleased at the birth of Kārttikeya 45 with his face full of joy gave orders for lavish expenditure showing all kinds of honour and liberality 46,bhavanamatha vigāhya śākyarājo bhava iva ṣaṇmukhajanmanā pratītaḥ |idamidamiti harṣapūrṇavaktro bahuvidhapuṣṭiyaśaskaraṁ vyadhatta || 193 (188)
https//bitly/2gSttKk, 94 Thus at the good fortune of the birth of the king’s son that city surnamed after Kapila with all the surrounding inhabitants was full of gladness like the city of the lord of wealth 47 crowded with heavenly nymphs at the birth of his son Nalakūvara,iti narapatiputrajanmavṛddhyā sajanapadaṁ kapilāhvayaṁ puraṁ tat |dhanadapuramivāpsaro vakīrṇaṁ muditamabhūnnalakūvaraprasūtau || 194 (189)
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 1 From the time of the birth of that son of his who the true master of himself was to end all birth and old age the king increased day by day in wealth elephants horses and friends as a river increases with its influx of waters,ā janmano janmajarāṁtakasya tasyātmajasyātmajitaḥ sa rājā |ahanyahanyarthagajāśvamitrairvṛddhiṁ yayau siṁdharivāṁbuvegaiḥ || 21
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 2 Of different kinds of wealth and jewels and of gold wrought or unwrought he found 01 treasures of manifold variety 02 surpassing even the capacity of his desires,dhanasya ratnasya ca tasya tasya kṛtākṛtasyaiva ca kāṁcanasya |tadā hi naikātmanidhīnavāpi manorathasyāpyatibhārabhūtān || 22
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 3 Elephants from Himavat raging with rut whom not even princes of elephants like Padma 03 could teach to go round in circles came without any effort and waited on him,ye padmakalpairapi ca dvipeṁdrairna maṁḍalaṁ śakyamihābhinetum |madotkaṭā haimavatā gajāste vināpi yatnādupatasthurenam || 23
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 4 His city was all astir with the crowds of horses some adorned with various marks and decked with new golden trappings others unadorned and with long flowing manes — suitable alike in strength gentleness and costly ornaments 04,nānāṁkacihnairnavahemabhāṁḍairabhūṣitairlaṁbasaṭaistathānyaiḥ |saṁcukṣubhe cāsya puraṁ turaṁgairbalena maitryā ca dhanena cāptaiḥ || 24
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 5 And many fertile cows with tall calves gathered in his kingdom well nourished and happy gentle and without fierceness and producing excellent milk,puṣṭāśca tuṣṭāśca tadāsya rājye sādhvyo rajaskā guṇavatpayaskāḥ |udagravatsaiḥ sahitā babhūvurbahvyo bahukṣīraduhaśca gāvaḥ || 25
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 6 His enemies became indifferent indifference grew into friendship his friends became specially united were there two sides — one passed into oblivion,madhyasthatāṁ tasya ripurjagāma madhyasvabhāvaḥ prayayau suhṛttvam |viśeṣato dārḍhyamiyāya mitraṁ dvāvasya pakṣāvaparastu nāśam || 26
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 7 Heaven rained in his kingdom in due time and place with the sound of gentle winds and clouds and adorned with wreaths of lightning and without any drawback of showers of stones or thunderbolts,tathāsya maṁdānilameghaśabdaḥ saudāminīkuṁḍalamaṁḍitāṁgaḥ |vināśmavarṣāśanipātadoṣaiḥ kāle ca deśe pravavarṣa devaḥ || 27
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 8 A fruitful crop sprang up according to season even without the labour of ploughing 05 and the old plants grew more vigorous in juice and substance,ruroha saṁyak phalavadyathārtu tadākṛtenāpi kṛṣiśrameṇa |tā eva caivauṣadhayo rasena sāreṇa caivābhyadhikā babhūvuḥ || 28
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 9 Even at that crisis which threatens danger to the body like the collision of battle pregnant women brought forth in good health in safety and without sickness,śarīrasaṁdehakare pi kāle saṁgrāmasaṁmarda iva pravṛtte |svasthāḥ sukhaṁ caiva nirāmayaṁ ca prajajñire garbhadharāśca nāryaḥ || 29
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 10 And whereas men do not willingly ask from others even where a surety’s property is available 06 — at that time even one possessed of slender means turned not his face away when solicited,yacca pratibhvo vibhave pi śakye na prārthayaṁti sma narāḥ parebhyaḥ |abhyarthitaḥ sūkṣmadhano pi cāyaṁ tadā na kaścidvimukho babhūva || 210
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 11 There was no ruin nor murder 07 — nay there was not even one ungenerous to his kinsmen no breaker of obligations none untruthful nor injurious — as in the days of Yayāti the son of Nahuṣa,nāśe vadho baṁdhuṣu nāpyadātā naivāvrato nānṛtiko na hiṁsraḥ |āsīttadā kaścana tasya rājye rājño yayāteriva nāhuṣasya || 211
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 12 Those who sought religious merit performed sacred works and made gardens temples and hermitages wells cisterns lakes and groves having beheld heaven as it were visible before their eyes,udyānadevāyatanāśramāṇāṁ kūpaprapāpuṣkariṇīvanānām |cakruḥ kriyāstatra ca dharmakāmāḥ pratyakṣataḥ svargamivopalabhya || 212
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 13 The people delivered from famine fear and sickness dwelt happily as in heaven and in mutual contentment husband transgressed not against wife nor wife against husband,muktaśca durbhikṣabhayāmayebhyo hṛṣṭo janaḥ svargamivābhireme |patnīṁ patirvā mahiṣī patiṁ vā parasparaṁ na vyabhiceratuśca || 213
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 14 None pursued love for mere sensual pleasure none hoarded wealth for the sake of desires none practised religious duties for the sake of gaining wealth none injured living beings for the sake of religious duty,kaścitsiṣeve rataye na kāmaṁ kāmārthamarthaṁ na jugopa kaścit |kaściddhanārthaṁ na cacāra dharmaṁ dharmāya kaścinna cakāra hiṁsām || 214
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 15 On every side theft and its kindred vices disappeared his own dominion was in peace and at rest from foreign interference 08 prosperity and plenty belonged to him and the cities in his realm were (healthy) like the forests 09,steyādibhiścāpyabhitaśca naṣṭaṁ svasthaṁ svacakraṁ paracakramuktam |kṣemaṁ subhikṣaṁ ca babhūva tasya purāṇyaraṇyāni yathaiva rāṣṭre || 215
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 16 When that son was born it was in that monarch’s kingdom as in the reign of Manu the son of the Sun — gladness went everywhere and evil perished right blazed abroad and sin was still,tadā hi tajjanmani tasya rājño manorivādityasutasya rājye |cacāra harṣaḥ praṇanāśa pāpmā jajvāla dharmaḥ kaluṣaḥ śaśāma || 216
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 17 Since at the birth of this son of the king such a universal accomplishment of all objects took place the king in consequence caused the prince’s name to be Sarvārthasiddha 10,evaṁvidhā rājasutasya tasya sarvārthasiddhiśca yato babhūva |tato nṛpastasya sutasya nāma sarvārthasiddho yamiti pracakre || 217
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 18 But the queen Māyā having seen the great glory of her new-born son like some Ṛṣi of the gods could not sustain the joy which it brought and that she might not die she went to heaven,devī tu māyā vibudharṣikalpaṁ dṛṣṭvā viśālaṁ tanayaprabhāvam |jātaṁ praharṣaṁ na śaśāka soḍhuṁ tato vināśāya divaṁ jagāma || 218
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 19 Then the queen’s sister with an influence like a mother’s undistinguished from the real mother in her affection or tenderness brought up as her own son the young prince who was like the offspring of the gods,tataḥ kumāraṁ suragarbhakalpaṁ snehena bhāvena ca nirviśeṣam |mātṛṣvasā mātṛsamaprabhāvā saṁvardhayāmātmajavadbabhūva || 219
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 20 Then like the young sun on the eastern mountain or the fire when fanned by the wind the prince gradually grew in all due perfection like the moon in the fortnight of brightness,tataḥ sa bālārka ivodayasthaḥ samīrito vahnirivānilena |krameṇa samyagvavṛdhe kumārastārādhipaḥ pakṣa ivātamaske || 220
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 21 Then they brought him as presents from the houses of his friends costly unguents of sandalwood and strings of gems exactly like wreaths of plants and little golden carriages yoked with deer,tato mahārhāṇi ca candanāni ratnāvalīścauṣadhibhiḥ sagarbhāḥ |mṛgaprayuktānrathakāṁśca haimānācakrire smai suhṛdālayebhyaḥ || 221
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 22 Ornaments also suitable to his age and elephants deer and horses made of gold 11 carriages and oxen decked with rich garments and carts 12 gay with silver and gold,vayo nurūpāṇi ca bhūṣaṇāni hiraṇmayā hastimṛgāśvakāśca |rathāśca gāvo vasanaprayuktā gaṁtrīśca cāmīkararūpyacitrāḥ || 222
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 23 Thus indulged with all sorts of such objects to please the senses as were suitable to his years child as he was he behaved not like a child in gravity purity wisdom and dignity,evaṁ sa taistairviṣayopacārairvayo nurūpairupacaryamāṇaḥ |bālo pyabālapratimo babhūva dhṛtyā ca śaucena dhiyā śriyā ca || 223
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 24 When he had passed the period of childhood and reached that of middle youth the young prince learned in a few days the various sciences suitable to his race which generally took many years to master,vayaśca kaumāramatītya madhyaṁ saṁprāpya bālaḥ sa hi rājasūnuḥ |alpairahobhirbahuvarṣagamyā jagrāha vidyāḥ svakulānurūpāḥ || 224
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 25 But having heard before from the great seer Asita his destined future which was to embrace transcendental happiness the anxious care 13 of the king of the present Śākya race turned the prince to sensual pleasures,naiḥśreyasaṁ tasya tu bhavyamarthaṁ śrutvā purastādasitānmahārṣeḥ |kāmeṣu saṁgaṁ janayāṁbabhūva vṛddhirbhavacchākyakulasya rājñaḥ || 225
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 26 Then he sought for him from a family of unblemished moral excellence a bride possessed of beauty modesty and gentle bearing of wide-spread glory Yaśodharā by name having a name well worthy of her a very goddess of good fortune,kulāttato smai sthiraśīlasaṁyutātsādhvīṁ vapurhrīvinayopapannām |yaśodharāṁ nāma yaśoviśālāṁ tulyābhidhānaṁ śriyamājuhāva || 226
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 27 Then after that the prince beloved of the king his father he who was like Sanatkumāra rejoiced in the society of that Śākya princess as the thousand-eyed (Indra) rejoiced with his bride Śacī,athāparaṁ bhūmipateḥ priyo yaṁ sanatkumārapratimaḥ kumāraḥ |sārdhaṁ tayā śākyanareṁdravadhvā śacyā sahasrākṣa ivābhireme || 227
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 28 He might perchance see some inauspicious sight which could disturb his mind’ — thus reflecting the king had a dwelling prepared for him apart from the busy press in the recesses of the palace,kiṁcinmanaḥkṣobhakaraṁ pratīpaṁ kathaṁca paśyediti so nuciṁtya |vāsaṁ nṛpo hyādiśati sma tasmai harmyodareṣveva na bhūpracāram || 228
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 29 Then he spent his time in those royal apartments furnished with the delights proper for every season gaily decorated like heavenly chariots upon the earth and bright like the clouds of autumn amidst the splendid musical concerts of singing-women,tataḥ śarattoyadapāṁḍareṣu bhūmau vimāneṣviva raṁjiteṣu |harmyeṣu sarvartusukhāśrayeṣu strīṇāmudārairvijahāra tūryaiḥ || 229
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 30 With the softly-sounding tambourines beaten by the tips of the women’s hands and ornamented with golden rims and with the dances which were like the dances of the heavenly nymphs that palace shone like Mount Kailāsa,kalairhi cāmīkarabaddhakakṣairnārīkarāgrābhihatairmṛdaṁgaiḥ |varāpsaronṛtyasamaiśca nṛtyaiḥ kailāsavattadbhavanaṁ rarāja || 230
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 31 There the women delighted him with their soft voices their beautiful pearl-garlands their playful intoxication their sweet laughter and their stolen glances concealed by their brows,vāgbhiḥ kalābhirlalitaiśca hārairmadaiḥ sakhelairmadhuraiśca hāsaiḥ |taṁ tatra nāryo ramayāṁbabhūvurbhrūvaṁcitairardhanirīkṣitaiśca || 231
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 32 Borne in the arms of these women well-skilled in the ways of love and reckless in the pursuit of pleasure he fell from the roof of a pavilion and yet reached not the ground like a holy sage stepping from a heavenly chariot,tataśca kāmāśrayapaṁḍitābhiḥ strībhirgṛhīto ratikarkaśābhiḥ |vimānapṛṣṭhānna mahīṁ jagāma vimānapṛṣthādiva puṇyakarmā || 232
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 33 Meanwhile the king for the sake of ensuring his son’s prosperity and stirred in heart by the destiny which had been predicted for him delighted himself in perfect calm ceased from all evil practised all self-restraint and rewarded the good,nṛpastu tasyaiva vivṛddhihetostadbhāvinārthena ca codyamānaḥ |śame bhireme virarāma pāpādbheje damaṁ saṁvibabhāja sādhūn || 233
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 34 He turned to no sensual pleasures like one wanting in self-control he felt no violent delight in any state of birth 14 he subdued by firmness the restless horses of the senses and he surpassed his kindred and citizens by his virtues,nādhīravat kāmasukhe sasaṁje na saṁraraṁje viṣamaṁ jananyām |dhṛtyeṁdriyāśvāṁścapalān vijigye baṁdhūṁśca paurāṁśca guṇairjigāya || 234
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 35 He sought not learning to vex another such knowledge as was beneficent that only he studied he wished well to all mankind as much as to his own subjects,nādhyaiṣṭa duḥkhāya parasya vidyāṁ jñānaṁ śivaṁ yattu tadadhyagīṣṭa |svābhyaḥ prajābhyo hi yathā tathaiva sarvaprajābhyaḥ śivamāśaśaṁse || 235
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 36 He worshipped also duly the brilliant (Agni) that tutelary god of the Aṅgirasas for his son’s long life and he offered oblations in a large fire and gave gold 15 and cows to the Brāhmans,taṁ bhāsuraṁ cāṁgirasādhidevaṁ yathāvadānarca tadāyuṣe saḥ |juhāva havyānyakṛśe kṛśānau dadau dvijebhyaḥ kṛśanaṁ ca gāśca || 236
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 37 He bathed to purify his body and mind with the waters of holy places and of holy feelings and at the same time he drank the soma-juice as enjoined by the Veda and the heartfelt self-produced happiness of perfect calm,sasnau śarīraṁ pavituṁ manaśca tīrthāṁbubhiścaiva guṇāṁbubhiśca |vedopadiṣṭaṁ samamātmajaṁ ca somaṁ papau śāṁtisukhaṁ ca hārdam || 237
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 38 He only spoke what was pleasant and not unprofitable he discoursed about what was true and not ill-natured he could not speak even to himself for very shame a false pleasant thing or a harsh truth,sāṁtvaṁ babhāṣe na ca nārthavadyajjajalpa tattvaṁ na ca vipriyaṁ yat |sāṁtvaṁ hyatatvaṁ paruṣaṁ ca tattvaṁ hriyāśakannātmana eva vaktum || 238
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 39 In things which required to be done whether they were pleasant or disagreeable he found no reason either for desire or dislike he pursued the advantageous which could be attained without litigation 16 he did not so highly value sacrifice,iṣṭeṣvaniṣṭeṣu ca kāryavatsu na rāgadoṣāśrayatāṁ prapede |śivaṁ siṣeve vyavahāralabdhaṁ yajñaṁ hi mene na tathā yathāvat || 239
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 40 When a suppliant came to him with a petition he at once hastened to quench his thirst with the water sprinkled on his gift 17 and without fighting by the battle-axe of his demeanour he smote down the arrogant armed with 18 double pride,āśāvate cābhigatāya sadyo deyāṁbubhistarṣamacecchidiṣṭa |yuddhādṛte vṛttaparaśvadhena dvidarpamudvṛttamabebhidiṣṭa || 240
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 41 Thus he took away the one and protected the seven he abandoned the seven and kept the five he obtained the set of three and learned the set of three he understood the two and abandoned the two,ekaṁ vininye sa jugopa sapta saptaiva tatyāja rarakṣa paṁca |prāpa trivargaṁ bubudhe trivargaṁ jajñe dvivargaṁ prajahau dvivargam || 241
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 42 Guilty persons even though he had sentenced them to death he did not cause to be killed nor even looked on them with anger he bound them with gentle words and with the reform produced in their character — even their release was accompanied by no inflicted injury,kṛtāgaso pi pratipādya vadhyānnājīghanannāpi ruṣā dadarśa |babaṁdha sāṁtvena phalena caitāṁstyāgo pi teṣāṁ hyanapāyadṛṣṭaḥ || 242
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 43 He performed great religious vows prescribed by ancient seers he threw aside hostile feelings long cherished he acquired glory redolent with the fragrance of virtue he relinquished all passions involving defilement,ārṣāṇyacārītparamavratāni vairāṇyahāsīccirasaṁbhṛtāni |yaśāṁsi cāpadguṇagaṁdhavaṁti rajāṁsyahāsīnmalinīkarāṇi || 243
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 44 He desired not to take his tribute of one-sixth without acting as the guardian of his people 19 he had no wish to covet another’s property he desired not to mention the wrong-doing of his enemies nor did he wish to fan wrath in his heart,na cājihīrṣīdbalimapravṛttaṁ na cācikīrṣītparavastvabhidhyām |na cāvivakṣīddviṣatāmadharmaṁ na cādidhakṣīddhṛdayena manyum || 244
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 45 When the monarch himself was thus employed his servants and citizens followed his example like the senses of one absorbed in contemplation whose mind is abstracted in profound repose,tasmiṁstathā bhūmipatau pravṛtte bhṛtyāśca paurāśca tathaiva ceruḥ |śamātmake cetasi viprasanne prayuktayogasya yatheṁdriyāṇi || 245
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 46 In course of time to the fair-bosomed Yaśodharā — who was truly glorious in accordance with her name — there was born from the son of Śuddhodana a son named Rāhula with a face like the enemy of Rāhu 20,kāle tataścārupayodharāyāṁ yaśodharāyāṁ suyaśodharāyām |śauddhodanerāhusapatnavaktro jajñe suto rāhula eva nāmnā || 246
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 47 Then the king who from regard to the welfare of his race had longed for a son and been exceedingly delighted  — as he had rejoiced at the birth of his son so did he now rejoice at the birth of his grandson,atheṣṭaputraḥ paramapratītaḥ kulasya vṛddhiṁ prati bhūmipālaḥ |yathaiva putraprasave nanaṁda tathaiva pautraprasave nanaṁda || 247
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 48 O how can I feel that love which my son feels for my grandson’ Thus thinking in his joy he at the due time attended to every enjoined rite like one who fondly loves his son and is about to rise to heaven,pautrasya me putragato mamaiva snehaḥ kathaṁ syāditi jātaharṣaḥ |kāle sa taṁ taṁ vidhimālalaṁbe putrapriyaḥ svargamivārurukṣan || 248
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 49 Standing in the paths of the pre-eminent kings who flourished in primaeval ages he practised austerities without laying aside his white garments and he offered in sacrifice only those things which involved no injury to living creatures,sthitvā pathi prāthamakalpikānāṁ rājarṣabhāṇāṁ yaśasānvitānām |śuklānyamuktvāpi tapāṁsyatapta yajñe ca hiṁsārahitairayaṣṭa || 249
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 50 He of holy deeds shone forth gloriously in the splendour of royalty and the splendour of penances conspicuous by his family and his own conduct and wisdom and desirous to diffuse brightness like the sun,ajājvaliṣṭātha sa puṇyakarmā nṛpaśriyā caiva tapaḥśriyā ca |kulena vṛttena dhiyā ca dīptastejaḥ sahasrāṁśurivotsisṛkṣuḥ || 250
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 51 Having offered worship he whose own glory was secure muttered repetitions of Vedic texts to Svayambhū for the safety of his son and performed various ceremonies hard to be accomplished like the god Ka in the first aeon wishing to create living beings,svāyaṁbhuvaṁ cārcikamarcayitvā jajāpa putrasthitaye sthitaśrīḥ |cakāra karmāṇi ca duṣkarāṇi prajāḥ sisṛkṣuḥ ka ivādikāle || 251
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 52 He laid aside weapons and pondered the Śāstra he practised perfect calm and underwent various observances like a hermit he refused all objects of sense he viewed all his kingdoms 21 like a father,tatjyāja śastraṁ vimamarśa śāstraṁ śamaṁ siṣeve niyamaṁ viṣehe |vaśīva kaṁcidviṣayaṁ na bheje piteva sarvānviṣayān dadarśa || 252
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 53 He endured the kingdom for the sake of his son his son for his family his family for fame fame for heaven heaven for the soul — he only desired the soul’s continuance for the sake of duty,babhāra rājyaṁ sa hi putrahetoḥ putraṁ kulārthaṁ yaśase kulaṁ tu |svargāya śabdaṁ divamātmahetordharmārthamātmasthitimācakāṁkṣa || 253
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 54 Thus did he practise the various observances as followed by the pious and established from revelation he asking himself now that he has seen the face of his son how may my son be stopped from going to the forest’,evaṁ sa dharmaṁ vividhaṁ cakāra sadbhirnipātaṁ śrutitaśca siddham |dṛṣṭvā kathaṁ putramukhaṁ suto me vanaṁ na yāyāditi nāthamānaḥ || 254
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, 55 The prudent 22 kings of the earth who wish to guard their prosperity watch over their sons in the world but this king though loving religion kept his son from religion and set him free towards all objects of pleasure,rirakṣiṣaṁtaḥ śriyamātmasaṁsthā rakṣaṁti putrān bhuvi bhūmipālāḥ |putraṁ nareṁdraḥ sa tu dharmakāmo rarakṣa dharmādviṣayeṣvamuṁcat || 255
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, sa ratimupasiṣeve bodhimāpannayāvat || 256,vanamanupamasattvā bodhisattvāstu sarveviṣayasukharasajñā jagmurutpannaputrāḥ |
https//bitly/2vG8Nwt, But all Bodhisattvas those beings of pre-eminent nature after knowing the flavour of worldly enjoyments have departed to the forest as soon as a son is born to them therefore he too though he had accomplished all his previous destiny even when the (final) motive had begun to germinate still went on pursuing worldly pleasure up to the time of attaining the supreme wisdom,ata upacitakarmā rūḍhamūle pi hetausa ratimupasiṣeve bodhimāpannayāvat || 256
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 1 On a certain day he heard of the forests carpeted with tender grass with their trees resounding with the kokilas adorned with lotus-ponds and which had been all bound up in the cold season,tataḥ kadācinmṛduśādvalāni puṁskokilonnāditapādapāni |śuśrāva padmākaramaṁḍitāni śīte nibaddhāni sa kānanāni || 31
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 2 Having heard of the delightful appearance of the city groves beloved by the women he resolved to go out of doors like an elephant long shut up in a house,śrutvā tataḥ strījanavallabhānāṁ manojñabhāvaṁ purakānanānām |bahiḥprayāṇāya cakāra buddhimaṁtargṛhe nāga ivāvaruddhaḥ || 32
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 3 The king having learned the character of the wish thus expressed by his son ordered a pleasure-party to be prepared worthy of his own affection and his son’s beauty and youth,tato nṛpastasya niśamya bhāvaṁ putrābhidhānasya manorathasya |snehasya lakṣmyā vayasaśca yogyām-ājñāpayāmāsa vihārayātrām || 33
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 4 He prohibited the encounter of any afflicted common person in the highroad heaven forbid that the prince with his tender nature should even imagine himself to be distressed’,nivartayāmāsa ca rājamārge saṁpātamārtasya pṛthagjanasya |mā bhūtkumāraḥ sukumāracittaḥ saṁvignacetā iva manyamānaḥ || 34
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 5 Then having removed out of the way with the greatest gentleness all those who had mutilated limbs or maimed senses the decrepit and the sick and all squalid beggars they made the highway assume its perfect beauty,pratyaṁgahīnān vikaleṁdriyāṁśca jīrṇāturādīn kṛpaṇāṁśca bhikṣūn |tataḥ samutsārya pareṇa sāmnā śobhāṁ parā rājapathasya cakruḥ || 35
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 6 Along this road thus made beautiful the fortunate prince with his well-trained attendants came down one day at a proper time from the roof of the palace and went to visit the king by his leave,tataḥ kṛte śrīmati rājamārge śrīmān vinītānucaraḥ kumāraḥ |prāsādapṛṣṭhādavatīrya kāle kṛtābhyanujño nṛpamabhyagacchat || 36
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 7 Then the king with tears rising to his eyes having smelt his son’s head 01 and long gazed upon him gave him his permission saying Go’ but in his heart through affection he could not let him depart,atho nareṁdraḥ sutamāgatāśruḥ śirasyupāghrāya ciraṁ nirīkṣya |gaccheti cājñāpayati sma vācā snehānna cainaṁ manasā mumoca || 37
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 8 He then mounted a golden chariot adorned with reins bright like flashing lightning 02 and yoked with four gentle horses all wearing golden trappings,tataḥ sa jāṁbūnadabhāṁḍabhṛdbhiryuktaṁ caturbhirnibhṛtaisturaṁgaiḥ |aklīvavidhyucchuciraśmidhārāṁ hiraṇmayaṁ syaṁdanamāruroha || 38
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 9 With a worthy retinue he entered the road which was strewn with heaps of gleaming flowers with garlands suspended and banners waving like the moon with its asterism entering the sky,tataḥ prakīrṇojjvalapuṣpajālaṁ viṣaktamālyaṁ pracalatpatākam |mārgaṁ prapede sadṛśānuyātraścaṁdraḥ sanakṣatra ivāntarīkṣam || 39
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 10 Slowly slowly he passed along the highway watched on every side by the citizens and beshowered by their eyes opened wide with curiosity like blue lotuses,kautūhalātsphītataraiśca netrairnīlotpalābhairiva kīryamāṇaḥ |śanaiḥ śanai rājapathaṁ jagāhe pauraiḥ samaṁtādabhivīkṣyamāṇaḥ || 310
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 11 Some praised him for his gentle disposition others hailed him for his glorious appearance others eulogised his beauty from his fine countenance and desired for him length of days,taṁ tuṣṭuvuḥ saumyaguṇena kecidvavaṁdire dīptatayā tathānye |saumukhyatastu śriyamasya kecidvaipulyamāśaṁsiṣurāyuṣaśca || 311
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 12 Hump-backed men coming out from the great families and troops of foresters and dwarfs 03 and women coming out from the meaner houses bowed down like the banners of some procession of the gods,niḥsṛtya kubjāśca mahākulebhyo vyūhāśca kairātakavāmanānām |nāryaḥ kṛśebhyaśca niveśanebhyo devānuyānadhvajavat praṇemuḥ || 312
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 13 04Hearing the news the prince is going out’ from the attendants of the female apartments the women hastened to the roofs of the different mansions having obtained the leave of their lords,tataḥ kumāraḥ khalu gacchatīti śrutvā striyaḥ preṣyajanātpravṛttim |didṛkṣayā harmyatalāni jagmurjanena mānyena kṛtābhyanujñāḥ || 313
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 14 Hindered by the strings of their girdles which had slipped down with their eyes bewildered as just awakened from sleep and with their ornaments hastily put on in the stir of the news and filled with curiosity they crowded round,tāḥ srastakāṁcīguṇavighnitāśca suptaprabuddhākulalocanāśca |vṛttāṁtavinyastavibhūṣaṇāśca kautūhalenāpi bhṛtāḥ parīyuḥ || 314
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 15 Frightening the flocks of birds which lived in the houses with the noise of their girdles and the jingling of their anklets which resounded on the staircases and roofs of the mansions and mutually reproaching one another for their hurry,prāsādasopānatalapraṇādaiḥ kāṁcīravairnūpuranisvanaiśca |vibhrāmayaṁtyo gṛhapakṣisaṁghānanyonyavegāṁśca samākṣipaṁtyaḥ || 315
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 16 Some of these women even in their haste as they rushed longing to see were delayed in their going by the weight of their hips and full bosoms,kāsāṁcidāsāṁ tu varāṁganānāṁ jātatvarāṇāmapi sotsukānām |gatiṁ gurutvājjagṛhurviśālāḥ śroṇīrathāḥ pīnapayodharāśca || 316
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 17 Another though well able to go herself checked her pace and forbore to run hiding with shame her ornaments hitherto worn only in seclusion and now too boldly displayed,śīghraṁ samarthāpi tu gaṁtumanyā gatiṁ nijagrāha yayau na tūrṇam |hriyā pragalbhāni nigūhamānā rahaḥ prayuktāni vibhūṣaṇāni || 317
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 18 There they were restlessly swaying about in the windows crowded together in the mutual press with their earrings polished by the continual collision and their ornaments all jingling,parasparotpīḍanapiṁḍitānāṁ saṁmardasaṁśobhitakuṁḍalānām |tāsāṁ tadā sasvanabhūṣaṇānāṁ vātāyaneṣvapraśamo babhūva || 318
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 19 The lotus-like faces of the women gleamed while they looked out from the windows with their earrings coming into mutual proximity 05 as if they were real lotuses fastened upon the houses,vātāyanebhyastu viniḥsṛtāni parasparopāsitakuṁḍalāni |strīṇāṁ virejurmukhapaṁkajāni saktāni harmyeṣviva paṁkajāni || 319
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 20 With the palaces all alive with crowds of damsels every aperture thrown open in eager curiosity the magnificent city appeared on every side like heaven with its divine chariots thronged with celestial nymphs,tato vimānairyuvatīkalāpaiḥ kautūhalodghāṭitavātayānaiḥ |śrīmatsamaṁtānnagaraṁ babhāse viyadvimānairiva sāpsarobhiḥ || 320
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 21 The faces of the beautiful women shone like lotuses wreathed in garlands while through the narrowness of the windows their earrings were transferred to each other’s cheeks,vātāyanānāmaviśālabhāvādanyonyagaṁḍārpitakuṁḍalāni |mukhāni rejuḥ pramadottamānāṁ baddhāḥ kalāpa iva paṁkajānām || 321
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 22 Gazing down upon the prince in the road the women appeared as if longing to fall to the earth gazing up to him with upturned faces the men seemed as if longing to rise to heaven 06,tasmin kumāraṁ pathi vīkṣamāṇāḥ striyo babhurgāmiva gaṁtukāmāḥ |ūrdhvonmukhāścainamudīkṣamāṇā narā babhurdyāmiva gaṁtukāmāḥ || 322
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 23 Beholding the king’s son thus radiant in his beauty and glory those women softly whispered happy is his wife’ with pure minds and from no baser feeling,dṛṣṭvā ca taṁ rājasutaṁ striyastā jājvalyamānaṁ vapuṣā śriyā ca |dhanyāsya bhāryeti śanairavocañśuddhairmanobhiḥ khalu nānyabhāvāt || 323
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 24 He with the long sturdy arms who stands in his beauty like the flower-armed god visibly present will leave his royal pomp and devote himself to religion’ thus thinking full of kindly feelings towards him they all offered reverence,ayaṁ kila vyāyatapīnabāhū rūpeṇa sākṣādiva puṣpaketuḥ |tyaktvā śriyaṁ dharmamupeṣyatīti tasmin hitā gauravameva cakruḥ || 324
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 25 Beholding for the first time that high-road thus crowded with respectful citizens all dressed in white sedate garments the prince for a while did feel a little pleasure and thought that it seemed to promise a revival of his youth,kīrṇaṁ tathā rājapathaṁ kumāraḥ paurairvinītaiḥ śucidhīraveṣaiḥ |tatpūrvamālokya jaharṣa kiṁcinmene punarbhāvamivātmanaśca || 325
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 26 But then the gods dwelling in pure abodes 07 having beheld that city thus rejoicing like heaven itself created an old man to walk along on purpose to stir the heart of the king’s son,puraṁ tu tatsvargamiva prahṛṣṭaṁ śuddhādhivāsāḥ samavekṣya devāḥ |jīrṇaṁ naraṁ nirmamire prayātuṁ saṁcodanārthaṁ kṣitipātmajasya || 326
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 27 The prince having beheld him thus overcome with decrepitude and different in form from other men with his gaze intently fixed on him thus addressed his driver 08 with simple confidence,tataḥ kumāro jarayābhibhūtaṁ dṛṣṭvā narebhyaḥ pṛthagākṛtiṁ tam |uvāca saṁgrāhakamāgatāsthastatraiva niṣkampaniviṣṭadṛṣṭiḥ || 327
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 28 Who is this man that has come here O charioteer with white hair and his hand resting on a staff his eyes hidden beneath his brows his limbs bent down and hanging loose — is this a change produced in him or his natural state or an accident’,ka eṣa bhoḥ sūta naro bhyupetaḥ keśaiḥ sitairyaṣṭiviṣaktahastaḥ |bhrūsaṁvṛtākṣaḥ śithilānatāṁgaḥ kiṁ vikriyaiṣā prakṛtiryadṛcchā || 328
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 29 Thus addressed the charioteer revealed to the king’s son the secret that should have been kept so carefully thinking no harm in his simplicity for those same gods had bewildered his mind,ityevamuktaḥ sa rathapraṇetā nivedayāmāsa nṛpātmajāya |saṁrakṣyamapyarthamadoṣadarśī taireva devaiḥ kṛtabuddhimohaḥ || 329
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 30 That is old age by which he is broken down — the ravisher of beauty the ruin of vigour the cause of sorrow the destruction of delights the bane of memories the enemy of the senses,rūpasya hartrī vyasanaṁ balasya śokasya yonirnidhanaṁ ratīnām |nāśaḥ smṛtīnāṁ ripuriṁdriyāṇāmeṣā jarā nāma yayaiṣa bhagnaḥ || 330
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 31 He too once drank milk in his childhood and in course of time he learned to grope on the ground having step by step become a vigorous youth he has step by step in the same way reached old age’,pītaṁ hyanenāpi payaḥ śiśutve kālena bhūyaḥ parimṛṣṭamurvyām |krameṇa bhūtvā ca yuvā vapuṣmān krameṇa tenaiva jarāmupetaḥ || 331
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 32 Being thus addressed the prince starting a little spoke these words to the charioteer What will this evil come to me also’ and to him again spoke the charioteer,ityevamukte calitaḥ sa kiṁcidrājātmajaḥ sūtamidaṁ babhāṣe |kimeṣa doṣo bhavitā mamāpītyasmai tataḥ sārathirabhyuvāca || 332
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 33 It will come without doubt by the force of time through multitude of years even to my long-lived lord all the world knows thus that old age will destroy their comeliness and they are content to have it so’,āyuṣmato pyeṣa vayaḥprakarṣānniḥsaṁśayaṁ kālavaśena bhāvī |evaṁ jarāṁ rūpavināśayitrīṁ jānāti caivecchati caiṣa lokaḥ || 333
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 34 Then he the great-souled one who had his mind purified by the impressions of former good actions who possessed a store of merits accumulated through many preceding aeons was deeply agitated when he heard of old age like a bull who has heard the crash of a thunderbolt close by,tataḥ sa pūrvāśayaśuddhabuddhirvistīrṇakalpācitapuṇyakarmā |śrutvā jarāṁ saṁvivije mahātmā mahāśanerghoṣamivāṁtike gauḥ || 334
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 35 Drawing a long sigh and shaking his head and fixing his eyes on that decrepit old man and looking round on that exultant multitude he then uttered these distressed words,niḥśvasya dīrghaṁ sa śiraḥ prakaṁpya tasmiṁśca jīrṇe viniveśya cakṣuḥ |tāṁ caiva dṛṣṭvā janatāṁ saharṣāṁ vākyaṁ sa saṁvignamidaṁ jagāda || 335
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 36 Old age thus strikes down all alike our memory comeliness and valour and yet the world is not disturbed even when it sees such a fate visibly impending,evaṁ jarā haṁti ca nirviśeṣaṁ smṛtiṁ ca rūpaṁ ca parākramaṁ ca |na caiva saṁvegamupaiti lokaḥ pratyakṣato pīdṛśamīkṣamāṇaḥ || 336
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 37 Since such is our condition O charioteer turn back the horses — go quickly home how can I rejoice in the pleasure-garden when the thoughts arising from old age overpower me’,evaṁ gate sūta nivartayāśvān śīghraṁ gṛhāṇyeva bhavānprayātu |udyānabhūmau hi kuto ratirme jarābhave cetasi vartamāne || 337
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 38 Then the charioteer at the command of the king’s son turned the chariot back and the prince lost in thought entered even that royal palace as if it were empty,athājñayā bhartṛsutasya tasya nivartayāmāsa rathaṁ niyaṁtā |tataḥ kumāro bhavanaṁ tadeva ciṁtāvaśaḥ śūnyamiva prapede || 338
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 39 But when he found no happiness even there as he continually kept reflecting old age old age’ then once more with the permission of the king he went out with the same arrangement as before,yadā tu tatraiva na śarma lebhe jarā jareti praparīkṣamāṇaḥ |tato nareṁdrānumataḥ sa bhūyaḥ krameṇa tenaiva bahirjagāma || 339
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 40 Then the same deities created another man with his body all afflicted by disease and on seeing him the son of Śuddhodana addressed the charioteer having his gaze fixed on the man,athāparaṁ vyādhiparītadehaṁ ta eva devāḥ sasṛjurmanuṣyam |dṛṣṭvā ca taṁ sārathimābabhāṣe śauddhodanistadgatadṛṣṭireva || 340
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 41 Yonder man with a swollen belly his whole frame shaking as he pants his arms and shoulders hanging loose his body all pale and thin uttering plaintively the word mother when he embraces a stranger — who pray is this’,sthūlodaraḥ śvāsacalaccharīraḥ srastāṁsabāhuḥ kṛśapāṇdugātraḥ |aṁbeti vācaṁ karuṇaṁ bruvāṇaḥ paraṁ samāśliṣya naraḥ ka eṣaḥ || 341
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 42 Then his charioteer answered Gentle Sir it is a very great affliction called sickness that has grown up caused by the inflammation of the (three) humours which has made even this strong man 09 no longer master of himself’,tato bravītsārathirasya saumya dhātuprakopaprabhavaḥ pravṛddhaḥ |rogābhidhānaḥ sumahānanarthaḥ śakro pi yenaiṣa kṛto svataṁtraḥ || 342
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 43 Then the prince again addressed him looking upon the man compassionately Is this evil peculiar to him or are all beings alike threatened by sickness’,ityūcivān rājasutaḥ sa bhūyastaṁ sānukaṁpo naramīkṣamāṇaḥ |asyaiva jātaḥ pṛthageṣa doṣaḥ sāmānyato rogabhayaṁ prajānām || 343
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 44 Then the charioteer answered O prince this evil is common to all thus pressed round by diseases men run to pleasure though racked with pain’ 10,tato babhāṣe sa rathapraṇetā kumāra sādhāraṇa eṣa doṣaḥ |evaṁ hi rogaiḥ paripīḍyamāno rujāturo harṣamupaiti lokaḥ || 344
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 45 Having heard this account his mind deeply distressed he trembled like the moon reflected in the waves of water and full of sorrow he uttered these words in a low voice,iti śrutārthaḥ sa viṣaṇṇacetāḥ prāvepatāṁbūrmigataḥ śaśīva |idaṁ ca vākyaṁ karuṇāyamānaḥ provāca kiṁcinmṛdunā svareṇa || 345
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 46 Even while they see all this calamity of diseases mankind can yet feel tranquillity alas for the scattered intelligence of men who can smile when still not free from the terrors of disease,idaṁ ca rogavyasanaṁ prajānāṁ paśyaṁśca viśraṁbhamupaiti lokaḥ |vistīrṇavijñānamaho narāṇāṁ hasaṁti ye rogabhayairamuktāḥ || 346
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 47 Let the chariot O charioteer be turned back from going outside let it return straight to the king’s palace having heard this alarm of disease my mind shrinks into itself repelled from pleasures’,nivartyatāṁ sūta vahiḥprayāṇānnareṁdrasadmaiva rathaḥ prayātu |śrutvā ca me rogabhayaṁ ratibhyaḥ pratyāhataṁ saṁkucatīva cetaḥ || 347
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 48 Then having turned back with all joy departed he entered his home absorbed in thought and having seen him thus return a second time the king himself entered the city,tato nivṛttaḥ sa nivṛttaharṣaḥ pradhyānayuktaḥ praviveśa sadma |taṁ dvistathā prekṣya ca saṁnivṛttaṁ puryāgamaṁ bhūmipatiścakāra || 348
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 49 Having heard the occasion of the prince’s return he felt himself as deserted by him and although unused to severe punishment even when displeased he rebuked him whose duty it was to see that the road was clear,śrutvā nimittaṁ tu nivartanasya saṁtyaktamātmānamanena mene |mārgasya śaucādhikṛtāya caiva cukrośa ruṣṭo pi ca nogradaṁḍaḥ || 349
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 50 And once more he arranged for his son all kinds of worldly enjoyments to their highest point imploring in his heart Would that he might not be able to forsake us even though rendered unable only through the restlessness of his senses’ 11,bhūyaśca tasmai vidadhe sutāya viśeṣayuktaṁ viṣayaprakāram |caleṁdriyatvādapi nāpi śakto nāsmānvijahyāditi nāthamānaḥ || 350
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 51 But when in the women’s apartments his son found no pleasure in the several objects of the senses sweet sounds and the rest he gave orders for another progress outside thinking to himself 12 It may create a diversion of sentiment’ 13,yadā ca śabdādibhiriṁdriyārthairaṁtaḥpure naiva suto sya reme |tato vahirvyādiśati sma yātrāṁ rasāntaraṁ syāditi manyamānaḥ || 351
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 52 And in his affection pondering on the condition of his son never thinking of any ills that might come from his haste he ordered the best singing-women to be in attendance as well-skilled in all the soft arts that can please,snehācca bhāvaṁ tanayasya buddhvā saṁvegadoṣānaviciṁtya kāṁścit |yogyāḥ samājñāpayati sma tatra kalāsvabhijña iti vāramukhyāḥ || 352
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 53 Then the royal road being specially adorned and guarded the king once more made the prince go out having ordered the charioteer and chariot to proceed in a contrary direction (to the previous one),tato viśeṣeṇa nareṁdramārge svalaṁkṛte caiva parīkṣite ca |vyatyāsya sūtaṁ ca rathaṁ ca rājā prasthāpayāmāsa bahiḥ kumāram || 353
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 54 But as the king’s son was thus going on his way the very same deities created a dead man and only the charioteer and the prince and none else beheld him as he was carried dead along the road,tatastathā gacchati rājaputre taireva devairvihito gatāsuḥ |taṁ caiva mārge mṛtamuhyamānaṁ sūtaḥ kumāraśca dadarśa nānyaḥ || 354
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 55 Then spoke the prince to the charioteer Who is this borne by four men followed by mournful companions who is bewailed adorned but no longer breathing’ 14,athābravīdrājasutaḥ sa sūtaṁ naraiścaturbhirhriyate ka eṣaḥ |dīnairmanuṣyairanugamyamāno yo bhūṣito śvāsyavarudyate ca || 355
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 56 Then the driver — having his mind overpowered by the gods who possess pure minds and pure dwellings — himself knowing the truth uttered to his lord this truth also which was not to be told,tataḥ sa śuddhātmabhireva devaiḥ śuddhādhivāsairabhibhūtacetāḥ |avācyamapyarthamimaṁ niyaṁtā pravyājahārārthavidīśvarāya || 356
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 57 This is some poor man who bereft of his intellect senses vital airs and qualities lying asleep and unconscious like mere wood or straw is abandoned alike by friends and enemies after they have carefully swathed and guarded him’,buddhīṁdriyaprāṇaguṇairviyuktaḥ supto visaṁjñastṛṇakāṣṭhabhūtaḥ |saṁbadhya saṁrakṣya ca yatnavadbhiḥ priyāpriyaistyajyata eṣa ko pi || 357
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 58 Having heard these words of the charioteer he was somewhat startled and said to him Is this an accident peculiar to him alone or is such the end of all living creatures’,iti praṇetuḥ sa niśamya vākyaṁ saṁcukṣubhe kiṁciduvāca cainam |kiṁ kevalasyaiva janasya dharmaḥ sarvaprajānāmayamīdṛśo ṁtaḥ || 358
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 59 Then the charioteer replied to him This is the final end of all living creatures be it a mean man a man of middle state or a noble destruction is fixed to all in this world’,tataḥ praṇetā vadati sma tasmai sarvaprajānāmayamaṁtakarmā |hīnasya madhyasya mahātmano vā sarvasya loke niyato vināśaḥ || 359
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 60 Then the king’s son sedate though he was as soon as he heard of death immediately sank down overwhelmed and pressing the end of the chariotpole with his shoulder spoke with a loud voice,tataḥ sa dhīro pi nareṁdrasūnuḥ śrutvaiva mṛtyuṁ viṣasāda sadyaḥ |aṁsena saṁśliṣya ca kūbarāgraṁ provāca nihrādavatā svareṇa || 360
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 61 Is this end appointed to all creatures and yet the world throws off all fear and is infatuated Hard indeed I think must the hearts of men be who can be self-composed in such a road,iyaṁ ca niṣṭhā niyataṁ prajānāṁ pramādyati tyaktabhayaśca lokaḥ |manāṁsi śaṁke kaṭhināni n�oṇāṁ svasthāstathā hyadhvani vartamānāḥ || 361
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 62 Therefore O charioteer turn back our chariot this is no time or place for a pleasure-excursion how can a rational being who knows what destruction is stay heedless here in the hour of calamity’ 15,tasmādrathaṁ sūta nivartyatāṁ no vihārabhūmau na hi deśakālaḥ |jānanvināśaṁ kathamārttikāle sacetanaḥ syādiha hi pramattaḥ || 362
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 63 Even when the prince thus spoke to him the charioteer did not turn the chariot back but at his peremptorily reiterated command he retired to the forest Padmakhaṇḍa,iti bruvāṇe pi narādhipātmaje nivartayāmāsa sa naiva taṁ ratham |viśeṣayuktaṁ tu nareṁdraśāsanātsa padmakhaṁḍaṁ vanameva niryayau || 363
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 64 There he beheld that lovely forest like Nandana itself full of young trees in flower with intoxicated kokilas wandering joyously about and with its bright lakes gay with lotuses and well-furnished with watering-places 16,tataḥ śivaṁ kusumitabālapādapaṁ paribhramatpramuditamattakokilam |vipānavatsakamalacārudīrghikaṁ dadarśa tadvanamiva naṁdanaṁ vanam || 364
https//bitly/2iglXgu, 65 The king’s son was perforce carried away to that wood filled with troops of beautiful women just as if some devotee who had newly taken his vow were carried off feeling weak to withstand temptation to the palace of the monarch of Alakā 17 gay with the dancing of the loveliest heavenly nymphs,varāṁganāgaṇakalilaṁ nṛpātmajastato balādvanamabhinīyate sma tat |varāpsaronṛtyamalakādhipālayaṁ navavrato muniriva vighnakātaraḥ || 365
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 1 Then from that city-garden with their eyes restless in excitement the women went out to meet the prince as a newly-arrived bridegroom,tatastasmāt purodyānāt kautūhalacalekṣaṇāḥ |pratyujjagmurnṛpasutaṁ prāptaṁ varamiva striyaḥ || 41
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 2 And when they came up to him their eyes wide open in wonder they performed their due homage with hands folded like a lotus-caly,xabhigamya ca tāstasmai vismayotphullalocanāḥ |cakrire samudācāraṁ padmakośanibhaiḥ karaiḥ || 42
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 3 Then they stood surrounding him their minds overpowered by passion as if they were drinking him in with their eyes motionless and blossoming wide with love,tasthuśca parivāryainaṁ manmathākṣiptacetasaḥ |niścalaiḥ prītivikacaiḥ pibaṁtya iva locanaiḥ || 43
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 4 Some of the women verily thought that he was Kāma incarnate — decorated as he was with his brilliant signs as with connate ornaments,taṁ hi tā menire nāryaḥ kāmo vigrahavāniti |śobhitaṁ lakṣaṇairdīptaiḥ sahajairbhūṣaṇairiva || 44
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 5 Others thought from his gentleness and majesty that it was the moon with its ambrosial beams as it were visibly come down to the earth,saumyatvāccaiva dhairyācca kāścidenaṁ prajajñire |avatīrṇo mahīṁ sākṣād sudhāṁśuścaṁdramā iva || 45
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 6 Others smitten by his beauty yawned 01 as if to swallow him and fixing their eyes on each other softly sighed,tasya tā vapuṣākṣiptā nirgrahītuṁ jajṛṁbhire |anyonyaṁ dṛṣṭibhirgatvā śanaiśca viniśaśvasuḥ || 46
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 7 Thus the women only looked upon him simply gazing with their eyes — they spoke not nor did they smile controlled by his power,evaṁ tā dṛṣṭimātreṇa nāryo dadṛśureva tam |na vyājahrurna jahasuḥ prabhāveṇāsya yaṁtritāḥ || 47
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 8 But having seen them thus listless bewildered in their love the wise son of the family priest Udāyin thus addressed them,tāstathā tu nirāraṁbhā dṛṣṭvā praṇayaviklavāḥ |purohitasuto dhīmānudāyī vākyamabravīt || 48
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 9 Ye are all skilled in all the graceful arts proficients in understanding the language of amorous sentiments possessed of beauty and gracefulness thorough masters in your own styles,sarvāḥ sarvakalājñāḥ stha bhāvagrahaṇapaṁḍitāḥ |rūpacāturyasaṁpannāḥ svaguṇairmukhyatāṁ gatāḥ || 49
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 10 With these graces of yours ye may embellish even the Northern Kurus yea even the dances 02 of Kuvera much more this little earth,śobhayata guṇairebhirapi tānuttarān kurūn |kuverasyāpi ca krīḍaṁ prāgeva vasudhāmimām || 410
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 11 Ye are able to move even sages who have lost all their desires and to ensnare even the gods who are charmed by heavenly nymphs,śaktāścālayituṁ yūyaṁ vītarāgānṛṣīnapi |apsarobhiśca kalitān grahītuṁ vibudhānapi || 411
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 12 By your skill in expressing the heart’s feelings by your coquetry your grace and your perfect beauty ye are able to enrapture even women how much more easily men,bhāvajñānena hāvena cāturyādrūpasaṁpadā |strīṇāmeva ca śaktāḥ stha saṁrāge kiṁ punarnṛṇām || 412
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 13 You thus skilled as ye are each set 03 in her own proper sphere — such as this is your power I am not satisfied with your simplicity ,tāsāmevaṁvidhānāṁ vo niyuktānāṁ svagocare |iyamevaṁvidhā ceṣṭā na tuṣṭo smyārjavena vaḥ || 413
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 14 This timid action of yours would be fit for new brides their eyes closed through shame — or it might be a blandishment worthy even of the wives of the cowherds 04,idaṁ navavadhūnāṁ vo hrīnikuṁcitacakṣuṣām |sadṛśaṁ ceṣṭitaṁ hi syādapi vā gopayoṣitām || 414
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 15 What though this hero be great by his exalted glory yet great is the might of women let this be your firm resolve,yadyapi syādayaṁ vīraḥ śrīprabhāvānmahāniti |strīṇāmapi mahatteja iti kāryo tra niścayaḥ || 415
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 16 In olden time a great seer hard to be conquered even by the gods was spurned by a harlot the beauty of Kāśi planting her feet upon him,purā hi kāśisuṁdaryā veśavadhvā mahānṛṣiḥ |tāḍito bhūt padanyāsāddurdharṣo daivatairapi || 416
