https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 17 The Bhikṣu Manthālagautama was also formerly spurned by Bālamukhyā with her leg and wishing to please her he carried out dead bodies for her sake to be buried,maṁthālagautamo bhikṣurjaṁghayā bālamukhyayā |piprīṣuśca tadarthārthaṁ vyasūn niraharat purā || 417
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 18 And a woman low in standing and caste fascinated the great seer Gautama though a master of long penances and old in years,gautamaṁ dīrghatapasaṁ mahārṣiṁ dīrghajīvinam |yoṣit saṁtoṣayāmāsa varṇasthānāvarā satī || 418
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 19 So Śāntā 05 by her various wiles captivated and subdued the sage’s son Ṛṣyaśṛṅga unskilled in women’s ways,ṛṣyaśṛṁgaṁ munisutaṁ tathaiva strīṣvapaṁḍitam |upāyairvividhaiḥ śāṁtā jagrāha ca jahāra ca || 419
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 20 And the great seer Viśvāmitra though plunged in a profound penance 06 was carried captive for ten years in the forests by the nymph Ghṛtācī 07,viśvāmitro maharṣiśca vigāḍho pi mahattapāḥ |daśavarṣāṇyaraṇyastho ghṛtācyāpsarasā hṛtaḥ || 420
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 21 Many such seers as these have women brought to shame — how much more then a delicate prince in the first flower of his age,evamādīnṛṣīṁstāṁstānanayan vikriyāṁ striyaḥ |lalitaṁ pūrvavayasaṁ kiṁ punarnṛpateḥ sutam || 421
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 22 This being so boldly put forth your efforts that the prosperity of the king’s family may not be turned away from him,tadevaṁ sati viśrabdhaṁ prayatadhvaṁ tathā yathā |iyaṁ nṛpasya vaṁśaśrīrito na syātparāṅmukhī || 422
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 23 Ordinary women captivate similar lovers but they are truly women who subdue the natures of high and low’,yā hi kāścidyuvatayo haraṁti sadṛśaṁ janam |nikṛṣṭotkṛṣṭayorbhāvaṁ yā gṛhṇaṁti tu tāḥ striyaḥ || 423
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 24 Having heard these words of Udāyin these women as stung to the heart rose even above themselves for the conquest of the prince,ityudāyivacaḥ śrutvā tā viddhā iva yoṣitaḥ |samāruruhurātmānaṁ kumāragrahaṇaṁ prati || 424
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 25 With their brows their glances their coquetries their smiles their delicate movements they made all sorts of significant gestures like women utterly terrified,tā bhrūbhiḥ prekṣitairbhāvairhasitairlalitairgataiḥ |cakrurākṣepikāśceṣṭā bhītabhītā ivāṁganāḥ || 425
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 26 But they soon regained their confidence 08 through the command of the king and the gentle temperament of the prince and through the power of intoxication and of love,rājñastu viniyogena kumārasya ca mārdavāt |jahruḥ kṣipramaviśraṁbhaṁ madena madanena ca || 426
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 27 Then surrounded by troops of women the prince wandered in the wood like an elephant in the forests of Himavat accompanied by a herd of females,atha nārījanavṛtaḥ kumāro vyacaradvanam |vāsitāyūthasahitaḥ karīva himavadvanam || 427
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 28 Attended by the women he shone in that pleasant grove as the sun surrounded by Apsarasas in his royal garden,sa tasmin kānane ramye jajvāla strīpuraḥsaraḥ |ākrīḍa iva babhrāje vivasvānapsarovṛtaḥ || 428
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 29 There some of them urged by passion pressed him with their full firm bosoms in gentle collisions,madenāvarjitā nāma taṁ kāścittatra yoṣitaḥ |kaṭhinaiḥ paspṛśuḥ pīnaiḥ saṁghaṭṭairvalgubhiḥ stanaiḥ || 429
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 30 Another violently embraced him after making a pretended stumble — leaning on him with her shoulders drooping down and with her gentle creeper-like arms dependent,srastāṁsakomalālaṁbamṛdubāhulatābalā |anṛtaṁ skhalitaṁ kācitkṛtvainaṁ sasvaje balāt || 430
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 31 Another with her mouth smelling of spirituous liquor her lower lip red like copper whispered in his ear Let my secret be heard’,kācit tāmrādharoṣṭhena mukhenāsavagaṁdhinā |viniśaśvāsa karṇe sya rahasyaṁ śrūyatāmiti || 431
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 32 Another all wet with unguents as if giving him her command clasped his hand eagerly and said Perform thy rites of adoration here’,kācidājñāpayaṁtīva provācārdrānulepanā |iha bhaktiṁ kuruṣveti hastaṁ saṁśliṣya lipsayā || 432
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 33 Another with her blue garments continually slipping down in pretended intoxication stood conspicuous with her tongue visible like the night with its lightning flashing,muhurmuhurmadavyājasrastanīlāṁśukāparā |ālakṣyarasanā reje sphuradvidyudiva kṣapā || 433
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 34 Others with their golden zones tinkling wandered about here and there showing to him their hips veiled with thin cloth,kāścitkanakakāṁcībhirmukharābhiritastataḥ |babhramurdarśayaṁtyo sya śroṇīstanvaṁśukāvṛtāḥ || 434
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 35 Others leaned holding a mango-bough in full flower displaying their bosoms like golden jars,cūtaśākhāṁ kusumitāṁ pragṛhyānyā lalaṁbire |suvarṇakalaśaprakhyān darśayaṁtyaḥ payodharān || 435
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 36 Another coming from a lotus-bed carrying lotuses and with eyes like lotuses stood like the lotus-goddess Padmā by the side of that lotus-faced prince,kācitpadmavanādetya sapadmā padmalocanā |padmavaktrasya pārśve sya padmaśrīriva tasthuṣī || 436
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 37 Another sang a sweet song easily understood and with the proper gesticulations rousing him self-subdued though he was by her glances as saying O how thou art deluded’,madhuraṁ gītamanvarthaṁ kācitsābhinayaṁ jagau |taṁ svasthaṁ codayaṁtīva vaṁcito sītyavekṣitaiḥ || 437
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 38 Another having armed herself 09 with her bright face with its brow-bow drawn to its full imitated his action as playing the hero,śubhena vadanenānyā bhrūkārmukavikarṣiṇā |prāvṛtyānucakārāsya ceṣṭitaṁ vīralīlayā || 438
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 39 Another with beautiful full bosoms and having her earrings waving in the wind 10 laughed loudly at him as if saying Catch me sir if you can’,pīnavalgustanī kācidvātāghūrṇitakuṁḍalā |uccairavajahāsainaṁ samāpnotu bhavāniti || 439
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 40 Some as he was going away bound him with strings of garlands — others punished him with words like an elephant-driver’s hook gentle yet reproachful,apayāntaṁ tathaivānyā babaṁdhurmālyadāmabhiḥ |kāścitsākṣepamadhurairjagṛhurvacanāṁkuśaiḥ || 440
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 41 Another wishing to argue with him seizing a mango-spray asked all bewildered with passion This flower whose is it’,pratiyogārthinī kācidgṛhītvā cūtavallarīm |idaṁ puṣpaṁ tu kasyeti papraccha madaviklavā || 441
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 42 Another assuming a gait and attitude like those of a man said to him Thou who art conquered by women go and conquer this earth’,kācitpuruṣavatkṛtvā gatiṁ saṁsthānameva ca |uvācainaṁ jitaḥ strībhirjaya bhoḥ pṛthivīmimām || 442
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 43 Then another with rolling eyes smelling a blue lotus thus addressed the prince with words slightly indistinct in her excitement,atha loleksaṇā kācijjighraṁtī nīlamutpalam |kiṁcinmadakalairvākyairnṛpātmajamabhāṣata || 443
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 44 See my lord this mango covered with its honey-scented flowers where the kokila sings as if imprisoned in a golden cage,paśya bhartaścitaṁ cūtaṁ kusumairmadhugaṁdhibhiḥ |hemapaṁjararuddho vā kokilo yatra kūjati || 444
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 45 Come and see this aśoka tree which augments lovers’ sorrows — where the bees make a noise as if they were scorched by fire,aśoko dṛśyatāmeṣa kāmiśokavivardhanaḥ |ruvaṁti bhramarā yatra dahyamānā ivāgninā || 445
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 46 Come and see this tilaka tree embraced by a slender mango-branch like a man in a white garment by a woman decked with yellow unguents,cūtayaṣṭyā samāśliṣṭo dṛśyatāṁ tilakadrumaḥ |śuklavāsā iva naraḥ striyā pītāṁgarāgayā || 446
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 47 Behold this kuruvaka in flower bright like fresh 11 resin-juice which bends down as if it felt reproached by the colour of women’s nails 12,phullaṁ kuruvakaṁ paśya nirmuktālaktakaprabham |yo nakhaprabhayā strīṇāṁ nirbhartsita ivānataḥ || 447
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 48 Come and see this young aśoka covered all over with new shoots which stands as it were ashamed at the beauty of our hands,bālāśokaśca nicito dṛśyatāmeṣa pallavaiḥ |yo smākaṁ hastaśobhābhirlajjamāna iva sthitaḥ || 448
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 49 See this lake surrounded by the sinduvāra shrubs growing on its banks 13 like a fair woman reclining clad in fine white cloth,dīrghikāṁ prāvṛtāṁ paśya tīrajaiḥ siṁduvārakaiḥ |pāṁḍurāṁśukasaṁvītāṁ śayānāṁ pramadāmiva || 449
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 50 See the imperial power of females — yonder ruddy-goose in the water goes behind his mate following her like a slave,dṛśyatāṁ strīṣu māhātmyaṁ cakravāko hyasau jale |pṛṣṭhataḥ preṣyavadbhāryāmanuvṛtyānugacchati || 450
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 51 Come and listen to the notes of this intoxicated cuckoo as he sings while another cuckoo sings as if consenting wholly without care,mattasya parapuṣṭasya ruvataḥ śrūyatāṁ dhvaniḥ |aparaḥ kokilo nutkaḥ pratiśrutyeva kūjati || 451
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 52 Would that thine was the intoxication of the birds which the spring produces — and not the thought of a thinking man ever pondering how wise he is’,api nāma vihaṁgānāṁ vasaṁtenāhito madaḥ |na tu ciṁtayataścittaṁ janasya prājñamāninaḥ || 452
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 53 Thus these young women their souls carried away by love assailed the prince with all kinds of stratagems,ityevaṁ tā yuvatayo manmathoddāmacetasaḥ |kumāraṁ vividhaistaistairupacakramire nayaiḥ || 453
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 54 But although thus attacked he having his senses guarded by self-control neither rejoiced nor smiled thinking anxiously One must die’,evamākṣipyamāṇo pi sa tu dhairyāvṛteṁdriyaḥ |martavyamiti sodvego na jaharṣa na sismiye || 454
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 55 Having seen them in their real condition 14 that best of men pondered with an undisturbed 15 and stedfast mind,tāsāṁ tattvena vasthānaṁ dṛṣṭvā sa puruṣottamaḥ |sasaṁvignena dhīreṇa ciṁtayāmāsa cetasā || 455
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 56 What is it that these women lack 16 that they perceive not that youth is fickle for this old age will destroy whatever has beauty,kiṁ vinā nāvagacchaṁti capalaṁ yauvanaṁ striyaḥ |yato rūpeṇa saṁpannaṁ jareyaṁ nāśayiṣyati || 456
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 57 Verily they do not see any one’s plunge into disease and so dismissing fear they are joyous in a world which is all pain,nūnametā na paśyaṁti kasyacid rogasaṁplavam |tathā hṛṣṭā bhayaṁ tyaktvā jagati vyādhidharmiṇi || 457
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 58 Evidently they know nothing of death which carries all away and so at ease and without distress they can sport and laugh,anabhijñāśca suvyaktaṁ mṛtyoḥ sarvāpahāriṇaḥ |tathā svasthā nirudvegāḥ krīḍaṁti ca hasaṁti ca || 458
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 59 What rational being who knows of old age death and sickness could stand 17 or sit down at his ease or sleep far less laugh,jarāṁ mṛtyuṁ ca vyādhiṁ ca ko hi jānan sacetanaḥ |svasthastiṣṭhan niṣīdedvā supedvā kiṁ punarhaset || 459
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 60 But he verily is like one bereft of sense who beholding another aged or sick or dead remains self-possessed and not afflicted,yastu dṛṣṭvā paraṁ jīrṇaṁ vyādhitaṁ mṛtameva ca |svastho bhavati nodvigno yathācetāstathaiva saḥ || 460
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 61 ‘(So) even when a tree is deprived of its flowers and fruits or if it is cut down and falls no other tree sorrows’,viyujyamāne pi tarau puṣpairapi phalairapi |patati cchidyamāne vā taruranyo na śocate || 461
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 62 Seeing him thus absorbed in contemplation with his desires estranged from all worldly objects Udāyin well skilled in the rules of policy with kindly feelings addressed him,iti dhyānaparaṁ dṛṣṭvā viṣayebhyo gataspṛham |udāyī nītiśāstrajñastamuvāca suhṛttayā || 462
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 63 Since I was appointed by the king as a fitting friend for thee therefore I have a wish to speak to thee in this friendliness of my heart,ahaṁ nṛpatinā dattaḥ sakhā tubhyaṁ kṣamaḥ kila |yasmāttvayi vivakṣā me tayā praṇayavattayā || 463
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 64 To hinder from what is disadvantageous to urge to what is advantageous — and not to forsake in misfortune — these are the three marks of a friend,ahitāt pratiṣedhaśca hite cānupravartanam |vyasane cāparityāgastrividhaṁ mitralakṣaṇam || 464
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 65 If I after having promised my friendship were not to heed when thou turnest away from the great end of man there would be no friendship in me,so haṁ maitrīṁ pratijñāya puruṣārthātparāṅmukham |yadi tvāṁ samupekṣeyaṁ na bhavenmitratā mayi || 465
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 66 Therefore I speak as thy friend — such rudeness as this to women is not befitting for one young in years and graceful in person,tadbravīmi suhṛdbhūtvā taruṇasya vapuṣmataḥ |idaṁ na pratirūpaṁ te strīṣvadākṣiṇyamīdṛśam || 466
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 67 It is right to woo a woman even by guile this is useful both for getting rid of shame and for one’s own enjoyment,anṛtenāpi nārīṇāṁ yuktaṁ samanuvartanam |tadvrīḍāparihārārthamātmaratyarthameva ca || 467
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 68 Reverential behaviour and compliance with her wishes are what binds a woman’s heart good qualities truly are a cause of love and women love respect,saṁnatiscānuvṛttiśca strīṇāṁ hṛdayabaṁdhanam |snehasya hi guṇā yonirmānakāmāśca yoṣitaḥ || 468
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 69 Wilt thou not then O large-eyed prince even if thy heart is unwilling seek to please them with a courtesy worthy of this beauty of thine,tadarhasi viśālākṣa hṛdaye pi parāṅmukhe |rūpasyāsyānurūpeṇa dākṣiṇyenānuvartitum || 469
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 70 Courtesy is the balm of women courtesy is the best ornament beauty without courtesy is like a grove without flowers,dākṣiṇyamauṣadhaṁ strīṇāṁ dākṣiṇyaṁ bhūṣaṇaṁ param |dākṣiṇyarahitaṁ rūpaṁ niṣpuṣpamiva kānanam || 470
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 71 But of what use is courtesy by itself let it be assisted by the heart’s feelings surely when worldly objects so hard to attain are in thy grasp thou wilt not despise them,kiṁ vā dākṣiṇyamātreṇa bhāvenāstu parigrahaḥ |viṣayān durlabhāṁllabdhvā na hyavajñātumarhasi || 471
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 72 Knowing that pleasure was the best of objects even the god Puraṁdara (Indra) wooed in olden time Ahalyā the wife of the saint Gautama,kāmaṁ paramiti jñātvā devo pi hi puraṁdaraḥ |gautamasya muneḥ patnīmahalyāṁ cakame purā || 472
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 73 So too Agastya wooed Rohiṇī the wife of Soma and therefore as Śruti saith a like thing befell Lopāmudrā 18,agastyaḥ prārthayāmāsa somabhāryāṁ ca rohiṇīm |tasmāt tatsadṛśaṁ lebhe lopāmudrāmiti śrutiḥ || 473
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 74 The great ascetic Vṛhaspati begot Bharadvāja on Mamatā the daughter of the Maruts the wife of Autathya 19,autathyasya ca bhāryāyāṁ mamatāyāṁ mahātapāḥ |mārutyāṁ janayāmāsa bharadvājaṁ vṛhaspatiḥ || 474
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 75 The Moon the best of offerers begat Budha of divine nature on the spouse of Vṛhaspati as she was offering a libation 20,vṛhaspatermahiṣyāṁ ca juhvatyāṁ juhvatāṁ varaḥ |budhaṁ vibudhadharmāṇaṁ janayāmāsa caṁdramāḥ || 475
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 76 So too in old time Parāśara overpowered by passion on the bank of the Yamunā lay with the maiden Kālī who was the daughter of the son of the Water (Agni),kālīm caiva purā kanyāṁ jalaprabhavasaṁbhavām |jagāma yamunātīre jātarāgaḥ parāśaraḥ || 476
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 77 The sage Vaśiṣṭha through lust begot a son Kapiñjalāda on Akṣamālā a despised low-caste woman 21,mātaṁgyāmakṣamālāyāṁ garhitāyāṁ riraṁsayā |kapiṁjalādaṁ tanayaṁ vasiṣṭho janayanmuniḥ || 477
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 78 And the seer-king Yayāti even when the vigour of his prime was gone sported in the Caitraratha forest with the Apsaras Viśvācī,yayātiścaiva rājarṣirvayasyapi vinirgate |viśvācyāpsarasā sārdhaṁ reme caitrarathe vane || 478
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 79 And the Kaurava king Pāṇḍu though he knew that intercourse with his wife would end in death yet overcome by the beauty and good qualities of Mādrī yielded to the pleasures of love,strīsaṁsargaṁ vināśāṁtaṁ pāṁḍurjñātvāpi kauravaḥ |mādrīrūpaguṇākṣiptaḥ siṣeve kāmajaṁ sukham || 479
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 80 And so Karālajanaka when he carried off the Brāhman’s daughter incurred loss of caste thereby but he would not give up his love,karālajanakaścaiva hṛtvā brāhmaṇakanyakām |avāpa bhraṁśam apyeva na tu tyajecca manmatham || 480
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 81 Great heroes such as these pursued even contemptible desires for the sake of pleasure how much more so when they are praiseworthy of their kind,evamādyā mahātmāno viṣayān garhitānapi |ratihetorbubhujire prāgeva guṇasaṁhitān || 481
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 82 And yet thou a young man possessed of strength and beauty despisest enjoyments which rightly belong to thee and to which the whole world is devoted’,tvaṁ punarnyāyataḥ prāptān balavān rūpavān yuvā |viṣayānavajānāsi yatra saktamidaṁ jagat || 482
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 83 Having heard these specious words of his well-supported by sacred tradition the prince made reply in a voice like the thundering of a cloud,iti śrutvā vacastasya ślakṣṇamāgamasaṁhitam |meghastanitanirghoṣaḥ kumāraḥ pratyabhāṣata || 483
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 84 This speech manifesting affection is well-befitting in thee but I will convince thee as to where thou wrongly judgest me,upapannamidaṁ vākyaṁ sauhārdavyaṁjakaṁ tvayi |atra ca tvānuneṣyāmi yatra mā duṣṭhu manyase || 484
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 85 I do not despise worldly objects I know that all mankind are bound up therein but remembering that the world is transitory my mind cannot find pleasure in them,nāvajānāmi viṣayāñjāne lokaṁ tadātmakam |anityaṁ tu jaganmatvā nātra me ramate manaḥ || 485
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 86 Old age disease and death — if these three things did not exist I too should find my enjoyment in the objects that please the mind,jarā vyādhiśca mṛtyuśca yadi na syādidaṁ trayam |mamāpi hi manojñeṣu viṣayeṣu ratirbhavet || 486
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 87 Yet even though this beauty of women were to remain perpetual still delight in the pleasures of desire would not be worthy of the wise man,nityaṁ yadyapi hi strīṇāmetadeva vapurbhavet |sasaṁvitkasya kāmeṣu tathāpi na ratiḥ kṣamā || 487
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 88 But since their beauty will be drunk up by old age to delight therein through infatuation cannot be a thing approved even by thyself 22,yadā tu jarayā pītaṁ rūpamāsāṁ bhaviṣyati |ātmano pyanabhipretaṁ mohāttatra ratirbhavet || 488
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 89 He who himself subject to death disease and old age can sport undisturbed with those whose very nature implies death disease and old age such a man is on a level with birds and beasts,mṛtyuvyādhijarādharmo mṛtyuvyādhijarātmabhiḥ |ramamāṇo pyasaṁvignaḥ samāno mṛgapakṣibhiḥ || 489
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 90 And as for what thou sayest as to even those great men having become victims to desire do not be bewildered by them for destruction was also their lot,yadapyāttha mahātmānaste pi kāmātmakā iti |saṁvego tra na kartavyo yadā teṣāmapi kṣayaḥ || 490
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 91 Real greatness is not to be found there where there is universally destruction or where there is attachment to earthly objects or a want of self-control,māhātmyaṁ na ca tanmanye yatra sāmānyataḥ kṣayaḥ |viṣayeṣu prasaktirvā yuktirvā nātmavattayā || 491
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 92 And when thou sayest Let one deal with women even by guile I know nought about guile even if it be accompanied with courtesy,yadapyātthānṛtenāpi strījane vartyatāmiti |anṛtaṁ nāvagacchāmi dākṣiṇyenāpi kiṁcana || 492
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 93 That compliance too with a woman’s wishes pleases me not if truthfulness be not there if there be not a union with one’s whole soul and nature then out upon it say I,na cānuvartanaṁ tanme rucitaṁ yatra nārjavam |sarvabhāvena saṁparko yadi nāsti dhigastu tat || 493
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 94 A soul overpowered by passion believing in falsehood carried away by attachment and blind to the faults of its objects — what is there in it worth being deceived,anṛte śraddadhānasya saktasyādoṣadarśinaḥ |kiṁ hi vaṁcayitavyaṁ syājjātarāgasya cetasaḥ || 494
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 95 And if the victims of passion do deceive one another — are not men unfit for women to look at and women for men,vaṁcayaṁti ca yadyeva jātarāgāḥ parasparam |nanu naiva kṣamaṁ draṣṭuṁ narāḥ strīṇāṁ nṛṇām striyaḥ || 495
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 96 Since then these things are so thou surely wouldest not lead me astray into ignoble pleasures — me afflicted by sorrow and subject to old age and death,tadevaṁ sati duḥkhārttaṁ jarāmaraṇabhoginam |na māṁ kāmeṣvanāryeṣu pratārayitumarhasi || 496
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 97 Ah thy mind must be very firm and strong if thou canst find substance in the transitory pleasures of sense even in the midst of violent alarm thou canst cling to worldly objects when thou seest all created beings in the road of death,aho tidhīraṁ balavacca te manaścaleṣu kāmeṣu ca sāradarśinaḥ |bhaye pi tīvre viṣayeṣu sajjase nirīkṣamāṇo maraṇādhvani prajāḥ || 497
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 98 But I am fearful and exceedingly bewildered as I ponder the terrors of old age death and disease I can find no peace no self-command much less can I find pleasure while I see the world as it were ablaze with fire,ahaṁ punarbhīruratīvaviklavo jarāvipadvyādhibhayaṁ viciṁtayan |labhe na śāṁtiṁ na dhṛtiṁ kuto ratiṁ niśāmayan dīptamivāgninā jagat || 498
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 99 If desire arises in the heart of the man who knows that death is certain — I think that his soul must be made of iron who restrains it in this great terror and does not weep’,asaṁśayaṁ mṛtyuriti prajānato narasya rāgo hṛdi yasya jāyate |ayomayīṁ tasya paraimi cetanāṁ mahābhaye rakṣati yo na roditi || 499
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 100 Then the prince uttered a discourse full of resolve and abolishing the objects of desire and the lord of day whose orb is the worthy centre of human eyes departed to the Western Mountain,athau kumāraśca viniścayātmikāṁ cakāra kāmāśrayaghātinīṁ kathām |janasya cakṣurgamanīyamaṁḍalo mahīdharaṁ cāstamiyāya bhāskaraḥ || 4100
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 101 And the women having worn their garlands and ornaments in vain with their graceful arts and endearments all fruitless concealing their love deep in their hearts 23 returned to the city with broken hopes,tato vṛthādhāritabhūṣaṇasrajaḥ kalāguṇaiśca praṇayaiśca niṣphalaiḥ |sva eva bhāve vinigṛhya manmathaṁ puraṁ yayurbhagnamanorathāḥ striyaḥ || 4101
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 102 Having thus seen the beauty 24 of the troop of women who had gone out to the city-garden now withdrawn in the evening — the prince pondering the transitoriness which envelopes all things entered his dwelling,tataḥ purodyānagatāṁ janaśriyaṁ nirīkṣya sāyaṁ pratisaṁhṛtāṁ punaḥ |anityatāṁ sarvagatāṁ viciṁtayan viveśa dhiṣṇyaṁ kṣitipālakātmajaḥ || 4102
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, na so nyatkāmebhyo niyamanamapaśyatsutamateḥ || 4103,tataḥ śrutvā rājā viṣayavimukhaṁ tasya tu manona śiśye tāṁ rātriṁ hṛdayagataśalyo gaja iva |
https//bitly/2wg2fa4, 103 Then the king when he heard how his mind turned away from all objects of sense could not lie down all that night like an elephant with an arrow in its heart but wearied in all sorts of consultation he and his ministers could find no other means beside these (despised) pleasures to restrain his son’s purpose,atha śrāṁto maṁtre bahuvividhamārge sasacivona so nyatkāmebhyo niyamanamapaśyatsutamateḥ || 4103
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 1 He the son of the Śākya king even though thus tempted by the objects of sense which infatuate others yielded not to pleasure and felt not delight like a lion deeply pierced in his heart by a poisoned arrow,sa tathā viṣayairvilobhyamānaḥ paramohairapi śākyarājasūnuḥ |na jagāma ratiṁ na śarma lebhe hṛdaye siṁha ivātidigdhaviddhaḥ || 51
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 2 Then one day accompanied by some worthy sons of his father’s ministers friends full of varied converse — with a desire to see the glades of the forest and longing for peace he went out with the king’s permission,atha maṁtrisutaiḥ kṣamaiḥ kadācitsakhibhiścitrakathaiḥ kṛtānuyātraḥ |vanabhūmididṛkṣayā śamepsurnaradevānumato vahiḥ pratasthe || 52
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 3 Having mounted his good horse Kaṁthaka decked with bells and bridle-bit of new gold with beautiful golden harness and the chowrie waving 01 he went forth like the moon 02 mounted on a comet,navarukmakhalīnakiṁkiṇīkaṁ pracalaccāmaracāruhemabhāṁḍam |abhiruhya sa kaṁṭhakaṁ sadaśvaṁ prayayau ketumiva drumābjaketuḥ || 53
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 4 Lured by love of the wood and longing for the beauties of the ground 03 he went to a spot near at hand 04 on the forest-outskirts and there he saw a piece of land being ploughed with the path of the plough broken like waves on the water,sa nikṛṣṭatarāṁ vanāṁtabhūmiṁ vanalobhācca yayau mahīguṇecchuḥ |salilormivikārasīramārgāṁ vasudhāṁ caiva dadarśa kṛṣyamāṇām || 54
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 5 Having beheld the ground in this condition with its young grass scattered and torn by the plough and covered with the eggs and young of little insects which were killed he was filled with deep sorrow as for the slaughter of his own kindred,halabhinnavikīrṇaśaṣpadarbhāṁ hatasūkṣmakrimikāṁḍajaṁtukīrṇām |samavekṣya rasāṁ tathāvidhāṁ tāṁ svajanasyeva badhe bhṛśaṁ śuśoca || 55
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 6 And beholding the men as they were ploughing their complexions spoiled by the dust the sun’s rays and the wind and their cattle bewildered with the burden of drawing the most noble one felt extreme compassion,kṛṣataḥ puruṣāṁśca vīkṣamāṇaḥ pavanārkāṁśurajovibhinnavarṇān |vahanaklamaviklavāṁśca dhuryān paramāryaḥ paramāṁ kṛpāṁ cakāra || 56
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 7 Having alighted from the back of his horse he went over the ground slowly overcome with sorrow — pondering the birth and destruction of the world he grieved exclaimed this is indeed pitiable’,avatīrya tatasturaṁgapṛṣṭhācchanakairgāṁ vyacarat śucā parītaḥ |jagato jananavyayaṁ vicinvan kṛpaṇaṁ khalvidamityuvāca cārttaḥ || 57
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 8 Then desiring to become perfectly lonely in his thoughts having stopped those friends who were following him he went to the root of a rose-apple in a solitary spot which had its beautiful leaves all tremulous (in the wind),manasā ca viviktatāmabhīpsuḥ suhṛdastānanuyāyino nivārya |abhitāralacāruparṇavatyā vijane mūlamupeyivān sa jaṁbvāḥ || 58
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 9 There he sat down on the ground covered with leaves 05 and with its young grass bright like lapis lazuli and meditating on the origin and destruction of the world he laid hold of the path that leads to firmness of mind,niṣasāda ca patrakhoravatyāṁ bhuvi vaidūryanikāśaśādvalāyām |jagataḥ prabhavavyayau viciṁtya manasaśca sthitimārgamālalaṁbe || 59
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 10 Having attained to firmness of mind 06 and being forthwith set free from all sorrows such as the desire of worldly objects and the rest he attained the first stage of contemplation unaffected by sin calm and argumentative’ 07,samavāptamanaḥ sthitiśca sadyo viṣayecchādibhirādhibhiśca muktaḥ |savitarkavicāramāpa śāṁtaṁ prathamaṁ dhyānamanāśravaprakāram || 510
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 11 Having then obtained the highest happiness sprung from deliberation 08 he next pondered this meditation — having thoroughly understood in his mind the course of the world,adhigamya tato vivekajaṁ tu paramaprītisukhaṁ  samādhim |idameva tataḥ paraṁ pradadhyau manasā lokagatiṁ niśamya samyak || 511
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 12 It is a miserable thing that mankind though themselves powerless 09 and subject to sickness old age and death yet blinded by passion and ignorant look with disgust on another who is afflicted by old age or diseased or dead,kṛpaṇaṁ vata yajjanaḥ svayaṁ sannaraso vyādhijarāvināśadharmaḥ |jarayārditamāturaṁ mṛtaṁ vā paramajño vijugupsate madāṁdhaḥ || 512
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 13 If I here being such myself should feel disgust for another who has such a nature it would not be worthy or right in me who know this highest duty’,iha cedahamīdṛśaḥ svayaṁ san vijugupseya paraṁ tathāsvabhāvam |na bhavetsadṛśaṁ hi tatkṣamaṁ vā paramaṁ dharmamimaṁ vijānato me || 513
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 14 As he thus considered thoroughly these faults of sickness old age and death which belong to all living beings all the joy which he had felt in the activity of his vigour his youth and his life vanished in a moment,iti tasya vipaśyato yathāvajjagato vyādhijarāvipattidoṣān |balayauvanajīvitapravṛttau vijagāmātmagato madaḥ kṣaṇena || 514
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 15 He did not rejoice he did not feel remorse he suffered no hesitation indolence nor sleep he felt no drawing towards the qualities of desire he hated not nor scorned another,na jaharṣa na cāpi cānutepe vicikitsāṁ na yayau na taṁdrinidre |na ca kāmaguṇeṣu saṁraraṁje na ca didveṣa paraṁ na cāvamene || 515
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 16 Thus did this pure passionless meditation grow within the great-souled one and unobserved by the other men there crept up a man in a beggar’s dress,iti buddhiriyaṁ ca nīrajaskā vavṛdhe tasya mahātmano viśuddhā |puruṣairaparairadṛśyamānaḥ puruṣaścopasasarpa bhikṣuveśaḥ || 516
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 17 The king’s son asked him a question — he said to him Tell me who art thou’ and the other replied Oh bull of men I being terrified at birth and death have become an ascetic for the sake of liberation,naradevasutastamabhyapṛcchadvada ko sīti śaśaṁsa so tha tasmai |sa ca puṁgava janmamṛtyubhītaḥ śramaṇaḥ pravrajito smi mokṣahetoḥ || 517
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 18 Desiring liberation in a world subject to destruction I seek that happy indestructible abode isolated from mankind with my thoughts unlike those of others and with my sinful passions turned away from all objects of sense,jagati kṣayadharmake mumukṣurmṛgaye haṁ śivamakṣayaṁ padaṁ tat |ajano nyajanairatulyabuddhirviṣayebhyo vinivṛttarāgadoṣaḥ || 518
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 19 Dwelling anywhere at the root of a tree or in an uninhabited house a mountain or a forest — I wander without a family and without hope a beggar ready for any fare seeking only the highest good’,nivasan kvacideva vṛkṣamūle vijane vāyatane girau vane vā |vicarāmyaparigraho nirāśaḥ paramārthāya yathopapannabhikṣuḥ || 519
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 20 When he had thus spoken while the prince was looking on he suddenly flew up to the sky it was a heavenly inhabitant who knowing that the prince’s thoughts were other than what his outward form promised had come to him for the sake of rousing his recollection,iti paśyata eva rājasūnoridamuktvā sa nabhaḥ samutpapāta |sa hi tadvapuranyabuddhidarśī smṛtaye tasya sameyivān divaukāḥ || 520
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 21 When the other was gone like a bird to heaven the foremost of men was rejoiced and astonished and having comprehended the meaning of the term dharma 10 he set his mind on the manner of the accomplishment of deliverance,gaganaṁ khagavadgate ca tasmin nṛvaraḥ saṁjahṛṣe visismiye ca |upalabhya tataśca dharmasaṁjñāmabhiniryāṇavidhau matiṁ cakāra || 521
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 22 Then like Indra himself and having tamed his senses — desiring to return home he mounted his noble steed and having made him turn back as he looked for his friends from that moment he sought no more the desired forest,tata iṁdrasamo jiteṁdriyaśca pravivikṣuḥ paramāśvamāruroha |parivartya janaṁ tvavekṣamāṇastata evābhimataṁ vanaṁ na bheje || 522
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 23 Ever seeking to make an end of old age and death fixing his thoughts in memory on dwelling in the woods he entered the city again but with no feelings of longing like an elephant entering an exercise-ground 11 after roaming in a forest-land,sa jarāmaraṇakṣayaṁ cikīrṣurvanavāsāya matiṁ smṛtau nidhāya |praviveśa punaḥ puraṁ na kāmādvanabhūmeriva maṁḍalaṁ dvipeṁdraḥ || 523
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 24 Happy truly and blessed is that woman whose husband is such as thou O long-eyed prince’ So on seeing him the princess exclaimed folding her hands to welcome him as he entered the road,sukhitā vata nirvṛtā ca sā strī patirīdṛktvamivāyatākṣa yasyāḥ |iti taṁ samudīkṣya rājakanyā praviśaṁtaṁ pathi sāṁjalirjagāda || 524
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 25 He whose voice was deep-sounding like a cloud heard this address and was filled with profound calm and as he heard the word blessed’ 12 he fixed his mind on the attainment of Nirvāṇa,atha ghoṣamimaṁ mahābhraghoṣaḥ pariśuśrāva śamaṁ paraṁ ca lebhe |śrutavāṁśca hi nirvṛteti śabdaṁ parinirvāṇavidhau matiṁ cakāra || 525
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 26 Then the prince whose form was like the peak of a golden mountain — whose eye voice and arm resembled a bull a cloud and an elephant 13 — whose countenance and prowess were like the moon and a lion — having a longing aroused for something imperishable — went into his palace,atha kāṁcanaśailaśṛṁgavarṣmā gajamegharṣabhabāhunisvanākṣaḥ |kṣayamakṣayadharmajātarāgaḥ śaśisiṁhānanavikramaḥ prapede || 526
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 27 Then stepping like a lion he went towards the king who was attended by his numerous counsellors like Sanatkumāra in heaven waiting on Indra resplendent in the assembly 14 of the Maruts,mṛgarājagatistato bhyagacchannṛpatiṁ maṁtrigaṇairupāsyamānam |samitau marutāmiva jvalaṁtaṁ maghavaṁtaṁ tridive sanatkumāraḥ || 527
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 28 Prostrating himself with folded hands he addressed him Grant me graciously thy permission O lord of men — I wish to become a wandering mendicant for the sake of liberation since separation is appointed for me’,praṇipatya ca sāṁjalirbabhāṣe diśa mahyaṁ naradeva sādhvanujñām |parivivrajiṣāmi mokṣahetorniyato hyasya janasya viprayogaḥ || 528
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 29 Having heard his words the king shook like a tree struck by an elephant and having seized his folded hands which were like a lotus he thus addressed him in a voice choked with tears,iti tasya vaco niśamya rājā kariṇevābhihato drumaścacāla |kamalapratime ṁjalau gṛhītvā vacanaṁ cedamuvāca vāṣpakaṁṭhaḥ || 529
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 30 O my son keep back this thought it is not the time for thee to betake thyself to dharma they say that the practice of religion is full of evils in the first period of life when the mind is still fickle,pratisaṁhara tāta buddhimetāṁ na hi kālastava dharmasaṁśrayasya |vayasi prathame matau calāyāṁ bahudoṣāṁ hi vadaṁti dharmacaryām || 530
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 31 The mind of the thoughtless ignorant young man whose senses are eager for worldly objects and who has no power of settled resolution for the hardships of vows of penance shrinks back from the forest for it is especially destitute of discrimination,viṣayeṣu kutūhaleṁdriyasya vratakhedeṣvasamarthaniścayasya |taruṇasya manaścalatyaraṇyādanabhijñasya viśeṣato vivekam || 531
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 32 It is high time for me to practise religion O my child of loved qualities 15 leaving my royal glory to thee who art well worthy to be distinguished by it but thy religion O firm-striding hero is to be accomplished by heroism it would be irreligion if thou wert to leave thine own father,mama tu priyadharma dharmakālastvayi lakṣmīmavasṛjya lakṣyabhūte |sthiravikrama vikrameṇa dharmastava hitvā tu guruṁ bhavedadharmaḥ || 532
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 33 Do thou therefore abandon this thy resolution devote thyself for the present to the duties of a householder to a man who has enjoyed the pleasures of his prime it is delightful to enter the penance-forest’,tadimaṁ vyavasāyamutsṛja tvaṁ bhava tāvannirato gṛhasthadharme |puruṣasya vayaḥsukhāni bhuktvā ramaṇīyo hi tapovanapraveśaḥ || 533
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 34 Having heard these words of the king he made his reply in a voice soft like a sparrow’s If thou wilt be my surety O king against four contingencies I will not betake myself to the forest,iti vākyamidaṁ niśamya rājñaḥ kalaviṁkasvara uttaraṁ babhāṣe |yadi me pratibhūścaturṣu rājan bhavasi tvaṁ na tapovanaṁ śrayiṣye || 534
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 35 Let not my life be subject to death and let not disease impair this health of mine let not old age attack my youth and let not misfortune destroy my weal’,na bhavenmaraṇāya jīvitaṁ me viharetsvāsthyamidaṁ ca me na rogaḥ |na ca yauvanamākṣipejjarā me na ca saṁpattimapāharedvipattiḥ || 535
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 36 When his son uttered a speech so hard to be understood the king of the Śākyas thus replied Abandon this idea bent upon departure extravagant desires are only ridiculous’,iti durlabhamarthamūcivāṁsaṁ tanayaṁ vākyamuvāca śākyarājaḥ |tyaja buddhimatimāṁ gatipravṛttāmavahāsyo timanorathakramaśca || 536
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 37 Then he who was firm as Mount Meru addressed his father If this is impossible then this course of mine is not to be hindered it is not right to lay hold of one who would escape 16 from a house that is on fire,atha merugururguruṁ babhāṣe yadi nāsti krama eṣa nāsti vāryaḥ |śaraṇājjvalanena dahyamānānna hi niścikramiṣuṁ kṣamaṁ grahītum || 537
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 38 As separation is inevitable to the world but not for Dharma 17 this separation is preferable will not death sever me helplessly my objects unattained and myself unsatisfied’,jagataśca yathā dhruvo viyogo na tu dharmāya varaṁ tvayaṁ viyogaḥ |avaśaṁ nanu viprayojayenmāmakṛtasvārthamatṛptameva mṛtyuḥ || 538
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 39 The monarch having heard this resolve of his son longing for liberation and having again exclaimed He shall not go’ set guards round him and the highest pleasures,iti bhūmipatirniśamya tasya vyavasāyaṁ tanayasya nirmumukṣoḥ |abhidhāya na yāsyatīti bhūyo vidadhe rakṣaṇamuttamāṁśca kāmān || 539
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 40 Then having been duly instructed 18 by the counsellors with all respect and affection according to the śāstras and being thus forbidden with tears by his father the prince sorrowing entered into his palace,sacivaistu nidarśito yathāvadbahumānāt praṇayācca śāstrapūrvam |guruṇā ca nivārito śrupātaiḥ praviveśāvasathaṁ tataḥ sa śocan || 540
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 41 There he was gazed at by his wives with restless eyes whose faces were kissed by their dangling earrings and whose bosoms were shaken with their thick-coming sighs — as by so many young fawns,calakuṇdalacuṁbitānanābhirghananiśvāsavikaṁpitastanībhiḥ |vanitābhiradhīralocanābhirmṛgaśāvābhirivābhyudīkṣyamāṇaḥ || 541
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 42 Bright like a golden mountain and bewitching the hearts of the noble women he enraptured their ears limbs eyes and souls by his speech touch form and qualities,sa hi kāṁcanaparvatāvadāto hṛdayonmādakaro varāṁganānām |śravanāṁgavilocanātmabhāvān vacanasparśavapurguṇairjahāra || 542
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 43 When the day was gone then shining with his form like the sun he ascended the palace as the rising sun ascends Mount Meru desiring to dispel the darkness by his own splendour,vigate divase tato vimānaṁ vapuṣā sūrya iva pradīpyamānaḥ |timiraṁ vijighāṁsurātmabhāsā ravirudyanniva merumāruroha || 543
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 44 Having ascended he repaired to a special golden seat decorated with embellishments of diamond with tall lighted candlesticks ablaze with gold and its interior filled with the incense of black aloe-wood,kanakojjvaladīptadīpavṛkṣaṁ varakālāgurudhūpapūrṇagarbham |adhiruhya sa vajrabhakticitraṁ pravaraṁ kāṁcanamāsanaṁ siṣeve || 544
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 45 Then the noblest of women waited during the night on the noblest of men who was like Indra himself with a concert of musical instruments as the crowds of heavenly nymphs wait on the son of the Lord of wealth 19 upon the summit of Himavat white like the moon,tata uttamamuttamāśca nāryo niśi tūryairupatasthuriṁdrakalpam |himavacchirasīva caṁdragaure draviṇeṁdrātmajamapsarogaṇaughāḥ || 545
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 46 But even by those beautiful instruments like heavenly music he was not moved to pleasure or delight since his desire to go forth from his home to seek the bliss of the highest end was never lulled,paramairapi divyatūryakalpaiḥ sa tu tairnaiva ratiṁ yayau na harṣam |paramārthasukhāya tasya sādhorabhiniścikramiṣā yato na reme || 546
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 47 Then by the power of the heavenly beings most excellent in self-mortification the Akaniṣṭhas who knew the purpose of his heart deep sleep was suddenly thrown on that company of women and their limbs and gestures became distorted 20,atha tatra suraistapovariṣṭhairakaniṣṭhairvyavasāyamasya buddhvā |yugapatpramadājanasya nidrā vihitāsīdvikṛtāśca gātraceṣṭāḥ || 547
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 48 One was lying there resting her cheek on her trembling arm leaving as in anger her lute though dearly loved which lay on her side decorated with gold-leaf,abhavacchayitā hi tatra kācidviniveśya pracale kare kapolam |dayitāmapi rukmapattracitrāṁ kupitevāṁkagatāṁ vihāya vīṇām || 548
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 49 Another shone with her flute clinging to her hand lying with her white garments fallen from her bosom — like a river whose banks are smiling with the foam of the water and whose lotuses are covered with a straight line of bees 21,vibabhau karalagnaveṇuranyā stanavisrastasitāṁśukā śayānā |ṛjuṣaṭpadapaṁktijuṣṭapadmā jalaphenaprahasattaṭā nadīva || 549
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 50 Another was sleeping 22 embracing her drum as a lover with her two arms tender like the shoot of young lotus and bearing their bracelets closely linked blazing with gold,navapuṣkaragarbhakomalābhyāṁ tapanīyojjvalasaṁgatāṁgadābhyām |svapiti sma tathā purā bhujābhyāṁ parirabhya priyavanmṛdaṁgameva || 550
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 51 Others decked with new golden ornaments and wearing peerless yellow garments fell down alas helpless with sleep like the boughs of the Karṇikāra broken by an elephant,navahāṭakabhūṣaṇāstathānyā vasanaṁ pītamanuttamaṁ vasānāḥ |avaśā vata nidrayā nipeturgajabhagnā iva karṇikāraśākhāḥ || 551
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 52 Another leaning on the side of a window with her willow-form bent like a bow shone as she lay with her beautiful necklace hanging down like a statue 23 in an archway made by art,avalaṁbya gavākṣapārśvamanyā śayitā cāpavibhugnagātrayaṣṭiḥ |virarāja vilaṁbicāruhārā racitā toraṇaśālabhaṁjikeva || 552
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 53 The lotus-face of another bowed down with the pinguent-lines on her person rubbed by the jewelled earrings appeared to be a lotus with its stalk bent into a half-circle and shaken by a duck standing on it 24,maṇikuṁḍaladaṣṭapatralekhaṁ mukhapadmaṁ vinataṁ tathāparasyāḥ |śatapatramivārdhacakranāḍaṁ sthitakāraṁḍavaghaṭṭitaṁ cakāśe || 553
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 54 Others lying as they sat with their limbs oppressed by the weight of their bosoms shone in their beauty mutually clasping one another with their twining arms decorated with golden bracelets,aparāḥ śayitā yathopaviṣṭāḥ stanabhārairavamanyamānagātrāḥ |upaguhya parasparaṁ virejurbhujapāśaistapanīyapārihāryaiḥ || 554
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 55 And another damsel lay sound asleep embracing her big lute as if it were a female friend and rolled it about while its golden strings trembled with her own face bright with her shaken earrings,mahatīṁ parivādinīṁ ca kācidvanitāliṁgya sakhīmiva prasuptā |vijughūrṇa calatsuvarṇasūtrāṁ vadanenākulakarṇikojjvalena || 555
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 56 Another lay with her tabour 25,paṇavaṁ yuvatirbhujāṁsadeśādavavisraṁsitacārupāśamanyā |savilāsaratāṁtatāṁtamūrvorvivare kāṁtamivābhinīya śiśye || 556
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 57 Others showed no lustre with their eyes shut although they were really full-eyed and fair-browed — like the lotus-beds with their buds closed at the setting of the sun,aparā na babhurnimīlitākṣyo vipulākṣyo pi śubhabhruvo pi satyaḥ |pratisaṁkucitāraviṁdakośāḥ savitaryastamite yathā nalinyaḥ || 557
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 58 Another with her hair loose and dishevelled and her skirts and ornaments fallen from her loins lay with her necklace in confusion like a woman crushed by an elephant and then dropped,śithilākulamūrdhajā tathānyā jaghanasrastavibhūṣaṇāṁśukāṁtā |aśayiṣṭa vikīrṇakaṁṭhasūtrā gajabhagnā pratipātitāṁganeva || 558
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 59 Others helpless and lost to shame though naturally self-possessed and endued with all graces of person breathed violently as they lay and yawned with their arms distorted and tossed about,aparāstvavaśā hriyā viyuktā dhṛtimatyo pi vapurguṇairupetāḥ |viniśaśvasurulvaṇaṁ śayānā vikṛtākṣiptabhujā jajṛṁbhire ca || 559
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 60 Others with their ornaments and garlands thrown off — unconscious with their garments spread out unfastened — their bright eyes wide open and motionless — lay without any beauty as if they were dead,vyapaviddhavibhūṣaṇasrajo nyā visṛtāgraṁthanavāsaso visaṁjñāḥ |animīlitaśuklaniścalākṣyo na virejuḥ śayitā gatāsukalpāḥ || 560
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 61 Another with fully-developed limbs her mouth wide open her saliva dropping and her person exposed lay as though sprawling in intoxication — she spoke not but bore every limb distorted,vivṛtāsyapuṭā vivṛddhagātrā prapatadvaktrajalā prakāśaguhyā |aparā madaghūrṇiteva śiśye na babhāṣe vikṛtaṁ vapuḥ pupoṣa || 561
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 62 Thus that company of women lying in different attitudes according to their disposition and family bore the aspect of a lake whose lotuses were bent down and broken by the wind,iti sattvakulānurūparūpaṁ vividhaṁ sa pramadājanaḥ śayānaḥ |sarasaḥ sadṛśaṁ babhāra rūpaṁ pavanāvarjitarugṇapuṣkarasya || 562
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 63 Then having seen these young women thus lying distorted and with uncontrolled gestures however excellent their forms and graceful their appearance — the king’s son felt moved with scorn,samavekṣya tataśca tāḥ śayānā vikṛtāstā yuvatīradhīraceṣṭāḥ |guṇavadvapuṣo pi valgubhāso nṛpasūnuḥ sa vigarhayāṁ babhūva || 563
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 64 Such is the nature of women impure and monstrous in the world of living beings but deceived by dress and ornaments a man becomes infatuated by a woman’s attractions,aśucirvikṛtaśca jīvaloke vanitānāmayamīdṛśaḥ svabhāvaḥ |vasanābharaṇaistu vaṁcyamānaḥ puruṣaḥ strīviṣayeṣu rāgameti || 564
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 65 If a man would but consider the natural state of women and this change produced in them by sleep assuredly he would not cherish his folly but he is smitten from a right will and so succumbs to passion’,vimṛśedyadi yoṣitāṁ manuṣyaḥ prakṛtiṁ svapnavikāramīdṛśaṁ ca |dhruvamatra na vardhayetpramādaṁ guṇasaṁkalpahatastu rāgameti || 565
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 66 Thus to him having recognised that difference there arose a desire to escape in the night and then the gods knowing his purpose caused the door of the palace to fly open,iti tasya tadaṁtaraṁ viditvā niśi niścikramiṣā samudbabhūva |avagamya manastato sya devairbhavanadvāramapāvṛtaṁ babhūva || 566
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 67 Then he went down from the roof of the palace scorning those women who lay thus distorted and having descended undauntedly he went out first into the courtyard 26,atha so vatatāra harmyapṛṣṭhādyuvatīstāḥ śayitā vigarhamāṇaḥ |avatīrya tataśca nirviśaṁko gṛhakakṣyāṁ prathamaṁ vinirjagāma || 567
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 68 Having awakened his horse’s attendant the swift Chaṁdaka he thus addressed him Bring me quickly my horse Kaṁthaka 27 I wish to-day to go hence to attain immortality,turagāvacaraṁ sa bodhayitvā javinaṁ chaṁdakamitthamityuvāca |hayamānaya kaṁthakaṁ tvarāvān amṛtaṁ prāptumito dya me yiyāsā || 568
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 69 Since such is the firm content which to-day is produced in my heart and since my determination is settled in calm resolve and since even in loneliness I seem to possess a guide — verily the end which I desire is now before me,hṛdi yā mama tuṣṭiradya jātā vyavasāyaśca yathā dhṛtau niviṣṭaḥ |vijane pi ca nāthavānivāsmi dhruvamartho bhimukhaḥ sa me ya iṣṭaḥ || 569
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 70 Since abandoning all shame and modesty these women lay before me as they did and the two doors opened of their own accord verily the time is come to depart for my true health’,hriyameva ca saṁnatiṁ ca hitvā śayitā matpramukhe yathā yuvatyaḥ |vivṛte ca yathā svayaṁ kapāṭe niyataṁ yātumanāmayāya kālaḥ || 570
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 71 Then accepting his lord’s command though he knew the purport of the king’s injunctions as being urged by a higher power in his mind he set himself to bring the horse,pratigṛhya tataḥ sa bharturājñāṁ viditārtho pi nareṁdraśāsanasya |manasīva pareṇa codyamānasturagasyānayane matiṁ cakāra || 571
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 72 Then he brought out for his master that noble steed his mouth furnished with a golden bit his back lightly touched by the bed on which he had been lying and endued with strength vigour speed and swiftness 28,atha hemakhalīnapūrṇavaktraṁ laghuśayyāstaraṇopagūḍhapṛṣṭham |balasattvajavatvaropapannaṁ sa varāśvaṁ tamupānināya bhartre || 572
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 73 With a long chine and root of the tail and heel — gentle with short hair back and ears — with his back belly and sides depressed and elevated with broad nostrils forehead hips and breast 29,pratatatrikapucchamūlapārṣṇiṁ nibhṛtaṁ hrasvatanūjapṛṣṭhakarṇam |vinatonnatapṛṣṭhakukṣipārśvaṁ vipulaprothalalāṭakaṭhyuraskam || 573
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 74 The broad-chested hero having embraced him and caressing him with his lotus-like hand ordered him with a gentle-toned voice as if he were desirous to plunge into the middle of an army,upaguhya sa taṁ viśālavakṣāḥ kamalābhena ca sāṁtvayan kareṇa |madhurākṣarayā girā śaśāsa dhvajinīmadhyamiva praveṣṭukāmaḥ || 574
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 75 Oftentimes have evil enemies been overthrown by the king when mounted on thee do thou O best of steeds so exert thyself that I too may obtain the highest immortality 30,bahuśaḥ kaliśatravo nirastāḥ samare tvāmadhiruhya pārthivena |ahamapyamṛtaṁ paraṁ yathāvatturagaśreṣṭha labheya tatkuruṣva || 575
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 76 Companions are easy to be found in battle or in the happiness obtained by winning worldly objects or in attaining wealth but companions are hard for a man to find who has fallen into misfortune or when he flies for refuge to Dharma,sulabhāḥ khalu saṁyuge sahāyā viṣayāvāptasukhe dhanārjane vā |puruṣasya tu durlabhāḥ sahāyāḥ patitasyāpadi dharmasaṁśraye vā || 576
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 77 And yet all those who in this world are companions whether in sinful custom or in seeking for Dharma — as my inner soul now recognises — they too are verily sharers in the common aim,iha caiva bhavaṁti ye sahāyāḥ kaluṣe dharmaṇi dharmasaṁśraye vā |avagacchati me yathāṁtarātmā niyataṁ te pi janāstadaṁśabhājaḥ || 577
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 78 Since then when I attain this righteous end my escape from hence will be for the good of the world — O best of steeds by thy speed and energy strive for thine own good and the good of the world’,tadidaṁ parigamya dharmayuktaṁ mama niryāṇamato jagaddhitāya |turagottama vegavikramābhyāṁ prayatasvātmahite jagaddhite ca || 578
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 79 Thus having exhorted the best of steeds like a friend to his duty he the best of men longing to go to the forest wearing a noble form in brightness like fire 31 mounted the white horse as the sun an autumnal cloud,iti suhṛdamivānuśiṣya kṛtye turagavaraṁ nṛvaro vanaṁ yiyāsuḥ |sitamasitagatidyutirvapuṣmān raviriva śāradamabhramāruroha || 579
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 80 Then that good steed avoiding all noises which would sound startling in the dead of night and awaken the household — all sound of his jaws hushed and his neighing silenced — went forth planting his hurrying steps at full speed,atha sa pariharanniśīthacaṁḍaṁ parijanabodhakaraṁ dhvaniṁ sadaśvaḥ |vigatahanuravaḥ praśāṁtaheṣaścakitavimuktapadakramā jagāma || 580
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 81 With their lotus-like hands whose fore-arms were adorned with golden bracelets the Yakṣas with their bodies bent down threw lotuses and bore up his hoofs as he rushed in startled haste,kanakavalayabhūṣitaprakoṣṭhaiḥ kamalanibhaiḥ kamalāni ca pravidhya |avanatatanavastato sya yakṣāścakitagaterdadhire khurān karāgraiḥ || 581
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 82 The city-roads which were closed with heavy gates and bars and which could be with difficulty opened 32 even by elephants flew open of their own accord without noise as the prince went through,guruparighakapāṭasaṁvṛtā yā na sukhamapi dviradairapāvriyaṁte |vrajati nṛpasute gatasvanāstāḥ svayamabhavan vivṛtāḥ puraḥ pratolyaḥ || 582
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 83 Firm in his resolve and leaving behind without hesitation his father who turned ever towards him 33 and his young son his affectionate people and his unparalleled magnificence he then went forth out of his father’s city,pitaramabhimukhaṁ sutaṁ ca bālaṁ janamanuraktamanuttamāṁ ca lakṣmīm |kṛtamatirapahāya nirvyapekṣaḥ pitṛnagarāt sa tato vinirjagāma || 583
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 84 Then he with his eyes long and like a full-blown lotus looking back on the city uttered a sound like a lion Till I have seen the further shore of birth and death I will never again enter the city called after Kapila’,atha sa vikacapaṁkajāyatākṣaḥ puramavalokya nanāda siṁhanādam |jananamaraṇayoradṛṣṭapāro na punarahaṁ kapilāhvayaṁ praviṣṭā || 584
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 85 Having heard this his utterance the troops of the court of the Lord of wealth 34 rejoiced and the hosts of the gods triumphing wished him a successful accomplishment of his purpose,iti vacanamidaṁ niśamya tasya draviṇapateḥ pariṣadgaṇā nanaṁduḥ | 585pramuditamanasaśca devasaṁghā vyavasitapāraṇamāśaśaṁsire smai ||
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 86 Other heavenly beings with forms bright like fire knowing that his purpose was hard to fulfil produced a light on his dewy path like the rays of the moon issuing from the rift of a cloud,hutavahavapuṣo divaukaso nye vyavasitamasya duṣkaraṁ viditvā |akuruta tuhine pathi prakāśaṁ ghanavivarapraṣṛtā iveṁdupādāḥ || 586
https//bitly/2vDja4a, 87 But he with his horse like the horse of Indra the lord of bay horses hurrying on as if spurred in his mind went over the leagues full of many conflicting emotions 35 — the sky all the while with its cloud-masses checkered with the light of the dawn,harituragaturaṁgavatturaṁgaḥ sa tu vicaran manasīva codyamānaḥ |aruṇaparuṣabhāramaṁtarīkṣaṁ sarasabahūni jagāma yojanāni || 587
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 1 Then when the sun the eye of the world was just risen he the noblest of men beheld the hermitage of the son of Bhṛgu,tato muhūrte bhyudite jagaccakṣuṣi bhāskare |bhārgavasyāśramapadaṁ sa dadarśa nṛṇāṁ varaḥ || 61
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 2 Its deer all asleep in quiet trust its birds tranquilly resting — seeing it he too became restful and he felt as if his end was attained,suptaviśvastahariṇaṁ svasthasthitavihaṁgamam |viśrāṁta iva yaddṛṣṭā kṛtārtha iva cābhavat || 62
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 3 For the sake of ending his wonder and to show reverence for the penances observed and as expressing his own conformity therewith 01 he alighted from the back of his horse,sa vismayanivṛttyarthaṁ tapaḥpūjārthameva ca |svāṁ cānuvartitāṁ rakṣannaśvapṛṣṭhādavātarat || 63
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 4 Having alighted he stroked the horse exclaiming All is saved’ and he spoke well-pleased to Chaṁdaka bedewing him as it were with tears from his eyes ,avatīrya ca pasparśa nistīrṇamiti vājinam |chaṁdakaṁ cābravīt prītaḥ snāpayanniva cakṣuṣā || 64
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 5 Good friend thy devotion to me and thy courage of soul have been proved by thy thus following this steed whose speed is like that of Tārkṣya 02,imaṁ tārkṣyopamajavaṁ turaṁgamanugacchatā |darśitā saumya madbhaktirvikramaścāyamātmanaḥ || 65
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 6 Bent even though I am on other business I am wholly won in heart by thee — one who has such a love for his master and at the same time is able to carry out his wish,sarvathāsmyanyakāryo pi gṛhīto bhavatā hṛdi |bhartṛsnehaśca yasyāyamīdṛśaḥ śakta eva ca || 66
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 7 One can be able without affection and affectionate though unable but one like thee at once affectionate and able is hard to find in the world,asnigdho pi samartho sti niḥsāmarthyo pi bhaktimān |bhaktimāṁscaiva śaktaśca durlabhastvadvidho bhuvi || 67
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 8 I am pleased with this noble action of thine this feeling is seen towards me even though I am regardless of conferring rewards,tatprīto smi tavānena mahābhāgena karmaṇā |dṛśyate mayi bhāvo yaṁ phalebhyo pi parāṅmukhe || 68
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 9 Who would not be favourably disposed to one who stands to him as bringing him reward but even one’s own people commonly become mere strangers in a reverse of fortune 03,ko janasya phalasthasya na syādabhimukho janaḥ |janībhavati bhūyiṣṭhaṁ svajano pi viparyaye || 69
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 10 The son is maintained for the sake of the family the father is honoured for the sake of our own (future) support the world shows kindness for the sake of hope there is no such a thing as unselfishness without a motive,kulārthaṁ dhāryate putraḥ poṣārthaṁ sevyate pitā |āśayāśliṣyati jagannāsti niṣkāraṇāsvatā || 610
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 11 Why speak many words in short thou hast done me a very great kindness take now my horse and return I have attained the desired wood’,kimuktvā bahu saṁkṣepātkṛtaṁ me sumahatpriyam |nivartasvāśvamādāya saṁprāpto smīpsitaṁ vanam || 611
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 12 Thus having spoken the mighty hero in his desire to show perfect gentleness 04 unloosed his ornaments and gave them to the other who was deeply grieved,ityuktvā sa mahābāhuranuśaṁsacikīrṣayā |bhūṣaṇānyavamucyāsmai saṁtaptamanase dadau || 612
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 13 Having taken a brilliant jewel whose effect illumined his diadem he stood uttering these words like the mountain Mandara with the sun resting on it,mukuṭoddīptakarmāṇaṁ maṇimādāya bhāsvaram |bruvan vākyamidaṁ tasthau sāditya iva maṁdaraḥ || 613
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 14 By thee with this jewel O Chaṁda having offered him repeated obeisance the king with his loving confidence still unshaken must be enjoined to stay his grief,anena maṇinā chaṁda praṇamya bahuśo nṛpaḥ |vijñāpyo muktaviśraṁbhaṁ saṁtāpavinivṛttaye || 614
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 15 “I have entered the ascetic-wood to destroy old age and death — with no thirst for heaven with no lack of love nor feeling of anger,jarāmaraṇanāśārthaṁ praviṣṭo smi tapovanam |na khalu svargatarṣeṇa nāsnehena na manyunā || 615
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 16 “Do not think of mourning for me who am thus gone forth from my home union however long it may last in time will come to an end,tadevamabhiniṣkrāṁtaṁ na māṁ śocitumarhasi |bhūtvāpi hi ciraṁ śleṣaḥ kālena na bhaviṣyati || 616
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 17 “Since separation is certain therefore is my mind fixed on liberation how shall there not be repeated severings from one’s kindred,dhruvo yasmācca viśleṣastasmānmokṣāya me matiḥ |viprayogaḥ kathaṁ na syādbhūyo pi svajanādibhiḥ || 617
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 18 “Do not think of mourning for me who am gone forth to leave sorrow behind it is the thralls of passion who are attached to desires the causes of sorrow for whom thou shouldst mourn,śokatyāgāya niṣkrāṁtaṁ na māṁ śocitumarhasi |śokahetuṣu kāmeṣu saktāḥ śocyāstu rāgiṇaḥ || 618
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 19 “This was the firm persuasion of our predecessors — I as one departing by a common road am not to be mourned for by my heir,ayaṁ ca kila pūrveṣāmasmākaṁ niścayaḥ sthiraḥ |iti dāyādabhūtena na śocyo smi pathā vrajan || 619
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 20 “At a man’s death there are doubtless heirs to his wealth but heirs to his merit are hard to find on the earth or exist not at all,bhavaṁti hyarthadāyādāḥ puruṣasya viparyaye |pṛthivyāṁ dharmadāyādā durlabhāstu na saṁti vā || 620
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 21 “Even though thou sayest He is gone at a wrong time to the wood’ — there is no wrong time for religious duty (dharma) life being fragile as it is,yadapi syādasamaye yāto vanamasāviti |akālo nāsti dharmasya jīvite caṁcale sati || 621
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 22 “Therefore my determination is I must seek my supreme good this very day’ what confidence can there be in life when death stands as our adversary,tasmādadyaiva me śreyaścetavyamiti niścayaḥ |jīvite ko hi viśraṁbho mṛtyau pratyarthini sthite || 622
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 23 Do thou address the king O friend with these and such-like words and do thou use thy efforts so that he may not even remember me,evamādi tvayā saumya vijñāpyo vasudhādhipaḥ |prayatethāstathā caiva yathā māṁ na smaredapi || 623
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 24 Yea do thou repeat to the king our utter unworthiness through unworthiness affection is lost — and where affection is lost there is no sorrow’,api nairguṇyamasmākaṁ vācyaṁ narapatau tvayā |nairguṇyāttyajyate snehaḥ snehatyāgānna śocyate || 624
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 25 Having heard these words Chaṁda overwhelmed with grief made reply with folded hands his voice choked by tears ,iti vākyamidaṁ śrutvā chaṁdaḥ saṁtāpaviklavaḥ |vāṣpagrathitayā vācā pratyuvāca kṛtāṁjaliḥ || 625
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 26 At this state of mind of thine causing affliction to thy kindred my mind O my lord sinks down like an elephant in the mud of a river,anena tava bhāvena bāṁdhavāyāsadāyinā |bhartaḥ sīdati me ceto nadīpaṁka iva dvipaḥ || 626
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 27 To whom would not such a determination as this of thine cause tears even if his heart were of iron — how much more if it were throbbing with love,kasya notpādayedvāṣpaṁ niścayaste yamīdṛśaḥ |ayomaye pi hṛdaye kiṁ punaḥ snehaviklave || 627
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 28 Where 05 is this delicacy of limb fit to lie only in a palace — and where is the ground of the ascetic forest covered with the shoots of rough kusa grass,vimānaśayanārhaṁ hi saukumāryamidaṁ kva ca |kharadarbhāṁkuravatī tapovanamahī kva ca || 628
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 29 When on hearing thy resolve I first brought thee this horse — it was fate only O my lord which made me do it mastering my will,śrutvā tu vyavasāyaṁ te yadaśvo yaṁ mayā hṛtaḥ |balātkāreṇa tannātha daivenaivāsmi kāritaḥ || 629
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 30 But how could I O king by mine own will knowing this thy decision — carry back the horse to the sorrow of Kapilavastu,kathaṁ hyātmavaśo jānan vyavasāyamimaṁ tava |upānayeyaṁ turagaṁ śokaṁ kapilavastunaḥ || 630
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 31 Surely thou wilt not abandon O hero that fond old king so devoted to his son as a heretic might the true religion,tannārhasi mahābāho vihātuṁ putralālasam |snigdhaṁ vṛddhaṁ ca rājānaṁ saddharmamiva nāstikaḥ || 631
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 32 And her thy second mother worn with the care of bringing thee up — thou wilt not surely forget her as an ingrate a benefit,saṁvardhanapariśrāṁtāṁ dvitīyāṁ tāṁ ca mātaram |deva nārhasi vismartuṁ kṛtaghna iva satkriyām || 632
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 33 Thou wilt not surely abandon thy queen endowed with all virtues illustrious for her family devoted to her husband and with a young son as a coward the royal dignity within his reach,bālaputrāṁ guṇavatīṁ kulaślāghyāṁ pativratām |devīmarhasi na tyaktuṁ klīvaḥ prāptāmiva śriyam || 633
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 34 Thou wilt not abandon the young son of Yaśodharā worthy of all praise thou the best of the cherishers of religion and fame as a dissolute spendthrift his choicest glory,putraṁ yāśodharaṁ ślāghyaṁ yaśodharmabhṛtāṁ varaḥ |bālamarhasi na tyaktuṁ vyasanīvottamaṁ yaśaḥ || 634
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 35 Or even if thy mind be resolved to abandon thy kindred and thy kingdom thou wilt not O master abandon me — thy feet are my only refuge,atha baṁdhuṁ ca rājyaṁ ca tyaktumeva kṛtā matiḥ |māṁ nārhasi vibho tyaktuṁ tvatpādau hi gatirmama || 635
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 36 I cannot go to the city with my soul thus burning leaving thee behind in the forest as Sumitra 06 left the son of Raghu,nāsmi yātuṁ puraṁ śakto dahyamānena cetasā |tvāmaraṇye parityajya sumitra iva rāghavam || 636
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 37 What will the king say to me returning to the city without thee or what shall I say to thy queens by way of telling them good news,kiṁ hi vakṣyati rājā māṁ tvadṛte nagaraṁ gatam |vakṣyāmyucitadarśitvātkiṁ tavāṁtaḥpurāṇi vā || 637
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 38 As for what thou saidst thou must repeat my unworthiness to the king — how shall I speak what is false of thee as of a sage without a fault,yadapyātthāpi nairguṇyaṁ vācyaṁ narapatāviti |kiṁ tadvakṣyāmyabhūtaṁ te nirdoṣasya muneriva || 638
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 39 Or even if I ventured to speak it with a heart ashamed and a tongue cleaving to my mouth who would think of believing it,hṛdayena salajjena jihvayā sajjamānayā |ahaṁ yadyapi vā brūyāṁ kastacchraddhātumarhati || 639
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 40 He who would tell of or believe the fierceness of the moon might tell of or believe thy faults O physician of faults,yo hi caṁdramasastaikṣṇya kathayecchraddadhīta vā |sa doṣāṁstava doṣajña kathayecchraddadhīta vā || 640
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 41 Him who is always compassionate and who never fails to feel pity it ill befits to abandon one who loves — turn back and have mercy on me’,sānukrośasya satataṁ nityaṁ karuṇavedinaḥ |snigdhatyāgo na sadṛśo nivartasva prasīda me || 641
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 42 Having heard these words of Chaṁda overcome with sorrow — self-possessed with the utmost firmness the best of speakers answered,iti śokābhibhūtasya śrutvā chaṁdasya bhāṣitam |svasthaḥ paramayā dhṛtyā jagāda vadatāṁ varaḥ || 642
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 43 Abandon this distress Chaṁda regarding thy separation from me — change is inevitable in corporeal beings who are subject to different births,madviyogaṁ prati cchaṁda saṁtāpastyajyatāmayam |nānābhāvo hi niyataṁ pṛthagjātiṣu dehiṣu || 643
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 44 Even if I through affection were not to abandon my kindred in my desire for liberation death would still make us helplessly abandon one another,svajanaṁ yadyapi snehānna tyajeyaṁ mumukṣayā |mṛtyuranyonyamavaśānasmān saṁtyājayiṣyati || 644
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 45 She my mother by whom I was borne in the womb with great thirst and pains — where am I now with regard to her all her efforts fruitless and where is she with regard to me,mahatyā tṛṣṇayā duḥkhairgarbheṇāsmi yayā dhṛtaḥ |tasyā niṣphalayatnāyāḥ kvāhaṁ mātuḥ kva sā mama || 645
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 46 As birds go to their roosting-tree and then depart so the meeting of beings inevitably ends in separation,vāsavṛkṣe samāgamya vigacchaṁti yathāṁḍajāḥ |niyataṁ viprayogāṁtastathā bhūtasamāgamaḥ || 646
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 47 As clouds having come together depart asunder again such I consider the meeting and parting of living things,sametya ca yathā bhūyo vyapayāṁti valāhakāḥ |saṁyogo viprayogaśca tathā me prāṇināṁ mataḥ || 647
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 48 And since this world goes away each one of us deceiving the other — it is not right to think anything thine own in a time of union which is a dream,yasmādyāti ca loko yaṁ vipralabhya parasparam |mamatvaṁ na kṣamaṁ tasmātsvapnabhūte samāgame || 648
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 49 Since the trees are parted from the innate colour of their leaves why should there not still more be the parting of two things which are alien to each other,sahajena viyujyaṁte parṇarāgeṇa pādapāḥ |anyenānyasya viśleṣaḥ kiṁ punarna bhaviṣyati || 649
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 50 Therefore since it is so grieve not my good friend but go or if thy love lingers then go and afterwards return,tadevaṁ sati saṁtāpaṁ mā kārṣīḥ saumya gamyatām |laṁbate yadi tu sneho gatvāpi punarāvraja || 650
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 51 Say without reproaching us to the people in Kapilavastu “Let your love for him be given up and hear his resolve,brūyāścāsmāsvanākṣepaṁ janaṁ kapilavastuni |tyajyatāṁ tadgataḥ snehaḥ śrūyatāṁ cāsya niścayaḥ || 651
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 52 “Either he will quickly come back having destroyed old age and death or else he will himself perish having failed in his purpose and lost hold of every support” ,kṣiprameṣyati vā kṛtvā jarāmṛtyukṣayaṁ kila |akṛtārtho nirālaṁbo nidhanaṁ yāsyatīti vā || 652
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 53 Having heard his words Kaṁthaka the noblest of steeds licked his feet with his tongue and dropped hot tears,iti tasya vacaḥ śrutvā kaṁthakasturagottamaḥ |jihvayā lilihe pādau vāṣpamuṣṇaṁ mumoca ca || 653
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 54 With his hand whose fingers were united with a membrane and which was marked with the auspicious svastika and with its middle part curved 07 the prince stroked him and addressed him like a friend,jālinā svastikāṁkena vakramadhyena pāṇinā |āmamarśa kumārastaṁ babhāṣe ca vayasyavat || 654
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 55 Shed not tears Kaṁthaka this thy perfect equine nature has been proved — bear with it this thy labour will soon have its fruit’,muṁca kaṁthaka mā vāṣpaṁ darśiteyaṁ sadaśvatā |mṛṣyatāṁ saphalaḥ śīghraṁ śramaste yaṁ bhaviṣyati || 655
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 56 Then seizing the sharp jewelled sword which was in Chaṁdaka’s hand he resolutely drew out from the sheath the blade decked with golden ornaments like a serpent from its hole,maṇitsaruṁ chaṁdakahastasaṁsthaṁ tataḥ sa dhīro niśitaṁ gṛhītvā |kośādasiṁ kāṁcanabhakticitraṁ vilādivāśīviṣamudbabarha || 656
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 57 Having drawn it forth dark blue like a blue lotus petal he cut his decorated tiara and his hair and he tossed it with its scattered muslin into the air as a grey goose into a lake,niṣkāsya taṁ cotpalapattranīlaṁ ciccheda citraṁ mukuṭaṁ sakeśam |vikīryamāṇāṁśukamaṁtarīkṣe cikṣepa cainaṁ sarasīva haṁsam || 657
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 58 And the heavenly beings with a longing to worship it seized it respectfully as it was thrown up and the divine hosts paid it due adoration in heaven with celestial honours,pūjābhilāṣeṇa ca bāhumānyāddivaukasastaṁ jagṛhuḥ praviddham |yathāvadenaṁ divi devasaṁghā divyairviśeṣairmahayāṁ ca cakruḥ || 658
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 59 Having thus divorced his ornaments and banished all royal magnificence from his head and seeing his muslin floating away like a golden goose the stedfast prince desired a sylvan dress,muktvā tvalaṁkārakalatravattāṁ śrīvipravāsaṁ śirasaśca kṛtvā |dṛṣṭvāṁśukaṁ kāṁcanahaṁsacitram vanyaṁ sa dhīro bhicakāṁkṣa vāsaḥ || 659
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 60 Then a celestial being wearing the form of a hunter pure in heart knowing his thoughts approached near him in dark-red garments and the son of the Śākya king thus addressed him,tato mṛgavyādhavapurdivaukā bhāvaṁ viditvāsya viśuddhabhāvaḥ |kāṣāyavastro bhiyayau samīpaṁ taṁ śākyarājaprabhavo bhyuvāca || 660
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 61 Thy red garments are auspicious the sign of a saint but this destructive bow is not befitting therefore my good friend if there is no strong preference in the matter do thou give me that dress and take this of mine’,śivaṁ ca kāṣāyamṛṣidhvajaste na yujyate hiṁsramidaṁ dhanuśca |tatsaumya yadyasti na saktiratra mahyaṁ prayacchedamidaṁ gṛhāṇa || 661
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 62 The hunter replied It has given me my desire 08 O giver of desires as by this I have inspired animals with confidence and then killed them but if thou hast need of it O thou who art like Indra accept it at once and give me the white dress’,vyādho bravītkāmada kāmamārādanena viśvāsya mṛgān nihatya |arthastu śakropama yadyanena haṁta pratīcchānaya śuklametat || 662
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 63 With extreme joy he then took that sylvan dress and gave away the linen one and the hunter assuming his heavenly form having taken the white garment went to heaven,pareṇa harṣeṇa tataḥ sa vanyaṁ jagrāha vāso ṁśukamutsasarja |vyādhastu divyaṁ vapureva bibhrat tacchuklamādāya divaṁ jagāma || 663
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 64 Then the prince and the attendant of the horse were filled with wonder as he was thus going and forthwith they paid great honour anew to that sylvan dress,tataḥ kumāraśca sa cāśvagopastasmiṁstathā yāti visismiyāte |āraṇyake vāsasi caiva bhūyastasminnakārṣṭāṁ bahumānamāśu || 664
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 65 Then the great-souled one having dismissed the weeping Chaṁda and wearing his fame veiled by the sign of the red garment went towards the hermitage like the king of mountains wrapped in an evening cloud,chaṁdaṁ tataḥ sāśrumukhaṁ visṛjya kāṣāyasaṁvidvṛtakīrtibhṛtsaḥ |yenāśramastena yayau mahātmā saṁdhyābhrasaṁvīta ivādrirājaḥ || 665
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 66 While his master thus regardless of his kingdom was going to the ascetic-wood in mean garments the groom tossing up his arms wailed bitterly and fell on the ground,tatastathā bhartari rājyaniḥspṛhe tapovanaṁ yāti vivarṇavāsasi |bhujau samutkṣipya tataḥ sa vājibhṛdbhṛśaṁ vicukrośa papāta ca kṣitau || 666
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 67 Having looked again he wept aloud and embraced the horse Kaṁthaka with his arms and then hopeless and repeatedly lamenting he went in body to the city not in soul,vilokya bhūyaśca ruroda sasvaraṁ hayaṁ bhujābhyāmupaguhya kaṁthakam |tato nirāśo vilapanmuhurmuhuryayau śarīreṇa puraṁ na cetasā || 667
https//bitly/2vGxl75, 68 Sometimes he pondered sometimes he lamented sometimes he stumbled and sometimes he fell and so going along wretched through his devoted attachment he performed all kinds of actions in the road without conscious will,kvacitpradadhyau vilalāpa ca kvacit kvacitpracaskhāla papāta ca kvacit |ato vrajan bhaktivaśena duḥkhitaścacāra bahvīravaśaḥ pathi kriyāḥ || 668
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 1 Then having left the weeping tear-faced Chaṁda — indifferent to all things in his longing for the forest he by whom all objects are accomplished overpowering the place by his beauty entered that hermitage as if it were fully blessed,tato visṛjyāśrumukhaṁ rudaṁtaṁ chaṁdaṁ vanacchaṁdatayā nirāsthaḥ |sarvārthasiddho vapuṣābhibhūya tamāśramaṁ siddhamiva prapede || 71
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 2 He the prince with a gait like the lion’s having entered that arena of deer himself like a deer — by the beauty of his person even though bereft of his magnificence attracted the eyes of all the dwellers in the hermitage,sa rājasūnurmṛgarājagāmī mṛgājiraṁ tanmṛgavat praviṣṭaḥ |lakṣmīviyukto pi śarīralakṣmyā cakṣūṁṣi sarvāśramiṇāṁ jahāra || 72
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 3 The drivers of wheeled carriages also with their wives stood still in curiosity holding the yokes in their hands — they gazed on him who was like Indra and moved not standing like their beasts of burden with their heads half bent down,sthitā hi hastasthayugāstathaiva kautūhalāccakradharāḥ sadārāḥ |tamiṁdrakalpaṁ dadṛśurna jagmurdhuryā ivārdhāvanataiḥ śirobhiḥ || 73
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 4 And the Brāhmans who had gone outside for the sake of fuel having come with their hands full of fuel flowers and kusa grass — pre-eminent as they were in penances and proficients in wisdom went to see him and went not to their cells,viprāśca gatvā bahiridhmahetoḥ prāptāḥ samitpuṣpapavitrahastāḥ |tapaḥpradhānāḥ kṛtabuddhayo pi taṁ draṣṭumīyurna maṭhānabhīyuḥ || 74
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 5 Delighted the peacocks uttered their cries as if they had seen a dark-blue cloud rising up and leaving the young grass and coming forward the deer with restless eyes and the ascetics who grazed like deer 01 stood still,hṛṣṭāśca kekā mumucurmayūrā dṛṣṭvāṁbudaṁ nīlamivonnamaṁtam |śaṣpāṇi hitvābhimukhāśca tasthurmṛgāścalākṣā mṛgacāriṇaśca || 75
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 6 Beholding him the lamp of the race of Ikṣvāku shining like the rising sun — even though their milking was over being filled with joy the oblation-giving cows poured forth their milk,dṛṣṭvā tamikṣvākukulapradīpaṁ jvalaṁtamudyaṁtamivāṁśumaṁtam |kṛte pi dohe janitapramodāḥ prasusruvurhomaduhaśca gāvaḥ || 76
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 7 It is one of the eight Vasus or one of the two Aśvins descended here’ — these words arose uttered aloud by the sages in their astonishment at seeing him,kaścidvasūnāmayamaṣṭamaḥ syātsyādaśvinoranyataraścyuto tra |ucceruruccairiti tatra vācastaddarśanādvismayajā munīnām || 77
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 8 Like a second form of the lord of the gods 02 like the personified glory of the universe he lighted up the entire wood like the sun come down of his own accord,lekharṣabhasyeva vapurdvitīyaṁ dhāmeva lokasya carācarasya |sa dyotayāmāsa vanaṁ hi kṛtsnaṁ yadṛcchayā sūrya ivāvatīrṇaḥ || 78
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 9 Then he being duly honoured and invited to enter by those dwellers in the hermitage paid his homage to the saints with a voice like a cloud in the rainy season 03,tataḥ sa tairāśramibhiryathāvadabhyarcitaścopanimaṁtritaśca |pratyarcayāṁ dharmabhṛto babhūva svareṇa bhādrāṁbudharopamena || 79
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 10 He the wise one longing for liberation traversed that hermitage filled with the holy company desirous of heaven — gazing at their strange penances,kīrṇaṁ tataḥ puṇyakṛtā janena svargābhikāmena vimokṣakāmaḥ |tamāśramaṁ so nucacāra dhīrastapāṁsi citrāṇi nirīkṣamāṇaḥ || 710
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 11 He the gentle one having seen the different kinds of penance practised by the ascetics in that sacred grove — desiring to know the truth thus addressed one of the ascetics who was following him,tapovikārāṁśca nirīkṣya saumyastapovane tatra tapodhanānām |tapasvinaṁ kaṁcidanuvrajaṁtaṁ tattvaṁ vijijñāsuridaṁ babhāṣe || 711
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 12 Since this to-day is my first sight of a hermitage I do not understand this rule of penance therefore will your honour kindly explain to me what resolve possesses each one of you’,tatpūrvamadyāśramadarśanaṁ me yasmādimaṁ dharmavidhiṁ na jāne |tasmādbhavānarhati bhāṣituṁ me yo niścayo yaṁ prati vaḥ pravṛttaḥ || 712
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 13 Then the Brāhman well-versed in penance told in order to that bull of the Śākyas a very bull in prowess all the various kinds of penance and the fruit thereof,tato dvijātiḥ sa tapovihāraḥ śākyarṣabhāyarṣabhavikramāya |kramena tasmai kathayāṁcakāra tapoviśeṣaṁ tapasaḥ phalaṁ ca || 713
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 14 Uncultivated food growing out of the water leaves water and roots and fruits — this is the fare of the saints according to the sacred texts but the different alternatives of penance vary,agrāmyamannaṁ salilaprarūḍhaṁ parṇāni toyaṁ phalamūlameva |yathāgamaṁ vṛttiriyaṁ munīnāṁ bhinnāstu te te tapasāṁ vikalpāḥ || 714
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 15 Some live like the birds on gleaned corn others graze on grass like the deer others live on air with the snakes as if turned into ant-hills 04,uṁchena jīvaṁti khagā ivānye tṛṇāni kecinmṛgavaccaraṁti |kecidbhujaṁgaiḥ saha vartayaṁti valmīkabhūtā iva mārutena || 715
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 16 Others win their nourishment with great effort from stones others eat corn ground with their own teeth some having boiled for others dress for themselves what may chance to be left,aśmaprayatnārjitavṛttayo nye kecitsvadaṁtāpahatānnabhakṣāḥ |kṛtvā parārthaṁ śrapaṇaṁ tathānye kurvaṁti kāryaṁ yadi śeṣamasti || 716
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 17 Others with their tufts of matted hair continually wet with water twice offer oblations to Agni with hymns others plunging like fishes into the water dwell there with their bodies scratched by tortoises,kecijjalaklinnajaṭākalāpā dviḥ pāvakaṁ juhvati maṁtrapūrvam |mīnaiḥ samaṁ kecidapo vigāhya vasaṁti kūrmollikhitaiḥ śarīraiḥ || 717
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 18 By such penances endured for a time — by the higher they attain heaven by the lower the world of men by the path of pain they eventually dwell in happiness — pain they say is the root of merit’,evaṁvidhaiḥ kālacitaistapobhiḥ parairdivaṁ yāṁtyaparairnṛlokam |duḥkhena mārgeṇa sukhaṁ kṣiyaṁti duḥkhaṁ hi dharmasya vadaṁti mūlam || 718
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 19 The king’s son having heard this speech of the ascetic even though he saw no lofty truth in it 05 was not content but gently uttered these thoughts to himself,ityevamādi dvipadeṁdravatsaḥ śrutvā vacastasya tapodhanasya |adṛṣṭatattvo pi na saṁtutoṣa śanairidaṁ cātmagataṁ jagāda || 719
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 20 The penance is full of pain and of many kinds and the fruit of the penance is mainly heaven at its best and all the worlds are subject to change verily the labour of the hermitages is spent for but little gain,duḥkhātmakaṁ naikavidhaṁ tapaśca svargapradhānaṁ tapasaḥ phalaṁ ca |lokāśca sarve pariṇāmavaṁtaḥ svalpe śramaḥ khalvayamāśramāṇām || 720
