https//bitly/2jICUB6, 21 Those who abandoning wealth kindred and worldly objects undertake vows for the sake of heaven — they when parted only wish to go to a still greater wood of their own again 06,śriyaṁ ca baṁdhūn viṣayāṁśca hitvā ye svargahetau niyamaṁ caraṁti |te viprayuktāḥ khalu gaṁtukāmā mahattaraṁ svaṁ vanameva bhūyaḥ || 721
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 22 He who by all these bodily toils which are called penances seeks a sphere of action for the sake of desire — not examining the inherent evils of mundane existence he only seeks pain by pain,kāyaklamairyaśca tapo bhidhānaiḥ pravṛttimākāṁkṣati kāmahetoḥ |saṁsāradoṣānaparīkṣamāṇo duḥkhena so nvicchati duḥkhameva || 722
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 23 There is ever to living creatures fear from death and they with all their efforts seek to be born again where there is action there must inevitably be death — he is always drowned therein just because he is afraid,trāsaśca nityaṁ maraṇātprajānāṁ yatnena cecchaṁti punaḥ prasūtim |satyāṁ pravṛttau niyataśca mṛtyustatraiva magno yata eva bhītaḥ || 723
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 24 Some undergo misery for the sake of this world others meet toil for the sake of heaven all living beings wretched through hope and always missing their aim fall certainly for the sake of happiness into misery,ihārthameke praviśaṁti khedaṁ svargārthamanye śramamāpnuvaṁti |sukhārthamāśākṛpaṇo kṛtārthaḥ patatyanarthe khalu jīvalokaḥ || 724
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 25 It is not the effort itself which I blame — which flinging aside the base pursues a high path of its own but the wise by all this common toil ought to attain that state in which nothing needs ever to be done again,na khalvayaṁ garhita eva yatno yo hīnamutsṛjya viśeṣagāmī |prājñaiḥ samānena pariśrameṇa kāryaṁ tu tadyatra punarna kāryam || 725
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 26 If the mortification of the body here is religion then the body’s happiness is only irreligion but by religion a man obtains happiness in the next world therefore religion here bears irreligion as its fruit,śarīrapīḍā tu yadīha dharmaḥ sukhaṁ śarīrasya bhavatyadharmaḥ |dharmeṇa cāpnoti sukhaṁ paratra tasmādadharmaṁ phalatīha dharmaḥ || 726
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 27 Since it is only by the mind’s authority that the body either acts or ceases to act therefore to control the thought is alone befitting — without the thought the body is like a log,yataḥ śarīraṁ manaso vaśena pravartate vāpi nivartate vā |yukto damaścetasa eva tasmāccittādṛte kāṣṭhasamaṁ śarīram || 727
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 28 If merit is gained by purity of food then there is merit also in the deer and in those men also who live as outcasts from all enjoyments through being estranged from them by the fault of their destiny,āhāraśuddhyā yadi puṇyamiṣṭaṁ tasmānmṛgāṇāmapi puṇyamasti |ye cāpi bāhyāḥ puruṣāḥ phalebhyo bhāgyāparādhena parāṅmukhatvāt || 728
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 29 If the deliberate choice of pain is a cause of merit why should not that same choice be directed to pleasure If you say that the choice of pleasure carries no authority is not the choice of pain equally without authority,duḥkhe bhisaṁdhistvatha puṇyahetuḥ sukhe pi kāryo nanu so bhisaṁdhiḥ |atha pramāṇaṁ na sukhe bhisaṁdhirduḥkhe pramāṇaṁ nanu nābhisaṁdhiḥ || 729
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 30 So too those who for the sake of purifying their actions earnestly sprinkle water on themselves saying this is a sacred spot — even there this satisfaction resides only in the heart — for waters will not cleanse away sin,tathaiva ye karmaviśuddhihetoḥ spṛśaṁtyapastīrthamiti pravṛttāḥ |tatrāpi toṣo hṛdi kevalo yaṁ na pāvayiṣyaṁti hi pāpamāpaḥ || 730
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 31 The water which has been touched by the virtuous — that is the spot if you wish for a sacred spot on the earth therefore I count as a place of pilgrimage only the virtues of a virtuous man’ 07 — water without doubt is only water’,spṛṣṭaṁ hi yadyadguṇavadbhiraṁbhastattatpṛthivyāṁ yadi tīrthamiṣṭam |tasmādguṇāneva paraimi tīrthamāpastu niḥsaṁśayamāpa eva || 731
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 32 Thus he uttered his discourse full of various arguments and the sun went down into the west then he entered the grove where penances had now ceased and whose trees were gray with the smoke of the (evening) oblations,iti sma tattadbahuyuktiyuktaṁ jagāda cāstaṁ ca yayau vivasvān |tato havirdhūmavivarṇavṛkṣaṁ tapaḥpraśāṁtaṁ sa vanaṁ viveśa || 732
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 33 Where the sacred fires had been duly transferred when kindled to other spots — all crowded with the holy hermits who had performed their ablutions and with the shrines of the gods murmuring with the muttered prayers — it seemed all alive like the full service of religion in exercise,abhyuddhṛtaprajvalitāgnihotraṁ kṛtābhiṣekarṣijanāvakīrṇam |jāpyasvanākūjitadevakoṣṭhaṁ dharmasya karmāṁtamiva pravṛttam || 733
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 34 He spent several nights there himself like the moon examining their penances and he departed from that penance-field feeling that he had comprehended the whole nature of penance,kāścinniśāstatra niśākarābhaḥ parīkṣamāṇaśca tapāṁsyuvāsa |sarvaṁ parikṣepya tapaśca matvā tasmāttapaḥkṣetratalājjagāma || 734
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 35 The dwellers of the hermitage followed him with their minds fixed on the greatness of soul visible in his person as if they were great seers beholding Religion herself withdrawn from a land invaded by the base,anvavrajannāśramiṇastatastaṁ tadrūpamāhātmyagatairmanobhiḥ |deśādanāryairabhibhūyamānānmahārṣayo dharmamivāpayāṁtam || 735
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 36 Then he looked on all those ascetics with their matted hair bark garments and rag-strips waving and he stood considering their penances under an auspicious and noble tree by the way-side,tato jaṭāvalkalacīrakhelāṁstapodhanāṁścaiva sa tāndadarśa |tapāṁsi caiṣāmanubudhyamānastasthau śive śrīmati mārgavṛkṣe || 736
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 37 Then the hermits having approached stood surrounding the best of men and an old man from among them thus addressed him respectfully in a gentle voice,athopasṛtyāśramavāsinastaṁ manuṣyavaryaṁ parivārya tasthuḥ |vṛddhaśca teṣāṁ bahumānapūrvaṁ kalena sāmnā giramityuvāca || 737
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 38 At thy coming the hermitage seems to have become full it becomes as it were empty when thou art gone — therefore my son thou wilt not surely desert it as the loved life the body of one who wishes to live,tvayyāgate pūrṇa ivāśramo bhūtsaṁpadyate śūnya iva prayāte |tasmādimaṁ nārhasi tāta hātuṁ jijīviṣordehamiveṣṭamāyuḥ || 738
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 39 In front stands the holy mountain Himavat inhabited by Brahmarṣis rājarṣis and surarṣis by whose mere presence the merit of these penances becomes multiplied to the ascetics,brahmarṣirājarṣisurarṣijuṣṭaḥ puṇyaḥ samīpe himavān hi śailaḥ |tapāṁsi tānyeva tapodhanānāṁ yatsaṁnikarṣādbahulībhavaṁti || 739
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 40 Near us also are holy spots of pilgrimage which become ladders to heaven loved by divine sages and saints whose souls are intent on devotion and who keep their souls in perfect control,tīrthāni puṇyānyabhitastathaiva sopānabhūtāni nabhastalasya |juṣṭāni dharmātmabhirātmavadbhirdevarṣibhiścaiva mahārṣibhiśca || 740
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 41 From hence again the Northern quarter is especially to be fitly followed for the sake of preeminent merit even one who was wise starting towards the south could not advance one single step,itaśca bhūyaḥ kṣamamuttaraiva diksevituṁ dharmaviśeṣahetoḥ |na hi kṣamaṁ dakṣiṇato budhena padaṁ bhavedekamapi prayātum || 741
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 42 Hast thou seen in this sacred grove one who neglects all ceremonies or who follows confused ceremonies or an outcast or one impure that thou dost not desire to dwell here Speak it out and let the abode be welcomed,tapovane sminnatha niṣkriyo vā saṁkīrṇadharmā patito śucirvā |dṛṣṭastvayā yena na te vivatsā tadbrūhi yāvadrucito stu vāsaḥ || 742
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 43 These hermits here desire thee as their companion in penance thee who art like a storehouse of penance — to dwell with thee who art like Indra would bring prosperity even to Vṛhaspati’,ime hi vāṁchaṁti tapaḥsahāyaṁ taponidhānapratimaṁ bhavaṁtam |vāsastvayā hīṁdrasamena sārdhaṁ vṛhaspaterabhyudayāvahaḥ syāt || 743
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 44 He the chief of the wise when thus addressed in the midst of the ascetics by their chief—having resolved in his mind to put an end to all existence — thus uttered his inward thought,ityevamukte sa tapasvimadhye tapasvimukhyena manīṣimukhyaḥ |bhavapraṇāśāya kṛtapratijñaḥ svaṁ bhāvamaṁtargatamācacakṣe || 744
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 45 The upright-souled saints the upholders of religion become the very ideal of our own kindred through their delight in showing hospitality by all these kind feelings of thine towards me affection is produced in me and the path which regards the self as supreme 08 is revealed,ṛjvātmanāṁ dharmabhṛtāṁ munīnāmiṣṭātithitvātsvajanopamānam |evaṁvidhairmāṁ prati bhāvajātaiḥ prītiḥ parātmā janitaśca mārgaḥ || 745
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 46 I seem to be all at once bathed by these gentle heart-touching words of thine and the joy now throbs in me once more which I felt when I first grasped the idea of dharma,snigdhābhirābhirhṛdayaṁgamābhiḥ samāsataḥ snāta ivāsmi vāgbhiḥ |ratiśca me dharmanavagrahasya vispaṁditā saṁprati bhūya eva || 746
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 47 There is sorrow to me when I reflect that I shall have to depart leaving you who are thus engaged you who are such a refuge and who have shown such excessive kindness to me — just as there was when I had to leave my kindred behind,evaṁ pravṛttān bhavataḥ śaraṇyānatīva saṁdarśitapakṣapātān |yāsyāmi hitveti mamāpi duḥkhaṁ yathaiva baṁdhūṁstyajatastathaiva || 747
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 48 But this devotion of yours is for the sake of heaven — while my desire is that there may be no fresh birth therefore I wish not to dwell in this wood the nature of cessation is different from that of activity,svargāya yuṣmākamayaṁ tu dharmo mamābhilāṣastvapunarbhavāya |asmin vane yena na me vivatsā bhinnaḥ pravṛttyā hi nivṛttidharmaḥ || 748
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 49 It is not therefore any dislike on my part or the wrong conduct of another which makes me go away from this wood for ye are all like great sages standing fast in the religious duties which are in accordance with former ages’,tannāratirme na parāpacāro vanādito yena parivrajāmi |dharme sthitāḥ pūrvayugānurūpe sarve bhavaṁto hi mahārṣikalpāḥ || 749
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 50 Then having heard the prince’s discourse gracious and of deep meaning gentle strong and full of dignity the ascetics paid him especial honour,tato vacaḥ sūnṛtamarthavacca suślakṣṇamojasvi ca garvitaṁ ca |śrutvā kumārasya tapasvinaste viśeṣayuktaṁ bahumānamīyuḥ || 750
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 51 But a certain Brāhman who was lying there in the ashes tall and wearing his hair in a tuft and clothed in the bark of trees with reddish eyes and a thin long nose and carrying a pot with water 09 in his hand thus lifted his voice,kaściddvijastatra tu bhasmaśāyī prāṁśuḥ śikhī dāravacīravāsāḥ |āpiṁgalākṣastanudīrghaghoṇaḥ kuṁḍodahasto giramityuvāca || 751
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 52 O sage brave indeed is thy purpose who young as thou art hast seen the evils of birth he who having pondered thoroughly heaven and liberation makes up his mind for liberation — he is indeed brave,dhīmannudāraḥ khalu niścayaste yastvaṁ yuvā janmani dṛṣṭadoṣaḥ |svargāpavargau hi vicārya samyagyasyāpavarge matirasti so sti || 752
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 53 By all those various sacrifices penances and vows the slaves of passion desire to go to heaven but the strong having battled with passion as with an enemy desire to obtain liberation,yajñaistapobhirniyamaiśca taistaiḥ svargaṁ yiyāsaṁti hi rāgavaṁtaḥ |rāgeṇa sārdhaṁ ripuṇeva yuddhvā mokṣaṁ parīpsaṁti tu sattvavaṁtaḥ || 753
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 54 If this is thy settled purpose go quickly to Viṁdhyakoṣṭha the Muni Arāḍa lives there who has gained an insight into absolute bliss,tadbuddhireṣā yadi niścitā te tūrṇaṁ bhavān gacchatu viṁdhyakoṣṭham |asau munistatra vasatyarāḍo yo naiṣṭhike śreyasi labdhacakṣuḥ || 754
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 55 From him thou wilt hear the path to truth and if thou hast a desire for it thou wilt embrace it but as I foresee this purpose of thine will go on further after having rejected his theory,tasmādbhavāñchroṣyati tattvamārgaṁ satyāṁ rucau saṁpratipatsyate ca |yathā tu paśyāmi matistavaiṣā tasyāpi yāsyatyavadhūya buddhim || 755
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 56 With the nose of a well-fed horse large long eyes a red lower lip white sharp teeth and a thin red tongue — this face of thine will drink up the entire ocean of what is to be known,puṣṭāśvaghoṇaṁ vipulāyatākṣaṁ tāmrādharoṣṭhaṁ sitatīkṣṇadaṁṣṭram |idaṁ hi vaktraṁ tanuraktajihvaṁ jñeyārṇavaṁ pāsyati kṛtsnameva || 756
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 57 That unfathomed depth which characterises thee that majesty and all those signs of thine — they shall win a teacher’s chair in the earth which was never won by sages even in a former age’,gaṁbhīratā yā bhavatastvagādhā yā dīptatā yāni ca lakṣaṇāni |ācāryakaṁ prāpsyasi tatpṛthivyāṁ yannarṣibhiḥ pūrvayuge pyavāptam || 757
https//bitly/2jICUB6, 58 The prince replied Very well’ and having saluted the company of sages he departed the hermits also having duly performed to him all the rites of courtesy entered again into the ascetic grove,paramamiti tato nṛpātmajastamṛṣijanaṁ pratinaṁdya niryayau |vidhivadanuvidhāya te pi taṁ praviviśurāśramiṇastapovanam || 758
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 1 Meanwhile the attendant of the horse in deep distress when his unselfish master thus went into the forest made every effort in the road to dissolve 01 his load of sorrow and yet in spite of it all not a tear dropped from him,tatasturaṁgāvacaraḥ sa durmanāstathā vanaṁ bhartari nirmame gate |cakāra yatnaṁ pathi śokavigrahe tathāpi caivāśru na tasya cikṣipe || 81
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 2 But the road which by his lord’s command he had traversed in one night with that horse — that same road he now travelled in eight days pondering his lord’s absence,yamekarātreṇa tu bharturājñayā jagāma mārgaṁ saha tena vājinā |iyāya bharturvirahaṁ viciṁtayaṁstameva paṁthānamahobhiraṣṭabhiḥ || 82
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 3 And the horse Kaṁthaka though he still went on bravely flagged and had lost all spirit in his heart and decked though he was with ornaments he had lost all his beauty when bereft of his master,hayaśca saujasvi cacāra kaṁthakastatāma bhāvena babhūva nirmadaḥ |alaṁkṛtaścāpi tathaiva bhūṣaṇairabhūdgataśrīriva tena varjitaḥ || 83
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 4 And turning round towards that ascetic-grove he neighed repeatedly with a mournful sound and though pressed with hunger he welcomed not nor tasted any grass or water on the road as before 02,nivṛtya caivābhimukhastapovanaṁ bhṛśaṁ jiheṣe karuṇaṁ muhurmuhuḥ |kṣudhānvito pyadhvani śaṣpamaṁbu vā yathā purā nābhinanaṁda nādade || 84
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 5 Slowly they two at last came back to the city called after Kapila which seemed empty when deserted by that hero who was bent on the salvation of the world — like the sky bereft of the sun,tato vihīnaṁ kapilāhvayaṁ puraṁ mahātmanā tena jagaddhitātmanā |krameṇa tau śūnyamivopajagmaturdivākareṇeva vinākṛtaṁ nabhaḥ || 85
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 6 Bright as it was with lotus-covered waters adorned also with trees full of flowers that garden of his which was now like a forest was no longer gay with citizens who had lost all their gladness,sapuṁḍarīkairapi śobhitaṁ jalairalaṁkṛtaṁ puṣpadharairnagairapi |tadeva tasyopavanaṁ vanopamaṁ gatapraharṣairna rarāja nāgaraiḥ || 86
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 7 Then those two — who were as it were silently forbidden by the sad inhabitants who were wandering in that direction their brightness gone and their eyes dim with tears — slowly entered the city which seemed all bathed in gloom,tato bhramadbhirdiśi dīnamānasairanujjvalairvāṣpahatekṣaṇairnaraiḥ |nivāryamāṇāviva tāvubhau puraṁ śanairajaḥsnātamivābhijagmatuḥ || 87
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 8 Having heard that they had returned with their limbs all relaxed coming back without the pride of the Śākya race the men of the city shed tears in the road as when in old days the chariot of the son of Daśaratha came back,niśamya ca srastaśarīragāminau vināgatau śākyakularṣabheṇa tau |mumoca vāṣpaṁ pathi nāgaro janaḥ purā rathe dāśaratherivāgate || 88
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 9 Full of wrath the people followed Chaṁdaka in the road crying behind him with tears Where is the king’s son the glory of his race and kingdom he has been stolen away by thee’,atha bruvaṁtaḥ samupetamanyavo janāḥ pathi cchaṁdakamāgatāśravaḥ |kva rājaputraḥ kularāṣṭravardhano hṛtastvayāsāviti pṛṣṭhato nvayuḥ || 89
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 10 Then he said to those faithful ones I have not left the king’s son but by him in the uninhabited forest I weeping and the dress of a householder were abandoned together’,tataḥ sa tān bhaktimato bravījjanānnareṁdraputraṁ na parityajāmyaham |rudannahaṁ tena tu nirjane vane gṛhasthaveśaśca visarjitāviti || 810
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 11 Having heard these words of his those crowds adopted a most difficult resolve they did not wipe away the tears which fell from their eyes and they blamed their own (evil) hearts on account of the consequences of their actions,idaṁ vacastasya niśamya te janāḥ suduṣkaraṁ khalviti niścayaṁ yayuḥ |patadvijahruḥ salilaṁ na netrajaṁ mano niniṁduśca phalārthamātmanaḥ || 811
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 12 Then they said Let us go this very day into that forest whither he is gone whose gait is like the king of elephants without him we have no wish to live like the senses when the souls depart,athocuradyaiva viśāma tadvanaṁ gataḥ sa yatra dviparājavikramaḥ |jijīviṣā nāsti hi tena no vinā yatheṁdriyāṇāṁ vigame śarīriṇām || 812
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 13 This city bereft of him is a forest and that forest which possesses him is a city the city without him has no charms for us like heaven without the lord of the Maruts when Vṛtra was slain’ 03,idaṁ puraṁ tena vivarjitaṁ vanaṁ vanaṁ ca tattena samanvitaṁ puram |na śobhate tena hi no vinā puraṁ marutvatā vṛtravadhe yathā divam || 813
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 14 Next the women crowded to the rows of windows crying to one another The prince has returned’ but having heard that his horse had an empty back they closed the windows again and wailed aloud,punaḥ kumāro vinivṛtta ityathau gavākṣamālāḥ pratipedire ṁganāḥ |viviktapṛṣṭhaṁ ca niśamya vājinaṁ punargavākṣāṇi pidhāya cukruśuḥ || 814
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 15 But the king having undertaken religious observances for the recovery of his son with his mind distressed by the vow and the sorrow was muttering prayers in the temple and performing such rites as suited the occasion,praviṣṭadīkṣastu sutopalabdhaye vratena śokena ca khinnamānasaḥ |jajāpa devāyatane narādhipaścakāra tāstāśca yathāśrayāḥ kriyāḥ || 815
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 16 Then with his eyes filled with tears — taking the horse his whole soul fixed on the horse — overcome with grief he 04 entered the palace as if his master had been killed by an enemy,tataḥ sa vāṣpapratipūrṇalocanasturaṁgamādāya turaṁgamānasaḥ | 816viveśa śokābhihato nṛpālayaṁ kṣayaṁ vinīte ripuṇeva bhartari ||
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 17 And entering the royal stable looking about with his eyes full of tears Kaṁthaka uttered a loud sound as if he were uttering his woe to the people,vigāhamānaśca nareṁdramaṁdiraṁ vilokayannaśruvahena cakṣuṣā |svareṇa puṣṭena rurāva kaṁthako janāya duḥkhaṁ prativedayanniva || 817
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 18 Then the birds that fed in the middle of the house and the carefully cherished horses that were tied near by re-echoed the sound of that horse thinking that it might be the return of the prince,tataḥ khagāśca kṣayamadhyagocarāḥ samīpabaddhāsturagāśca satkṛtāḥ |hayasya tasya pratisasvanuḥ svanaṁ nareṁdrasūnorupayānaśaṁkitāḥ || 818
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 19 And the people deceived by an excessive joy who were in the neighbourhood of the king’s inner apartments thought in their hearts Since the horse Kaṁthaka neighs it must be that the prince is coming’,janāśca harṣātiśayena vaṁcitā janādhipāṁtaḥpurasaṁnikarṣagāḥ |yathā hayaḥ kaṁthaka eṣa heṣate dhruvaṁ kumāro viśatīti menire || 819
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 20 Then the women who were fainting with sorrow now in wild joy with their eyes rolling to see the prince rushed out of the palace full of hope like flickering lightnings from an autumn cloud,atipraharṣādatha śokamūrchitāḥ kumārasaṁdarśanalolalocanāḥ |gṛhādviniścakramurāśayā striyaḥ śaratpayodādiva vidyutaścalāḥ || 820
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 21 With their dress hanging down and their linen garments soiled their faces untouched by collyrium and with eyes dimmed by tears dark and discoloured and destitute of all painting 05 like the stars in the sky pale-red with the ending of night,vilaṁbaveśyo malināṁśukāṁbarā niraṁjanairvāṣpahatekṣaṇairmukhaiḥ |kṛṣṇā vivarṇāṁjanayā vinākṛtā divīva tārā rajanīkṣayāruṇāḥ || 821
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 22 With their feet unstained by red and undecked by anklets — their faces without earrings and their ears in their native simplicity — their loins with only nature’s fulness and uncircled by any girdle — and their bosoms bare of strings of pearls as if they had been robbed,araktatāmraiścaraṇairanūpurairakuṁḍalairārjavakarṇikairmukhaiḥ |svabhāvapīnairjaghanairamekhalairahārayoktrairmuṣitairiva stanaiḥ || 822
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 23 But when they saw Chaṁdaka standing helpless his eyes filled with tears and the horse the noble women wept with pale faces like cows abandoned by the bull in the midst of the forest,nirīkṣitā vāṣpaparītalocanaṁ nirāśrayaṁ chaṁdakamaśvameva ca |vivarṇavaktrā rurudurvarāṁganā vanāṁtare gāva ivarṣabhojjhitāḥ || 823
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 24 Then the king’s principal queen Gautamī like a fond cow that has lost her calf fell bursting into tears on the ground with outstretched arms like a golden plantain-tree with trembling leaves,tataḥ savāṣpā mahiṣī mahīpateḥ pranaṣṭavatsā mahiṣīva vatsalā |pragṛhya bāhū nipapāta gautamī vilolaparṇā kadalīva kāṁcanī || 824
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 25 Some of the other women bereft of their brightness and with arms and souls lifeless and seeming to have lost their senses in their despondency raised no cry shed no tear and breathed not standing senseless as if painted 06,hatatviṣo nyāḥ śithilātmabāhavaḥ striyo viṣādena vicetanā iva |na cukruśurnāśru jahurna śaśvasurna cetanā ullikhitā iva sthitāḥ || 825
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 26 Others as having lost all self-control fainting in their sorrow for their lord their faces pouring tears from their eyes watered their bosoms from which all sandal-wood was banished like a mountain the rocks with its streams,adhīramanyāḥ patiśokamūrchitā vilocanaprasravaṇairmukhaiḥ striyaḥ |siṣiṁcire proṣitacaṁdanān stanān dharādharaḥ prasravaṇairivopalān || 826
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 27 Then that royal palace was illumined with their faces pelted by the tears from their eyes as a lake in the time of the first rains with its dripping lotuses pelted by the rain from the clouds,mukhaiśca tāsāṁ nayanāṁbutāḍitaiḥ rarāja tadrājaniveśanaṁ tadā |navāṁbukāle ṁbudavṛṣṭitāḍitaiḥ sravajjalaistāmarasairyathā saraḥ || 827
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 28 The noble women beat their breasts with their lotus-like hands falling incessantly whose fingers were round and plump which had their arteries hidden and bore no ornaments — as creepers tossed by the wind strike themselves with their shoots,suvṛttapīnāṁgulibhirniraṁtarairabhūṣaṇairgūḍhaśirairvarāṁganāḥ |urāṁsi jaghnuḥ kamalopamaiḥ karaiḥ svapallavairvātacalā latā iva || 828
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 29 And again how those women shine forth as their bosoms rose up together after the blow from the hand and trembled with the shock like the streams when their pairs of ruddy geese shake as the lotuses on which they sit wave about with the wind from the wood 07,karaprahārapracalaiśca tā babhuryathāpi nāryaḥ sahitonnataiḥ stanaiḥ |vanānilāghūrṇitapadmakaṁpitaiḥ rathāṁganāmnāṁ mithunairivāpagāḥ || 829
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 30 As they pressed their breasts with their hands so too they pressed their hands with their breasts — dull to all feelings of pity they made their hands and bosoms inflict mutual pains on each other,yathā ca vakṣāṁsi karairapīḍayaṁstathaiva vakṣobhirapīḍayan karān |akārayaṁstatra parasparaṁ vyathāḥ karāgravakṣāṁsyabalā dayālasāḥ || 830
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 31 Then thus spoke Yaśodharā shedding tears with deep 08 sorrow her bosom heaving with her sighs her eyes discoloured with aneer and her voice choking with emotion through the influence of despondency,tatastu roṣapraviraktalocanā viṣādasaṁbaṁdhakaṣāyagadgadam |uvāca niḥśvāsacalatpayodharā vigādhaśokāśrudharā yaśodharā || 831
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 32 Leaving me helplessly asleep in the night whither O Chaṁdaka is he the desire of my heart gone and when thou and Kaṁthaka are alone come back while three went away together my mind trembles,niśi prasuptāmavaśāṁ vihāya māṁ gataḥ kva sa cchaṁdaka manmanorathaḥ |upāgate ca tvayi kaṁthake ca me samaṁ gateṣu triṣu kaṁpate manaḥ || 832
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 33 Why dost thou weep to-day O cruel one having done a dishonourable pitiless and unfriendly deed to me Cease thy tears and be content in thy heart — tears and that deed of thine ill agree,anāryamasnidghamamitrakarma me nṛśaṁsa kṛtvā kimihādya rodiṣi |niyaccha vāṣpaṁ bhava tuṣṭamānaso na saṁvadatyaśru ca tacca karma te || 833
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 34 Through thee his dear obedient faithful loyal companion always doing what was right the son of my lord is gone never to return — rejoice — all hail thy pains have gained their end,priyeṇa vaśyena hitena sādhunā tvayā sahāyena yathārthakāriṇā |gato ryaputro hyapunarnivṛttaye ramasva diṣṭyā saphalaḥ śramastava || 834
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 35 Better for a man a wise enemy rather than a foolish friend unskilled in emergencies by thee the unwise self-styled friend a great calamity has been brought upon this family,varaṁ manuṣyasya vicakṣaṇo ripurna mitramaprājñamayogapeśalam |suhṛdbruveṇa hyavipaścitā tvayā kṛtaḥ kulasyāsya mahānupaplavaḥ || 835
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 36 These women are sorely to be pitied who have put away their ornaments having their eyes red and dimmed with continuous tears who are as it were desolate widows though their lord still stands as unshaken as the earth or Mount Himavat,imā hi śocyā vyavamuktabhūṣaṇāḥ prasaktavāṣpāvilaraktalocanāḥ |sthite pi patyau himavanmahīsame pranaṣṭaśobhā vidhavā iva striyaḥ || 836
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 37 And these lines of palaces seem to weep aloud flinging up their dovecots for arms with the long unbroken moan of their doves — separated verily with him from all who could restrain them,imāśca vikṣiptaviṭaṁkabāhavaḥ prasaktapārāvatadīrghanisvanāḥ |vinākṛtāstena sahaiva rodhanairbhṛśaṁ rudaṁtīva vimānapaṁktayaḥ || 837
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 38 Even that horse Kaṁthaka without doubt desired my utter ruin for he bore away from hence my treasure when all were sound asleep in the night — like one who steals jewels,anarthakāmo sya janasya sarvathā turaṁgamo pi dhruvameṣa kaṁthakaḥ |jahāra sarvasvamitastathā hi me jane prasupte niśi ratnacauravat || 838
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 39 When he was able to bear even the onsets of arrows and still more the strokes of whips — how then for fear of the fall of a whip could he go carrying with him my prosperity and my heart together,yadā samarthaḥ khalu soḍhumāgatāniṣuprahārānapi kiṁ punaḥ kaśāḥ |gataḥ kaśāpātabhayāt kathaṁ tvayaṁ śriyaṁ gṛhītvā hṛdayaṁ ca me samam || 839
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 40 The base creature now neighs loudly filling the king’s palace with the sound but when he carried away my beloved then this vilest of horses was dumb,anāryakarmā bhṛśamadya heṣate nareṁdradhiṣṇyaṁ pratipūrayanniva |yadā tu nirvāhayati sma me priyaṁ tadā hi mūkasturagādhamo bhavat || 840
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 41 If he had neighed and so woke up the people or had even made a noise with his hoofs on the ground or had made the loudest sound he could with his jaws my grief would not have been so great’,yadi hyaheṣiṣyata bodhayañjanaṁ khuraiḥ kṣitau vāpyakariṣyata dhvanim |hanusvanaṁ vājanayiṣyaduttamaṁ na cābhaviṣyanmama duḥkhamīdṛśam || 841
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 42 Having thus heard the queen’s words their syllables choked with tears and full of lament slowly Chaṁdaka uttered this answer with his face bent down his voice low with tears and his hands clasped in supplication,itīha devyāḥ paridevitāśrayaṁ niśamya vāṣpagrathitākṣaraṁ vacaḥ |adhomukhaḥ sāśrukalaḥ kṛtāṁjaliḥ śanairidaṁ chaṁdaka uttaraṁ jagau || 842
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 43 Surely O queen thou wilt not blame Kaṁthaka nor wilt thou show thy anger against me know that we two are entirely guiltless — that god amongst men O queen is gone away like a god,vigarhituṁ nārhasi devi kaṁthakaṁ na cāpi roṣaṁ mayi kartumarhasi |anāgasau svaḥ samavehi sarvaśo gato nṛdevaḥ sa hi devi devavat || 843
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 44 I indeed though I well knew the king’s command as though dragged by force by some divine powers brought quickly to him this swift steed and followed him on the road unwearied,ahaṁ hi jānannapi rājaśāsanaṁ balātkṛtaḥ kairapi daivatairiva |upānayaṁ tūrṇamimaṁ turaṁgamaṁ tathānvagacchaṁ vigataśramo dhvani || 844
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 45 And this best of horses as he went along touched not the ground with the tips of his hoofs as if they were kept aloft from it and so too having his mouth restrained as by fate he made no sound with his jaws and neighed not,vrajannayaṁ vājivaro pi nāspṛśanmahīṁ khurāgrairvidhṛtairivāṁtarā |tathaiva daivādiva saṁyatānano hanusvanaṁ nākṛta nāpyaheṣata || 845
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 46 When the prince went out then the gate was thrown open of its own accord and the darkness of the night was as it were pierced by the sun — we may learn from hence too that this was the ordering of fate,yadā vahirgacchati pārthivātmajastadābhavaddvāramapāvṛtaṁ svayam |tamaśca naiśaṁ raviṇeva pāṭitaṁ tato pi daivo vidhireṣa gṛhyatām || 846
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 47 When also by the king’s command in palace and city diligent guards had been placed by thousands and at that time they were all overcome by sleep and woke not — we may learn from hence too that this was the ordering of fate,yadāpramatto pi nareṁdraśāsanādgṛhe pure caiva sahasraśo janaḥ |tadā sa nābudhyata nidrayā hṛtastato pi daivo vidhireṣa gṛhyatām || 847
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 48 When also the garment approved for a hermit’s dwelling in the forest was offered to him at the moment by some denizen of heaven and the tiara which he threw into the sky was carried off — we may learn from hence too that this was the ordering of fate,yataśca vāso vanavāsasaṁmataṁ visṛṣṭamasmai samaye divaukasā |divi praviddhaṁ mukuṭaṁ ca taddhṛtaṁ tato pi daivo vidhireṣa gṛhyatām || 848
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 49 Do not therefore assume 09 that his departure arises from the fault of either of us O queen neither I nor this horse acted by our own choice he went on his way with the gods as his retinue’,tadevamāvāṁ naradevi doṣato na tatprayātaṁ pratigaṁtumarhasi |na kāmakāro mama nāsya vājinaḥ kṛtānuyātraḥ sa hi daivatairgataḥ || 849
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 50 Having thus heard the history of the prince’s departure so marvellous in many ways those women as though losing their grief were filled with wonder but they again took up their distress at the thought of his becoming an ascetic,iti prayāṇaṁ bahudhaivamadbhutaṁ niśamya tāstasya mahātmanaḥ striyaḥ |pranaṣṭaśokā iva vismayaṁ yayurmanojvaraṁ pravrajanāttu lebhire || 850
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 51 With her eyes filled with the tears of despondency wretched like an osprey who has lost her young — Gautamī abandoning all self-control wailed aloud — she fainted and with a weeping face exclaimed,viṣādapāriplavalocanā tataḥ pranaṣṭapotā kurarīva duḥkhitā |vihāya dhairyaṁ virurāva gautamī tatāma caivāśrumukhī jagāda ca || 851
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 52 Beautiful soft black and all in great waves growing each from its own special root — those hairs of his are tossed on the ground worthy to be encircled by a royal diadem,mahormimaṁto mṛdavo sitāḥ śubhāḥ pṛthakpṛthagmūlaruhāḥ samudgatāḥ |praceritāste bhuvi tasya mūrdhajā nareṁdramaulīpariveṣṭanakṣamāḥ || 852
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 53 With his long arms and lion-gait his bull-like eye and his beauty bright like gold his broad chest and his voice deep as a drum or a cloud should such a hero as this dwell in a hermitage,pralaṁbabāhurmṛgarājavikramo mahārṣabhākṣaḥ kanakojjvaladyutiḥ |viśālavakṣā ghanaduṁdubhisvanastathāvidho pyāśramavāsamarhati || 853
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 54 This earth is indeed unworthy as regards that peerless doer of noble actions for such a virtuous hero has gone away from her — it is the merits and virtues of the subjects which produce their king,abhāginī nūnamiyaṁ vasuṁdharā tamāryakarmāṇamanuttamaṁ prati |gatastato sau guṇavān hi tādṛśo nṛpaḥ prajābhāgyaguṇaiḥ prasūyate || 854
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 55 Those two feet of his tender with their beautiful web spread between the toes with their ankles concealed and soft like a blue lotus — how can they bearing a wheel marked in the middle walk on the hard ground of the skirts of the forest,sujātajālāvatatāṁgulī mṛdū nigūḍhagulphau viṣapuṣpakomalau |vanāṁtabhūmiṁ kaṭhināṁ kathaṁ nu tau sacakramadhyau caraṇau gamiṣyataḥ || 855
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 56 That body which deserves to sit or lie on the roof of a palace — honoured with costly garments aloes and sandal-wood — how will that manly body live in the woods exposed to the attacks of the cold the heat and the rain,vimānapṛṣṭhe śayanāsanocitaṁ mahārhavastrāgurucaṁdanārcitam |kathaṁ nu śītoṣṇajalāgameṣu taccharīramojasvi vane bhaviṣyati || 856
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 57 He who was proud of his family goodness strength energy sacred learning beauty and youth — who was ever ready to give not to ask — how will he go about begging alms from others,kulena sattvena balena varcasā śrutena lakṣmyā vayasā ca garvitaḥ |pradātumevābhyudito na yācituṁ kathaṁ sa bhikṣāṁ parataścariṣyati || 857
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 58 He who lying on a spotless golden bed was awakened during the night by the concert of musical instruments — how alas will he my ascetic sleep to-day on the bare ground with only one rag of cloth interposed’,śucau śayitvā śayane hiraṇmaye prabodhyamāno niśi tūryanisvanaiḥ |kathaṁ vata svapsyati so dya me vratī paṭaukadeśāṁtarite mahītale || 858
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 59 Having heard this piteous lamentation the women embracing one another with their arms rained the tears from their eyes as the shaken creepers drop honey from their flowers,imaṁ vilāpaṁ karuṇaṁ niśamya tā bhujaiḥ pariṣvajya parasparaṁ striyaḥ |vilocanebhyaḥ salilāni tatyajurmadhūni puṣpebhya iveritā latāḥ || 859
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 60 Then Yaśodharā fell upon the ground like the ruddy goose parted from her mate and in utter bewilderment she slowly lamented with her voice repeatedly stopped by sobs,tato dharāyāmapatadyaśodharā vicakravākeva rathāṁgasāhvayā |śanaiśca tattadvilalāpa viklavā muhurmuhurgadgadaruddhayā girā || 860
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 61 If he wishes to practise a religious life after abandoning me his lawful wife widowed — where is his religion who wishes to follow penance without his lawful wife to share it with him,sa māmanāthāṁ sahadharmacāriṇīmapāsya dharmaṁ yadi kartumicchati |kuto sya dharmaḥ sahadharmacāriṇīṁ vinā tapo yaḥ paribhoktumicchati || 861
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 62 He surely has never heard of the monarchs of olden times his own ancestors Mahāsudarśa 10 and the rest — how they went with their wives into the forest — that he thus wishes to follow a religious life without me,śṛṇoti nūnaṁ sa na pūrvapārthivān mahāsudarśaprabhṛtīn pitāmahān |vanāni patnīsahitānupeyuṣastathā sa dharmaṁ madṛte cikīrṣati || 862
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 63 He does not see that husband and wife are both consecrated in sacrifices and both purified by the performance of the rites of the Veda and both destined to enjoy 11 the same results afterwards — he therefore grudges me a share in his merit,makheṣu vā vedavidhānasaṁskṛtau na daṁpatī paśyati dīkṣitāvubhau |samaṁ bubhukṣū parato pi tatphalaṁ tato sya jāto mayi dharmamatsaraḥ || 863
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 64 Surely it must be that this fond lover of religion knowing that my mind was secretly quarrelling even with my beloved lightly and without fear has deserted me thus angry in the hope to obtain heavenly nymphs in lndra’s world,dhruvaṁ sa jānan mama dharmavallabho manaḥ priye pyākalahaṁ muhurmithaḥ |sukhaṁ vibhīrmāmapahāya rosaṇāṁ maheṁdraloke psaraso jighṛkṣati || 864
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 65 But what kind of a thought is this of mine those women even there have the attributes which belong to bodies — for whose sake he thus practises austerities in the forest deserting his royal magnificence and my fond devotion,iyaṁ tu ciṁtā mama kīdṛśaṁ nu tā vapurguṇaṁ bibhrati tatra yoṣitaḥ |vane yadarthaṁ sa tapāṁsi tapyate śriyaṁ ca hitvā mama bhaktimeva ca || 865
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 66 I have no such longing for the joy of heaven nor is that hard for even common people to win if they are resolute 12 but my one desire is how he my beloved may never leave me either in this world or the next,na khalviyaṁ svargasukhāya me spṛhā na tajjanasyātmavato pi durlabham |sa tu priyo māmiha vā paratra vā kathaṁ na jahyāditi me manorathaḥ || 866
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 67 Even if I am unworthy to look on my husbands face with its long eyes and bright smile still is this poor Rāhula never to roll about in his father’s lap,abhāginī yadyahamāyatekṣaṇaṁ śucismitaṁ bharturudīkṣituṁ mukham |na maṁdabhāgyo rhati rāhulo pyayaṁ kadācidaṁke parivartituṁ pituḥ || 867
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 68 Alas the mind of that wise hero is terribly stern — gentle as his beauty seems it is pitilessly cruel — who can desert of his own accord such an infant son with his inarticulate talk one who would charm even an enemy,aho nṛśaṁsaṁ sukumāravarcasaḥ sudāruṇaṁ tasya manasvino manaḥ |kalapralāpaṁ dviṣato pi harṣaṇaṁ śiśuṁ sutaṁ yastyajatīdṛśaṁ svataḥ || 868
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 69 My heart too is certainly most stern yea made of rock or fashioned even of iron which does not break when its lord is gone to the forest deserted by his royal glory like an orphan — he so well worthy of happiness’,mamāpi kāmaṁ hṛdayaṁ sudāruṇaṁ śilāmayaṁ vāpyayasāpi vā kṛtam |anāthavacchrīrahite sukhocite vanaṁ gate bhartari yanna dīryate || 869
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 70 So the queen fainting in her woe wept and pondered and wailed aloud repeatedly — self-possessed as she was by nature yet in her distress she remembered not her fortitude and felt no shame,itīha devī patiśokamūrchitā ruroda dadhyau vilalāpa cāsakṛt |svabhāvadhīrāpi hi sā satī śucā dhṛtiṁ na sasmāra cakāra no hriyam || 870
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 71 Seeing Yaśodharā thus bewildered with her wild utterances of grief and fallen on the ground all the women cried out with their faces streaming with tears like large lotuses beaten by the rain,tatastathā śokavilāpaviklavāṁ yaśodharāṁ prekṣya vasuṁdharāgatām |mahāraviṁdairiva vṛṣṭitāḍitairmukhaiḥ savāṣpairvanitā vicukruśuḥ || 871
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 72 But the king having ended his prayers and performed the auspicious rites of the sacrifice now came out of the temple and being smitten by the wailing sound of the people he tottered like an elephant at the crash of a thunderbolt,samāptajāpyaḥ kṛtahomamaṁgalo nṛpastu devāyatanādviniryayau |janasya tenārttaraveṇa cāhataścacāla vajradhvanineva vāraṇaḥ || 872
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 73 Having heard (of the arrival) of both Chaṁdaka and Kaṁthaka and having learned the fixed resolve of his son the lord of the earth fell struck down by sorrow like the banner of Indra when the festival is over 13,niśāmya ca cchaṁdakakaṁthakāvubhau sutasya saṁśrutya ca niścayaṁ sthiram |papāta śokābhihato mahīpatiḥ śacīpatervṛtta ivotsave dhvajaḥ || 873
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 74 Then the king distracted by his grief for his son being held up for a moment by his attendants all of the same race gazed on the horse with his eyes filled with tears and then falling on the ground wailed aloud,tato muhūrtaṁ sutaśokamohito janena tulyābhijanena dhāritaḥ |nirīkṣya dṛṣṭyā jalapūrṇayā hayaṁ mahītalastho vilalāpa pārthivaḥ || 874
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 75 After having done many dear exploits for me in battle one great deed of cruelty O Kaṁthaka hast thou done — for by thee that dear son of mine dear for his every virtue has been tossed down in the wood dear as he was like a worthless thing,bahūni kṛtvā samare priyāṇi me mahattvayā kaṁthaka vipriyaṁ kṛtam |guṇapriyo yena vane sa me priyaḥ priyo pi sannapriyavat praceritaḥ || 875
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 76 Therefore either lead me to-day where he is or go quickly and bring him back again without him there is no life left to me as to one plunged in sickness without the true medicine,tadadya māṁ vā naya tatra yatra sa vraja drutaṁ vā punarenamānaya |ṛte hi tasmānmama nāsti jīvitaṁ vigāḍharogasya sadauṣadhādiva || 876
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 77 When Suvarṇaniṣṭhīvin was carried away by death it seemed impossible that Sṛṁjaya 14 should not die and shall I when my duty-loving son is gone fear to set my soul free like any coward,suvarṇaniṣṭhīvini mṛtyunā hṛte suduṣkaraṁ yanna mamāra sṛṁjayaḥ |ahaṁ punardharmaratau sute gate mumukṣurātmānamanātmavāniva || 877
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 78 How should not the mind of Manu himself be distracted when parted from his dear virtuous son 15 — (Manu) the son of Vivasvat who knew the higher and the lower the mighty lord of creatures the institutor of the ten chieftains 16,vibhordaśakṣatrakṛtaḥ prajāpateḥ parāparajñasya vivasvadātmanaḥ |priyeṇa putreṇa satā vinākṛtaṁ kathaṁ na muhyeddhi mano manorapi || 878
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 79 I envy the monarch that friend of Indra the wise son of king Aja 17 who when his son went into the forest went himself to heaven and dragged out no miserable life here with vain tears,ajasya rājñastanayāya dhīmate narādhipāyeṁdrasakhāya me spṛhā |gate vanaṁ yastanaye divaṁ gato na moghavāṣpaḥ kṛpaṇaṁ jijīva ha || 879
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 80 Describe to me O beloved one the court of that hermitage whither thou hast carried him who is as my funeral oblation of water these my vital airs are all ready to depart and are eager for it longing to drink it’,pracakṣva me bhadra tadāśramājiraṁ hṛtastvayā yatra sa me jalāṁjaliḥ |ime parīpsaṁti hi te pipāsavo mamāsavaḥ pretagatiṁ yiyāsavaḥ || 880
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 81 Thus the king in his grief for his separation from his son — losing all his innate firmness which was stedfast like the earth — loudly lamented as one distraught like Daśaratha a prey to his sorrow for Rāma,iti tanayaviyogajātaduḥkhaṁ kṣitisadṛśaṁ sahajaṁ vihāya dhairyam |daśaratha iva rāmaśokavaśyo bahu vilalāpa nṛpo visaṁjñakalpaḥ || 881
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 82 Then the wise counsellor endued with religious learning courtesy and virtue and the old family priest spoke to him as was befitting in these well-weighed words neither with their faces overwhelmed by grief nor yet wholly unmoved,śrutavinayaguṇānvitastatastaṁ matisacivaḥ pravayāḥ purohitaśca |avadhṛtamidamūcaturyathāvanna ca paritaptamukhau na cāpyaśokau || 882
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 83 Cease O noblest of men thy grief regain thy firmness — surely thou wilt not O firm hero shed tears like one of no self-control many kings on this earth have gone into the forests throwing away their royal pomp like a crushed wreath,tyaja naravara śokamehi dhairyaṁ kudhṛtirivārhasi dhīra nāśru moktum |srajamiva mṛditāmapāsya lakṣmīṁ bhuvi bahavo hi nṛpā vanānyatīyuḥ || 883
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 84 Moreover this his state of mind was all predetermined remember those words long ago of the holy sage Asita He will never be made to dwell even for a moment contentedly in heaven or in an emperor’s domain,api ca niyata eṣa tasya bhāvaḥ smara vacanaṁ tadṛṣeḥ purāsitasya |na hi sa divi na cakravartirājye kṣaṇamapi vāsayituṁ sukhena śakyaḥ || 884
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 85 But if O best of men the effort must be made quickly speak the word we two will at once go together let the battle be waged in every way with thy son and his fate whatever it be’,yadi tu nṛvara kārya eva yatnastvaritamudāhara yāvadatra yāvaḥ |bahuvidhamiha yuddhamastu tāvattava tanayasya vidheśca tasya tasya || 885
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 86 Then the king commanded them both Do you both go quickly hence — my heart will not return to quiet any more than a bird’s in the woods longing for its young’,narapatiratha tau śaśāsa tasmāddrutamita eva yuvāmabhiprayātam |na hi mama hṛdayaṁ prayāti śāṁtiṁ vanaśakuneriva putralālasasya || 886
https//bitly/2vH1mn6, 87 With a prompt acquiescence at the king’s order the counsellor and the family priest went to that forest and then with his wives and his queen the king also saying It is done’ performed the remainder of the rites,paramamiti nareṁdraśāsanāttau yayaturamātyapurohitau vanaṁ tat |kṛtamiti savadhūjanaḥ sadāro nṛpatirapi pracakāra śeṣakāryam || 887
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 1 Then the two the counsellor and the family priest beaten by the king with his scourge of tears went with every effort to that forest in the hurry of affection like two noble horses goaded,tatastadā maṁtripurohitau tau vāṣpapratodābhihatau nṛpeṇa |viddhau sadaśvāviva sarvayatnātsauhārdaśīghraṁ yayaturvanaṁ tat || 91
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 2 Having come at last full of weariness to that hermitage accompanied by a fitting train — they dismissed their royal pomp and with sober gestures entered the abode of Bhārgava,tamāśramam jātapariśramau tāvupetya kāle sadṛśānuyātrau |rājarddhimutsṛjya vinītaceṣṭāvupeyaturbhārgavadhiṣṇyameva || 92
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 3 Having saluted that Brāhman with due respect and having been honoured by him with due reverence in return having seated themselves plunging at once into the subject they addressed Bhārgava who was likewise seated concerning their errand,tau nyāyatastaṁ pratipūjya vipraṁ tenārcitau tāvapi cānurūpam |kṛtāsanau bhārgavamāsanasthaṁ chittvā kathāmūcaturātmakṛtyam || 93
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 4 Let your honour know us to be respectively imperfect proficients in preserving the sacred learning and in retaining the state-counsels — in the service of the monarch of the Ikṣvāku race pure in his valour and pure and wide in his glory,śuddhaujasaḥ śuddhaviśālakīrterikṣvākuvaṁśaprabhavasya rājñaḥ |imaṁ janaṁ vettu bhavānadhīraṁ śrutagrahe maṁtraparigrahe ca || 94
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 5 His son who is like Jayanta while he himself is like Indra has come here it is said desirous to escape from the fear of old age and death — know that we two are come here on account of him’,tasyeṁdrakalpasya jayaṁtakalpaḥ putro jarāmṛtyubhayaṁ titīrṣuḥ |ihābhyupetaḥ kila tasya hetorāvāmupetau bhagavānavaitu || 95
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 6 He answered them That prince of the long arms did indeed come here but not as one unawakened this dharma only brings us back again — recognising this he went off forthwith towards Arāḍa seeking liberation’,tau so bravīdasti sa dīrghabāhuḥ prāptaḥ kumāro na tu nāvabuddhaḥ |dharmo yamāvartaka ityavetya yātastvarāḍābhimukho mumukṣuḥ || 96
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 7 Then they two having understood the true state of things bade that Brāhman at once farewell and wearied though they were went on as if they were unwearied thither whither the prince was gone,tasmāttatastāvupalabhya tattvaṁ taṁ vipramāmaṁttya tadaiva sadyaḥ |khinnāvakhinnāviva rājaputraḥ prasasratustena yataḥ sa yātaḥ || 97
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 8 As they were going they saw him bereft of all ornaments 01 but still radiant with his beauty sitting like a king in the road at the foot of a tree like the sun under the canopy of a cloud,yāṁtau tatastau sṛjayā vihīnamapaśyatāṁ taṁ vapuṣā jvalaṁtam |nṛpopaviṣṭaṁ pathi vṛkṣamūle sūryaṁ ghanābhogamiva praviṣṭam || 98
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 9 Leaving his chariot the family priest then went up to the prince with the counsellor as the saint Aurvaśeya 02 went with Vāmadeva wishing to see Rāma when he dwelt in the forest,yānaṁ vihāyopayayau tatastaṁ purohito maṁtradhareṇa sārdham |yathā vanasthaṁ sahavāmadevo rāmaṁ didṛkṣurmuniraurvaśeyaḥ || 99
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 10 They paid him honour as was fitting as Śukra and Aṅgiras honoured Indra in heaven and he in return paid due honour to them as Indra in heaven to Śukra and Aṅgiras,tāvarcayāmāsaturarhatastaṁ divīva śukrāṁgirasau maheṁdram |pratyarcayāmāsa sa cārhatastau divīva śukrāṁgirasau maheṁdraḥ || 910
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 11 Then they having obtained his permission sat down near him who was the banner of the Śākya race and they shone in his proximity like the two stars of the asterism Punarvasū in conjunction with the moon,kṛtābhyanujñāvabhitastatastau niṣīdatuḥ śākyakuladhvajasya |virejatustasya ca saṁnikarṣe punarvasū yogagatāviveṁdoḥ || 911
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 12 The family priest addressed the prince who shone brightly as he sat at the foot of the tree as Vṛhaspati addressed Indra’s son Jayanta seated in heaven under the heavenly tree pārijāta,taṁ vṛkṣamūlasthamabhijvalaṁtaṁ purohito rājasutaṁ babhāṣe |yathopaviṣṭaṁ divi pārijāte vṛhaspatiḥ śakrasutaṁ jayaṁtam || 912
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 13 O prince consider for a moment what the king with his eyes raining tears said to thee as he lay fainting on the ground with the arrow of thy sorrow plunged into his heart,tvacchokaśalye hṛdayāvagāḍhe mohaṁ gato bhūmitale muhūrtam |kumāra rājā nayanāṁbuvarṣo yattvāmavocattadidaṁ nibodha || 913
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 14 “I know that thy resolve is fixed upon religion and I am convinced that this purpose of thine is unchanging 03 but I am consumed with a flame of anguish like fire at thy flying to the woods at an inopportune time,jānāmi dharmaṁ prati niścayaṁ te paraimi te cyāvinametamartham |ahaṁ tvakāle vanasaṁśrayātte śokāgnināgnipratimena dahye || 914
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 15 “Come thou who lovest duty for the sake of what is my heart’s desire — abandon this purpose for the sake of duty this huge swollen stream of sorrow sweeps me away as a river’s torrent its bank,tadehi dharmapriya matpriyārthaṁ dharmārthameva tyaja buddhimetām |ayaṁ hi mā śokarayaḥ pravṛddho nadīrayaḥ kūlamivābhihaṁti || 915
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 16 “That effect 04 which is wrought in the clouds water the dry grass and the mountains by the wind the sun the fire and the thunderbolt — that same effect this grief produces in us by its tearing in pieces its drying up its burning and its cleaving,meghāṁbukakṣādriṣu yā hi vṛttiḥ samīraṇārkāgnimahāśanīnām |tāṁ vṛttimasmāsu karoti śoko vikarṣaṇocchoṣaṇadāhabhedaiḥ || 916
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 17 “Enjoy therefore for a while the sovereignty of the earth — thou shalt go to the forest at the time provided by the śāstras — do not show disregard for thy unhappy kindred — compassion for all creatures is the true religion,tadbhuṁkṣva tāvadvasudhādhipatyaṁ kāle vanaṁ yāsyasi śāstradṛṣṭe |aniṣṭabaṁdhau kuru māpyupekṣāṁ sarveṣu bhūteṣu dayā hi dharmaḥ || 917
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 18 “Religion is not wrought out only in the forests the salvation of ascetics can be accomplished even in a city thought and effort are the true means the forest and the badge are only a coward’s signs,na caiṣa dharmo vana eva siddhaḥ pure pi siddhirniyatā yatīnām |buddhiśca yatnaśca nimittamatra vanaṁ ca liṁgaṁ ca hi bhīrucihnam || 918
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 19 “Liberation has been attained even by householders Indras among men who wore diadems and carried strings of pearls suspended on their shoulders whose garlands were entangled with bracelets and who lay cradled in the lap of Fortune,maulīdharairaṁsaviṣaktahāraiḥ keyūraviṣṭabdhasrajairnareṁdraiḥ |lakṣmyaṁkamadhye parivartamānaiḥ prāpto gṛhasthairapi mokṣadharmaḥ || 919
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 20 “Bali and Vajrabāhu the two younger brothers of Dhruva Vaibhrāja Āṣāḍha and Antideva 05 and Janaka also the king of the Videhas and king Senajit’s son his tree of ripe blessing 06,dhruvānujau yau balivajrabāhū vaibhrājamāṣāḍhamathāṁtidevam |videharājaṁ janakaṁ tathaiva pākadrumaṁ senajitaśca rājñaḥ || 920
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 21 “Know that all these great kings who were householders were well skilled in attaining the merit which leads to final bliss — do thou also therefore obtain both 07 simultaneously — royal magnificence and the control over the mind,etān gṛhasthān nṛpatīnavehi naiḥśreyase dharmavidhau vinītān |ubhe pi tasmādyugapadbhajasva cittādhipatyaṁ ca nṛpaśriyaṁ ca || 921
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 22 “I desire — when I have once closely embraced thee after thy kingly consecration is once performed and while thou art still wet with the sacred water — when I behold thee with the pomp of the royal umbrella — in the fulness of that joy to enter the forest,icchāmi hi tvāmupaguhya gāḍhaṁ kṛtābhiṣekaṁ salilārdrameva |dhṛtātapatraṁ samudīkṣamāṇastenaiva harṣeṇa vanaṁ praveṣṭum || 922
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 23 Thus did the king say to thee in a speech whose words were stopped by tears — surely having heard it for the sake of what is so dear to him thou wilt with all affection follow his affection,ityabravīdbhūmipatirbhavaṁtaṁ vākyena vāṣpagrathitākṣareṇa |śrutvā bhavānarhati tatpriyārthaṁ snehena tatsnehamanuprayātum || 923
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 24 The king of the Śākyas is drowned in a deep sea of sorrow full of waves of trouble springing from thee do thou therefore deliver him helpless and protectorless like an ox drowning in the sea,śokāṁbhasi tvatprabhave hyagādhe duḥkhārṇave majjati śākyarājaḥ |tasmāttamuttāraya nāthahīnaṁ nirāśrayaṁ magnamivārṇave gām || 924
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 25 Having heard that Bhīṣma who sprang from Gaṅgā’s womb Rāma and Rāma the son of Bhṛgu — all did what would please their fathers surely thou too wilt do thy father’s desire,bhīṣmeṇa gaṁgodarasaṁbhavena rāmeṇa rāmeṇa ca bhārgaveṇa |śrutvā kṛtaṁ karma pituḥ priyārthaṁ pitustvamapyarhasi kartumiṣṭam || 925
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 26 Consider also the queen who brought thee up who has not yet gone to the region inhabited by Agastya 08 — wilt thou not take some heed of her who ceaselessly grieves like a fond cow that has lost her calf,saṁvardhayitrīṁ ca samehi devīmagastyajuṣṭāṁ diśamaprayātām |pranaṣṭavatsāmiva vatsalāṁ gāmajasramārttāṁ kalituṁ na cārhasi || 926
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 27 Surely thou wilt succour thy wife by the sight of thee who now mourns widowed yet with her lord still alive — like a swan separated from her mate or a female elephant deserted in the forest by her companion,haṁsena haṁsīmiva viprayuktāṁ tyaktāṁ gajeneva vane kareṇum |ārttāṁ sanāthāmapi nāthahīnāṁ trātuṁ vadhūmarhasi darśanena || 927
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 28 Thy only son a child little deserving such woe distressed with sorrow and 09  — O deliver Rāhula from the grief of his kindred like the full moon from the contact of Rāhu,ekaṁ sutaṁ bālamanarhaduḥkhaṁ saṁtāpasaṁtapta  |taṁ rāhulaṁ mokṣaya baṁdhuśokād rāhūpasargādiva pūrṇacaṁdram || 928
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 29 Burned with the fire of anguish within him to which thy absence adds fresh fuel — a fire whose smoke is sighs and its flame despair — he wanders for a sight of thee through the women’s apartments and the whole city’,śokāgninā tvadviraheṁdhanena niḥśvāsadhūmena tamaḥśikhena |tvaddarśanāyarchati dahyamānaḥ so ṁtaḥpuraṁ caiva puraṁ ca kṛtsnam || 929
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 30 The Bodhisattva — whose perfection was absolute — having heard the words of the family priest reflected for a moment knowing all the virtues of the virtuous and then thus uttered his gentle reply,sa bodhisattvaḥ paripūrṇasattvaḥ śrutvā vacastasya purohitasya |dhyātvā muhūrtaṁ guṇavadguṇajñaḥ pratyuttaraṁ praśritamityuvāca || 930
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 31 I well know the paternal tenderness 10 of the king especially that which he has displayed towards me yet knowing this as I do still alarmed at sickness old age and death I am inevitably forced to leave my kindred,avaimi bhāvaṁ tanayaprasaktaṁ viśeṣato yo mayi bhūmipasya |jānannapi vyādhijarāvipadbhyo bhītastvagatyā svajanaṁ tyajāmi || 931
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 32 Who would not wish to see his dear kindred if but this separation from beloved ones did not exist but since even after it has been once separation will still come again it is for this that I abandon my father however loving,draṣṭuṁ priyaṁ kaḥ svajanaṁ hi necchennāsau yadi syātpriyaviprayogaḥ |yadā tu bhūtvāpi bhavedviyogastato guruṁ snigdhamapi tyajāmi || 932
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 33 I do not however approve that thou shouldst consider the king’s grief as caused by me when in the midst of his dream-like unions he is afflicted by thoughts of separations in the future,maddhetukaṁ yattu narādhipasya śokaṁ bhavānarhati na priyaṁ me |yatsvapnabhūteṣu samāgameṣu saṁtapyate bhāvini viprayogaiḥ || 933
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 34 Thus let thy thoughts settle into certainty having seen the multiform in its various developments neither a son nor kindred is the cause of sorrow — this sorrow is only caused by ignorance,evaṁ ca te niścayametu buddhirdṛṣṭvā vicitraṁ vividhapracāram |saṁtāpaheturna suto na baṁdhurajñānanaimittika eṣa tāpaḥ || 934
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 35 Since parting is inevitably fixed in the course of time for all beings just as for travellers who have joined company on a road — what wise man would cherish sorrow when he loses his kindred even though he loves them 11,yadādhvagānāmiva saṁgatānāṁ kāle viyogo niyataḥ prajānām |prājño janaḥ ko nu bhajeta śokaṁ baṁdhupriyaḥ sannapi baṁdhuhīnaḥ || 935
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 36 Leaving his kindred in another world he departs hither and having stolen away 12 from them here he goes forth once more having gone thither go thou elsewhere also — such is the lot of mankind — what consideration can the yogin have for them 13,ihaiti hitvā svajanaṁ paratra pralabhya cehāpi punaḥ prayāti |gatvāpi tatrāpyaparatra gacchetyevaṁ jano yogini ko nurodhaḥ || 936
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 37 Since from the moment of leaving the womb death is a characteristic adjunct 15 why in thy affection for thy son hast thou called my departure to the forest ill-timed,yadā ca garbhātprabhṛti prajānāṁ vadhāya  nubadhāya mṛtyuḥ 14 |kasmādakāle vanasaṁśrayaṁ me putrapriyastatra bhavān avocat || 937
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 38 There may be an ill time in one’s attaining a worldly object — time indeed is described as inseparably connected with all things 16 time drags the world into all its various times but all time suits a bliss which is really worthy of praise 17,bhavatyakālo viṣayābhipattau kālastathaivābhividhau pradiṣṭaḥ | 938kālo jagatkarṣati sarvakālānarcārhake śreyasi sarvakālaḥ ||
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 39 That the king should wish to surrender to me his kingdom — this is a noble thought well worthy of a father but it would be as improper for me to accept it as for a sick man through greed to accept unwholesome food,rājyaṁ mumukṣurmayi yacca rājā tadapyudāraṁ sadṛśaṁ pituśca |pratigrahītuṁ mama na kṣamaṁ tu lobhādapathyānnamivāturasya || 939
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 40 How can it be right for the wise man to enter royalty the home of illusion where are found anxiety passion and weariness and the violation of all right through another’s service,kathaṁ nu mohāyatanaṁ nṛpatvaṁ kṣamaṁ prapattuṁ viduṣā nareṇa |sodvegatā yatra madaḥ śramaśca paropacāreṇa ca dharmapīḍā || 940
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 41 The golden palace seems to me to be on fire the daintiest viands seem mixed with poison infested with crocodiles 19 ’,jāṁbūnadaṁ harmyamiva pradīptaṁ viṣeṇa saṁyuktamivottamānnam |grāhākulaṁ ca sthitaṁ  ramyaṁ vyasanāśrayaṁ ca 18 || 941
https//bitly/2wta1x6, And thus kingship is neither pleasure nor dharma so that the kings of old when age came on with it’s unavoidable suffering felt disgust and giving up their kingdoms betook themselves to the forest,itthaṁ ca rājyaṁ na sukhaṁ na dharmaḥ pūrve yathā jātaghṛṇā nareṁdrāḥ |vayaḥprakarṣe parihāryaduḥkhe rājyāni muktvā vanameva jagmuḥ || 942
https//bitly/2wta1x6, For it is better to eat herbs in the forest embracing the highest contentment as if one were concealing a jewel than to live with the dangers to which sovereignty is exposed as if with loathsome black snakes,varaṁ hi bhuktāni tṛṇānyaraṇye toṣaṁ paraṁ ratnamivopaguhya |sahoṣitaṁ śrīsulabhairna caiva doṣairadṛśyairiva kṛṣṇasarpaiḥ || 943
https//bitly/2wta1x6, For it is praiseworthy for kings to leave their kingdoms and enter the forest in the desire for dharma but it is not fitting to break one’s vow and forsaking the forest to go to one’s home,ślāghyaṁ hi rājyāni vihāya rājñāṁ dharmābhilāṣeṇa vanaṁ praveṣṭum |bhagnapratijñasya na tūpapannaṁ vanaṁ parityajya gṛhaṁ praveṣṭum || 944
https//bitly/2wta1x6, For what man of resolution and good family having once gone to the forest in the desire for dharma would cast off the robe and dead to shame proceed to the city even of Puraṁdara,jātaḥ kule ko hi naraḥ sasattvo dharmābhilāṣeṇa vanaṁ praviṣṭaḥ |kāṣāyamutsṛjya vimuktalajjaḥ puraṁdarasyāpi puraṁ śrayeta || 945
https//bitly/2wta1x6, For only the man who from greed delusion or fear would take again the food he has vomited up would from greed delusion or fear abondon the lusts of the flesh and then return to them,lobhāddhi mohādathavā bhayena yo vāṁtamannaṁ punarādadīta |lobhātsa mohādathavā bhayena saṁtyajya kāmān punarādadīta || 946
https//bitly/2wta1x6, And the man who after escaping with difficulty from a burning house would enter that very house again only he after giving up the state of a householder because he sees its dangers would desire out of delusion to assume it again,yaśca pradīptāccharaṇātkathaṁcinniṣkramya bhūyaḥ praviśettadeva |gārhasthyamutsṛjya sa dṛṣṭadoṣo mohena bhūyo bhilaṣedgrahītum || 947
https//bitly/2wta1x6, As for the tradition that kings obtained final emancipation while remaining in their homes this is not the case How can the dharma of salvation in which quietude predominates be reconciled with the dharma of kings in which severity of action predominates,yā ca śrutirmokṣamavāptavanto nṛpā gṛhasthā iti naitadasti |śamapradhānaḥ kva ca mokṣadharmo daṁḍapradhānaḥ kva ca rājadharmaḥ || 948
https//bitly/2wta1x6, If a king delights in quietude his kingdom collapses if his mind turns to his kingdom his quietude is ruined For quietude and severity are incompatible like the union of water which is cold and fire which is hot,śame ratiścecchithilaṁ ca rājyaṁ rājye matiścecchamaviplavaśca |śamaśca taikṣṇyaṁ ca hi nopapannaṁ śītoṣṇayoraikyamivodakāgnyoḥ || 949
https//bitly/2wta1x6, Either therefore these lords of the earth resolutely cast aside their kingdoms and obtained quietude or stained by kingship they claimed to have attained liberation on the ground that their senses were under control but in fact only reached a state that was not final,tanniścayādvā vasudhādhipāste rājyāni muktvā śamamāptavaṁtaḥ |rājyāṁgitā vā nibhṛtendriyatvādanaiṣṭhike mokṣakṛtābhimānāḥ || 950
https//bitly/2wta1x6, Or let it be conceded they duly attained quietude while holding kingship still I have not gone to the forest with an undecided mind for having cut through the net known as home and kindred I am freed and have no intention of re-entering the net,teṣāṁ ca rājye stu śamo yathāvatprāpto vanaṁ nāhamaniścayena |chittvā hi pāśaṁ gṛhabaṁdhusaṁjñaṁ muktaḥ punarna pravivikṣurasmi || 951
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 42 Having heard the king’s son uttering this discourse well suitable to his virtues and knowledge of the soul freed from all desires full of sound reasons and weighty — the counsellor thus made answer,ityātmavijñānaguṇānurūpaṁ muktaspṛhaṁ hetumadūrjitaṁ ca |śrutvā nareṁdrātmajamuktavantaṁ pratyuttaraṁ maṁtradharo pyuvāca || 942 (952)
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 43 This resolve of thine is an excellent counsel not unfit in itself but only unfit at the present time it could not be thy duty loving duty as thou dost to leave thy father in his old age to sorrow,yo niścayo maṁtravarastavāyaṁ nāyaṁ na yukto na tu kālayuktaḥ |śokāya hitvā pitaraṁ vayaḥsthaṁ syāddharmakāmasya hi te na dharmaḥ || 943 (953)
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 44 Surely thy mind is not very penetrating or it is ill-skilled in examining duty wealth and pleasure 20 — when for the sake of an unseen result thou departest disregarding a visible end,nūnaṁ ca buddhistava nātisūkṣmā dharmārthakāmeṣvavicakṣaṇā vā |hetoradṛṣṭasya phalasya yastvaṁ pratyakṣamarthaṁ paribhūya yāsi || 9 44 (954)
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 45 Again some say that there is another birth — others with confident assertion say that there is not since then the matter is all in doubt it is right to enjoy the good fortune which comes into thy hand,punarbhavo stīti ca kecidāhurnāstīti kecinniyatapratijñāḥ |evaṁ yadā saṁśayito yamarthastasmāt kṣamaṁ bhoktumupasthitā śrīḥ || 945 (955)
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 46 If there is any activity hereafter we will enjoy ourselves in it as may offer or if there is no activity beyond this life then there is an assured liberation to all the world without any effort,bhūyaḥ pravṛttiryadi kācidasti raṁsyāmahe tatra yathopapattau |atha pravṛttiḥ parato na kācitsiddho prayatnājjagato sya mokṣaḥ || 946 (956)
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 47 Some say there is a future life but they do not allow the possibility of liberation as fire is hot by nature and water liquid so they hold that there is a special nature in our power of action 21,astīti kecitparalokamāhurmokṣasya yogaṁ na tu varṇayaṁti |agneryathā hyuṣṇamapāṁ dravatvaṁ tadvatpravṛttau prakṛtiṁ vadaṁti || 947 (957)
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 48 Some maintain that all things arise from inherent properties — both good and evil and existence and non-existence and since all this world thus arises spontaneously therefore also all effort of ours is vain,kecitsvabhāvāditi varṇayaṁti śubhāśubhaṁ caiva bhavābhavau ca |svābhāvikaṁ sarvamidaṁ ca yasmādato pi mogho bhavati prayatnaḥ || 948 (958)
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 49 Since the action of the senses is fixed and so too the agreeableness or the disagreeableness of outward objects — then for that which is united to old age and pains what effort can avail to alter it Does it not all arise spontaneously,yadiṁdriyāṇāṁ niyataḥ pracāraḥ priyāpriyatvaṁ viṣayeṣu caiva |saṁyujyate yajjarayārttibhiśca kastatra yatno nanu sa svabhāvaḥ || 949 (959)
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 50 The fire becomes quenched by water and fire causes 22 water to evaporate and different elements united in a body producing unity bear up the world,adbhirhutāśaḥ śamamabhyupaiti tejāṁsi cāpo gamayaṁti śoṣam |bhinnāni bhūtāni śarīrasaṁsthānyaikyaṁ ca dattvā jagadudvahaṁti || 950 (960)
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 51 That the nature of the embryo in the womb is produced as composed of hands feet belly back and head and that it is also united with the soul — the wise declare that all this comes of itself spontaneously,yatpāṇipādodarapṛṣṭhamūrdhnā nirvartate garbhagatasya bhāvaḥ |yadātmanastasya ca tena yogaḥ svābhāvikaṁ tatkathayaṁti tajjñāḥ || 951 (961)
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 52 Who causes the sharpness of the thorn or the various natures of beasts and birds All this has arisen spontaneously there is no acting from desire how then can there be such a thing as will,kaḥ kaṁṭakasya prakaroti taikṣṇyaṁ vicitrabhāvaṁ mṛgapakṣiṇāṁ vā |svabhāvataḥ sarvamidaṁ pravṛttaṁ na kāmakāro sti kutaḥ prayatnaḥ || 952 (962)
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 53 Others say that creation comes from Īśvara what need then is there of the effort of the conscious soul 23 That which is the cause of the action of the world is also determined as the cause of its ceasing to act,sargaṁ vadaṁtīśvaratastathānye tatra prayatne puruṣaṣya ko rthaḥ |ya eva heturjagataḥ pravṛttau heturnivṛttau niyataḥ sa eva || 953 (963)
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 54 Some say that the coming into being and the destruction of being are alike caused by the soul but they say that coming into being arises without effort while the attainment of liberation is by effort,kecidvadaṁtyātmanimittameva prādurbhavaṁ caiva bhavakṣayaṁ ca |prādurbhavaṁ tu pravadaṁtyayatnādyatnena mokṣādhigamaṁ bruvaṁti || 954 (964)
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 55 A man discharges his debt to his ancestors by begetting offspring to the saints by sacred lore to the gods by sacrifices he is born with these three debts upon him — whoever has liberation (from these) he indeed has liberation,naraḥ pit�oṇāmanṛṇaḥ prajābhirvedairṛṣīṇāṁ kratubhiḥ surāṇām |utpadyate sārdhamṛṇaistribhistairyasyāsti mokṣaḥ kila tasya mokṣaḥ || 955 (965)
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 56 Thus by this series of rules the wise promise liberation to him who uses effort but however ready for effort with all their energy those who seek liberation will find weariness,ityevametena vidhikrameṇa mokṣaṁ sayatnasya vadaṁti tajjñāḥ |prayatnavaṁto pi hi vikrameṇa mumukṣavaḥ khedamavāpnuvaṁti || 956 (966)
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 57 Therefore gentle youth if thou hast a love for liberation follow rightly the prescribed rule thus wilt thou thyself attain to it and the king’s grief will come to an end,tatsaumya mokṣe yadi bhaktirasti nyāyena sevasva vidhiṁ yathoktam |evaṁ bhaviṣyatyupapattirasya saṁtāpanāśaśca narādhipasya || 957 (967)
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 58 And as for thy meditations on the evils of life ending in thy return from the forest to thy home — let not the thought of this trouble thee my son — those in old time also have returned from the forests to their houses,yā ca pravṛttā bhavadoṣabuddhistapovanebhyo bhavanaṁ praveṣṭum |tatrāpi ciṁtā tava tāta mā bhūt pūrve pi jagmuḥ svagṛhaṁ vanebhyaḥ || 958 (968)
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 59 The king Ambarīṣa 24 though he had dwelt in the forest went back to the city surrounded by his children so too Rāma seeing the earth oppressed by the base came forth from his hermitage and ruled it again,tapovanastho pi vṛtaḥ prajābhirjagāma rājā puramaṁbarīṣaḥ |tathā mahīṁ viprakṛtāmanāryaistapovanādetya rarakṣa rāmaḥ || 959 (969)
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 60 So too Drumākṣa the king of the Śālvas came to his city from the forest with his son and Sāṁkṛti Antideva 25 after he had become a Brahmarṣi received his royal dignity from the saint Vaśiṣṭha’,tathaiva śālvādhipatirdrumākṣo vanātsasūnuḥ svapuraṁ praviśya |brahmarṣibhūtaśca munervaśiṣṭhāddadhre śriyaṁ sāṁkṛtiraṁtidevaḥ || 960 (970)
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 61 Such men as these illustrious in glory and virtue left the forests and came back to their houses therefore it is no sin to return from a hermitage to one’s home if it be only for the sake of duty’,evaṁvidhā dharmayaśaḥpradīptā vanāni hitvā bhavanānyabhīyuḥ |tasmānna doṣo sti gṛhaṁ praveṣṭuṁ tapovanāddharmanimittameva || 961 (971)
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 62 Then having heard the affectionate and loyal words of the minister who was as the eye of the king — firm in his resolve the king’s son made his answer with nothing omitted or displaced 26 neither tedious 27 nor hasty,tato vacastasya niśamya maṁtriṇaḥ priyaṁ hitaṁ caiva nṛpasya cakṣuṣaḥ |anūnamavyastamasaktamadrutaṁ dhṛtau sthito rājasuto bravīdvacaḥ || 962 (972)
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 63 This doubt whether anything exists or not is not to be solved for me by another’s words having determined the truth by asceticism or quietism I will myself grasp whatever is ascertained concerning it,ihāsti nāstīti ya eṣa saṁśayaḥ parasya vākyairna mamātra niścayaḥ |avetya tattvaṁ tapasā śamena vā svayaṁ grahīṣyāmi yadatra niścitam || 963 (973)
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 64 It is not for me to accept a theory which depends on the unknown and is all controverted and which involves a hundred prepossessions what wise man would go by another’s belief Mankind are like the blind directed in the darkness by the blind,na me kṣamaṁ saṁgaśataṁ hi darśanaṁ grahītumavyaktaparaṁ parāhatam |buddhaḥ parapratyayato hi ko vrajejjano ṁdhakāre ṁdha ivāṁdhadeśitaḥ || 964 (974)
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 65 But even though I cannot discern the truth yet still if good and evil are doubted let one’s mind be set on the good even a toil 28 in vain is to be chosen by him whose soul is good while the man of base soul has no joy even in the truth,adṛṣṭatattvasya sato pi kiṁ tu me śubhāśubhe saṁśayite śubhe matiḥ |vṛthāpi khedo pi varaṁ śubhātmanaḥ sukhaṁ na tattve pi vigarhitātmanaḥ || 965 (975)
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 66 But having seen that this sacred tradition is uncertain know that that only is right which has been uttered by the trustworthy and know that trustworthiness means the absence of faults he who is without faults will not utter an untruth,imaṁ tu dṛṣṭvāgamamavyavasthitaṁ yaduktamāptaistadavehi sādhviti |prahīṇadoṣatvamavehi cāptatāṁ prahīṇadoṣo hyanṛtaṁ na vakṣyati || 966 (976)
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 67 And as for what thou saidst to me in regard to my returning to my home by alleging Rāma and others as examples they are no authority — for in determining duty how canst thou quote as authorities those who have broken their vows,gṛhapraveśaṁ prati yacca me bhavānuvāca rāmaprabhṛtīn nidarśanam |na te pramāṇaṁ na hi dharmaniścayeṣvalaṁ pramāṇāya parikṣatavratāḥ || 967 (977)
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 68 Even the sun therefore may fall to the earth even the mountain Himavat may lose its firmness but never would I return to my home as a man of the world with no knowledge of the truth and my senses only alert for external objects,tadevamapyeva ravirmahīṁ patedapi sthiratvaṁ himavān giristyajet |adṛṣṭatattvo viṣayonmukheṁdriyaḥ śrayeya na tveva gṛhān pṛthagjanaḥ || 968 (978)
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 69 I would enter the blazing fire but not my house with my purpose unfulfilled’ Thus he proudly made his resolve and rising up in accordance with it full of disinterestedness went his way,ahaṁ viśeyaṁ jvalitaṁ hutāśanaṁ na cākṛtārthaḥ praviśeyamālayam |iti pratijñāṁ sa cakāra garvito yatheṣṭamutthāya ca nirmamo yayau || 969 (979)
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 70 Then the minister and the Brāhman both full of tears having heard his firm determination and having followed him awhile with despondent looks and overcome with sorrow slowly returned of necessity to the city,tataḥ savāṣpau sacivadvijāvubhau niśamya tasya sthirameva niścayam |viṣaṇṇavaktrāvanugamya duḥkhitau śanairagatyā purameva jagmatuḥ || 970 (980)
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 71 Through their love for the prince and their devotion to the king they returned and often stopped looking back 29 they could neither behold him on the road nor yet lose the sight of him — shining in his own splendour and beyond the reach of all others like the sun,tatsnehādatha nṛpateśca bhaktitastau sāpekṣaṁ pratiyayatuśca tasthatuśca |durdharṣaṁ ravimiva dīptamātmabhāsā taṁ draṣṭuṁ na hi pathi śekaturna moktum || 971 (981)
https//bitly/2wta1x6, 72 Having placed faithful emissaries in disguise to find out the actions of him who was the supreme refuge of all they went on with faltering steps saying to each other How shall we approach the king and see him who is longing for his dear son’,tau jñātuṁ paramagatergatiṁ tu tasya pracchannāṁścarapuruṣāñchucīn vidhāya |rājānaṁ priyasutalālasaṁ nu gatvā drakṣyāvaḥ kathamiti jagmatuḥ kathaṁcit || 972 (982)
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 1 The prince he of the broad and lusty chest having thus dismissed the minister and the priest crossed the Ganges with its speeding waves and went to Rājagṛha with its beautiful palaces,sa rājavatsaḥ pṛthupīnavakṣāstau havyamaṁtrādhikṛtau vihāya |uttīrya gaṁgāṁ pracalattaraṁgāṁ śrīmadgṛhaṁ rājagṛhaṁ jagāma || 101
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 2 He reached the city distinguished by the five hills well guarded and adorned with mountains and supported and hallowed by auspicious sacred places 01 — like Brahman 02 in a holy calm going to the uppermost heaven,śailaiḥ suguptaṁ ca vibhūṣitaṁ ca dhṛtaṁ ca pūtaṁ ca śivaistapodaiḥ |paṁcācalāṁkaṁ nagaraṁ prapede śāṁtaḥ svayaṁbhūriva nākapṛṣṭham || 102
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 3 Having heard of his majesty and strength and his splendid beauty surpassing all other men the people of that region were all astonished as at him who has a bull for his sign and is immovable in his vow 03,gāṁbhīryamojaśca niśāmya tasya vapuśca dīptaṁ puruṣānatītya |visismiye tatra janastadānīṁ sthāṇuvratasyeva vṛṣadhvajasya || 103
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 4 On seeing him he who was going elsewhere stood still and he who was standing there followed him in the way he who was walking gently and gravely ran quickly and he who was sitting at once sprang up,taṁ prekṣya yo nyena yayau sa tasthau yaścātra tasthau pathi so nvagacchat |drutaṁ yayau yaṁ sadayaṁ sadhīraṁ yaḥ kaścidāste sma sa cotpapāta || 104
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 5 Some people reverenced him with their hands others in worship saluted him with their heads some addressed him with affectionate words — not one went on without paying him homage,kaścittamānarca janaḥ karābhyāṁ satkṛtya kaścicchirasā vavaṁde |snigdhena kaścidvacasābhyanaṁdannaivaṁ jagāmāpratipūjya kaścit || 105
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 6 Those who were wearing gay-coloured dresses were ashamed when they saw him those who were talking on random subjects fell to silence on the road no one indulged in an improper thought as at the presence of Religion herself embodied,taṁ jihriyuḥ prekṣya vicitraveṣāḥ prakīrṇavācaḥ pathi maunamīyuḥ |dharmasya sākṣādiva saṁnikarṣānna kaścidanyāyamatirbabhūva || 106
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 7 In the men and the women on the highway even though they were intent on other business that conduct alone with the profoundest reverence seemed proper which is enjoined by the rules of royal homage but his eyes never looked upon them,anyakriyāṇāmapi rājamārge strīṇāṁ nṛṇāṁ vā bahumānapūrvam |tadeva kalpaṁ naradevasūtraṁ nirīkṣamāṇā na tu tasya dṛṣṭiḥ || 107
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 8 His brows his forehead his mouth or his eyes — his body his hands his feet or his gait — whatever part of him any one beheld that at once riveted his eyes,bhruvau lalāṭaṁ mukhamīkṣaṇaṁ vā vapuḥ karau vā caraṇau gatiṁ vā |yadeva yastasya dadarśa tatra tadeva tasyānubabaṁdha cakṣuḥ || 108
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 9 Having beheld him with the beautiful circle of hair between his brows 04 and with long eyes with his radiant body and his hands showing a graceful membrane between the fingers — so worthy of ruling the earth and yet wearing a mendicant’s dress — the Goddess of Rājagṛha was herself perturbed,dṛṣṭvā śubhorṇabhruvamāyatākṣaṁ jvalaccharīraṁ śubhajālahastam |taṁ bhikṣuveśaṁ kṣitipālanārhaṁ saṁcukṣubhe rājagṛhasya lakṣmīḥ || 109
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 10 Then Śreṇya 05 the lord of the court of the Magadhas beheld from the outside of his palace the immense concourse of people and asked the reason of it and thus did a man recount it to him,śreṇyo tha bhartā magadhājirasya vāhyādvimānādvipulaṁ janaugham |dadarśa papraccha ca tasya hetuṁ tatastamasmai puruṣaḥ śaśaṁsa || 1010
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 11 He who was thus foretold by the Brāhmans he will either attain supreme wisdom or the empire of the earth — it is he the son of the king of the Śākyas who is the ascetic whom the people are gazing at’,jñānaṁ paraṁ vā pṛthivīśriyaṁ vā viprairya ukto dhigamiṣyatīti |sa eva śākyādhipatestanūjo nirīkṣyate pravrajito janena || 1011
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 12 The king having heard this and perceived its meaning with his mind thus at once spoke to that man Let it be known whither he is going’ and the man receiving the command followed the prince,tataḥ śrutārtho manasā gatārtho rājā babhāṣe puruṣaṁ tameva |vijñāyatāṁ kva pratigacchatīti tathetyathainaṁ puruṣo nvagacchat || 1012
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 13 With unrestless eyes seeing only a yoke’s length before him 06 with his voice hushed and his walk slow and measured he the noblest of mendicants went begging alms keeping his limbs and his wandering thoughts under control,alolacakṣuryugamātradarśī nivṛttavāgyaṁtritamaṁdagāmī |cacāra bhikṣāṁ sa tu bhikṣuvaryo nidhāya gātrāṇi calaṁ ca cetaḥ || 1013
