https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 14 Having received such alms as were offered he retired to a lonely cascade of the mountain and having eaten it there in the fitting manner he ascended the mountain Pāṇḍava 07,ādāya bhaikṣaṁ ca yathopapannaṁ yayau gireḥ prasravaṇaṁ viviktam |nyāyena tatrābhyavahṛtya cainanmahīdharaṁ pāṁḍavamāruroha || 1014
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 15 In that wood thickly filled with lodhra trees having its thickets resonant with the notes of the peacocks he the sun of mankind shone wearing his red dress like the morning sun above the eastern mountain,tasminvane lodhravanopagūḍhe mayūranādapratipūrṇakuṁje |kāṣāyavāsāḥ sa babhau nṛsūryo yathodayasyopari bālasūryaḥ || 1015
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 16 That royal attendant having thus watched him there related it all to the king Śreṇya and the king when he heard it in his deep veneration started himself to go thither with a modest retinue,tatraivamālokya sa rājabhṛtyaḥ śreṇyāya rājñe kathayāṁ cakāra |saṁśrutya rājā sa ca bāhumānyāttatra pratasthe nibhṛtānuyātraḥ || 1016
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 17 He who was like the Pāṇḍavas in heroism and like a mountain in stature ascended Pāṇḍava that noblest of mountains — a crown-wearer of lion-like gait a lion among men as a maned lion ascends a mountain,sa pāṁḍavaṁ pāṁḍavatulyavīryaḥ śailottamaṁ śailasamānavarṣmā |maulīdharaḥ siṁhagatirnṛsiṁhaścalatsaṭaḥ siṁha ivāruroha || 1017
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 18 There he beheld the Bodhisattva resplendent as he sat on his hams with subdued senses as if the mountain were moving 08 and he himself were a peak thereof — like the moon rising from the top of a cloud,calasya tasyopari śṛṁgabhūtaṁ śāṁteṁdriyaṁ paśyati bodhisattvam |paryaṁkamāsthāya virocamānaṁ śaśāṁkamudyaṁtamivābhrakūṭāt || 1018
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 19 Him distinguished by his beauty of form and perfect tranquillity as the very creation of Religion herself — filled with astonishment and affectionate regard the king of men approached as Indra the self-existent (Brahman),taṁ rūpalakṣmyā ca śamena caiva dharmasya nirmāṇamivopadiṣṭam |savismayaḥ praśrayavān nareṁdraḥ svayaṁbhuvaṁ śakra ivopatasthe || 1019
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 20 He the chief of the courteous having courteously drawn nigh to him inquired as to the equilibrium of his bodily humours and the other with equal gentleness assured the king of his health of mind and freedom from all ailments,taṁ nyāyato nyāyavatāṁ variṣṭhaḥ sametya papraccha ca dhātusāmyam |sa cāpyavocatsadṛśena sāmnā nṛpaṁ manaḥsvāsthyamanāmayaṁ ca || 1020
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 21 Then the king sat down on the clean surface of the rock dark blue like an elephant’s ear and being seated 09 with the other’s assent he thus spoke desiring to know his state of mind,tataḥ śucau vāraṇakarṇanīle śilātale sau niṣasāda rājā |nṛpopaviśyānumataśca tasya bhāvaṁ vijijñāsuridaṁ babhāṣe || 1021
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 22 I have a strong friendship with thy family come down by inheritance and well proved since from this a desire to speak to thee my son has arisen in me therefore listen to my words of affection,prītiḥ parā me bhavataḥ kulena kramāgatā caiva parīkṣitā ca |jātā vivakṣā suta yā yato me tasmādidaṁ snehavaco nibodha || 1022
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 23 When I consider thy widespread race beginning with the sun thy fresh youth and thy conspicuous beauty — whence comes this resolve of thine so out of all harmony with the rest set wholly on a mendicant’s life not on a kingdom,ādityapūrvaṁ vipulaṁ kulaṁ te navaṁ vayo dīptamidaṁ vapuśca |kasmādiyaṁ te matirakrameṇa bhaikṣāka evābhiratā na rājye || 1023
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 24 Thy limbs are worthy of red sandal-wood 10 perfumes — they do not deserve the rough contact of red cloth this hand is fit to protect subjects it deserves not to hold food given by another,gātraṁ hi te lohitacaṁdanārhaṁ kāṣāyasaṁśleṣamanarhametat |hastaḥ prajāpālanayogya eṣa bhoktuṁ na cārhaḥ paradattamannam || 1024
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 25 If therefore gentle youth through thy love for thy father thou desirest not thy paternal kingdom in thy generosity — then at any rate thy choice must not be excused — accepting forthwith one half of my kingdom,tatsaumya rājyaṁ yadi paitṛkaṁ tvaṁ snehātpiturnecchasi vikrameṇa |na ca kṣamaṁ marṣayituṁ matiste bhuktvārdhamasmadviṣayasya śīghram || 1025
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 26 If thou actest thus there will be no violence shown to thine own people and by the mere lapse of time imperial power at last flies for refuge to the tranquil mind therefore be pleased to do me a kindness — the prosperity of the good becomes very powerful when aided by the good 11,evaṁ hi na syātsvajanāvamardaḥ kālakrameṇāpi śamaśrayā śrīḥ |tasmātkuruṣva praṇayaṁ mayi tvaṁ sadbhiḥ sahīyā hi satāṁ samṛddhiḥ || 1026
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 27 But if from thy pride of race thou dost not now feel confidence in me then plunge with thy arrows into countless armies and with me as thy ally seek to conquer thy foes,atha tvidānīṁ kulagarvitatvādasmāsu viśraṁbhaguṇo na te sti |vyūhānyanekāni vigāhya vāṇairmayā sahāyena parāñjigīṣa || 1027
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 28 Choose thou therefore one of these ends pursue according to rule religious merit wealth and pleasure for these love and the rest in reverse order are the three objects in life when men die they pass into dissolution as far as regards this world,tadbuddhimatrānyatarāṁ vṛṇīṣva dharmārthakāmān vidhivadbhajasva |vyatyasya rāgādi ha hi trivargaṁ pretyeha vibhraṁśamavāpnuvaṁti || 1028
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 29 That which is pleasure when it has overpowered wealth and merit is wealth when it has conquered merit and pleasure so too it is merit when pleasure and wealth fall into abeyance but all would have to be alike abandoned if thy desired end 12 were obtained,yo hyarthadharmau paripīḍya kāmaḥ syāddharmakāmye paribhūya cārthaḥ |kāmārthayoścoparameṇa dharmastyājyaḥ sa kṛtsno yadi kāṁkṣitārthaḥ || 1029
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 30 Do thou therefore by pursuing the three objects of life cause this beauty of thine to bear its fruit they say that when the attainment of religion wealth and pleasure is complete in all its parts then the end of man is complete,tasmāttrivargasya niṣevaṇena tvaṁ rūpametatsaphalaṁ kuruṣva |dharmārthakāmādhigamaṁ hyanūnaṁ nṛṇāmanūnaṁ puruṣārthamāhuḥ || 1030
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 31 Do not thou let these two brawny arms lie useless which are worthy to draw the bow they are well fitted like Māndhātṛ’s to conquer the three worlds much more the earth,tanniṣphalau nārhasi kartumetau pīnau bhujau cāpavikarṣaṇārhau |māṁdhātṛvajjetumimau hi yogyau lokāni hi trīṇi hi kiṁ punargām || 1031
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 32 I speak this to you out of affection — not through love of dominion or through astonishment beholding this mendicant-dress of thine I am filled with compassion and I shed tears,snehena khalvetadahaṁ bravīmi naiśvaryarāgeṇa na vismayena |imaṁ hi dṛṣṭvā tava bhikṣuveśaṁ jātānukaṁpo smyapi cāgatāśruḥ || 1032
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 33 O thou who desirest the mendicant’s stage of life enjoy pleasures now in due time O thou lover of religion thou shalt practise religion — ere old age comes on and overcomes this thy beauty well worthy of thy illustrious race,tadbhuṁkṣva bhikṣāśramakāma kāmānkāle si kartā priyadharma dharmam |yāvatsvavaṁśapratirūparūpaṁ na te jarābhyetyabhibhūya bhūyaḥ || 1033
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 34 The old man can obtain merit by religion old age is helpless for the enjoyment of pleasures therefore they say that pleasures belong to the young man wealth to the middle-aged and religion to the old,śaknoti jīrṇaḥ khalu dharmamāptuṁ kāmopabhogeṣvagatirjarāyāḥ |ataśca yūnaḥ kathayaṁti kāmānmadhyasya vittaṁ sthavirasya dharmam || 1034
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 35 Youth in this present world is the enemy of religion and wealth — since pleasures however we guard them are hard to hold therefore wherever pleasures are to be found there they seize them,dharmasya cārthasya ca jīvaloke pratyarthibhūtāni hi yauvanāni |saṁrakṣyamāṇānyapi durgrahāṇi kāmā yatastena yathā haraṁti || 1035
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 36 Old age is prone to reflection’ 13 it is grave and intent on remaining quiet it attains unimpassionedness with but little effort unavoidably and for very shame,vayāṁsi jīrṇāni vimarśayaṁti dhīrāṇyavasthānaparāyaṇāni |alpena yatnena śamātmakāni bhavaṁtyagatyeva ca lajjayā ca || 1036
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 37 Therefore having passed through the deceptive period of youth fickle intent on external objects heedless impatient not looking at the distance — they take breath like men who have escaped safe through a forest,ataśca lolaṁ viṣayapradhānaṁ pramattamakṣāṁtamadīrghadarśi |bahucchalaṁ yauvanamabhyatītya nistīrya kāṁtāramivāśvasaṁti || 1037
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 38 Let therefore this fickle time of youth first pass by reckless and giddy — our early years are the mark for pleasure they cannot be kept from the power of the senses,tasmādadhīraṁ capalapramādi navaṁ vayastāvadidaṁ vyapaitu |kāmasya pūrvaṁ hi vayaḥ śaravyaṁ na śakyate rakṣitumiṁdriyebhyaḥ || 1038
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 39 Or if religion is really thy one aim then offer sacrifices — this is thy family’s immemorial custom — climbing to highest heaven by sacrifices even Indra the lord of the winds went thus to highest heaven,athau cikīrṣā tava dharma eva yajasva yajñaṁ kuladharma eṣaḥ |yajñairadhiṣṭhāya hi nākapṛṣṭhaṁ yayau marutvānapi nākapṛṣṭham || 1039
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 40 With their arms pressed 14 by golden bracelets and their variegated diadems resplendent with the light of gems royal sages have reached the same goal by sacrifices which great sages reached by self-mortification’,suvarṇakeyūravidaṣṭabāhavo maṇipradīpojjvalacitramaulayaḥ |nṛparṣayastāṁ hi gatiṁ gatā makhaiḥ śrameṇa yāmeva mahārṣayo yayuḥ || 1040
https//bitly/2xgEaQC, 41 Thus spoke the monarch of the Magadhas who spoke well and strongly like Indra 16 but having heard it the prince did not falter (firm) like the mountain Kailāsa having its many summits variegated (with lines of metals),ityevaṁ magadhapatir 15 babhāṣe yaḥ samyagvalabhidiva dhruvaṁ babhāṣe |tacchrutvā na sa vicacāra rājasūnuḥ kailāso giririva naikacitrasānuḥ || 1041
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 1 Being thus addressed by the monarch of the Magadhas in a hostile speech with a friendly face self-possessed unchanged pure by family and personal purity the son of Śuddhodana thus made answer,athaivamukto magadhādhipena suhṛnmukhena pratikūlamartham |svastho vikāraḥ kulaśaucaśuddhaḥ śauddhodanirvākyamidaṁ jagāda || 111
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 2 This is not to be called a strange thing for thee born as thou art in the great family whose ensign is the lion 01 — that by thee of pure conduct O lover of thy friends this line of conduct should be adopted towards him who stands as one of thy friends,nāścaryametadbhavato bhidhātuṁ jātasya haryaṁkakule viśāle |yanmitrapakṣe tava mitrakāma syādvṛttireṣā pariśuddhavṛtteḥ || 112
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 3 Amongst the bad a friendship worthy of their family ceases to continue (and fades) like prosperity among the faint-hearted it is only the good who keep increasing the old friendship of their ancestors by a new succession of friendly acts,asatsu maitrī svakulānurūpā na tiṣṭhati śrīriva viklaveṣu |pūrvaiḥ kṛtāṁ prītiparaṁparābhistāmeva saṁtastu vivardhayaṁti || 113
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 4 But those men who act unchangingly towards their friends in reverses of fortune I esteem in my heart as true friends who is not the friend of the prosperous man in his times of abundance,ye cārthakṛcchreṣu bhavaṁti loke samānakāryāḥ suhṛdāṁ manuṣyāḥ |mitrāṇi tānīti paraimi buddhyā svasthasya vṛddhiṣviha ko hi na syāt || 114
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 5 So those who having obtained riches in the world employ them for the sake of their friends and religion — their wealth has real solidity and when it perishes it produces no pain at the end,evaṁ ca ye dravyamavāpya loke mitreṣu dharme ca niyojayaṁti |avāptasārāṇi dhanāni teṣāṁ bhraṣṭāni nāṁte janayaṁti tāpam || 115
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 6 This thy determination concerning me O king is prompted by pure generosity and friendship 02 I will meet thee courteously with simple friendship I would not utter aught else in my reply,suhṛttayā cāryatayā ca rājan vibhāvya māmeva viniścayaste |atrānuneṣyāmi suhṛttayaiva brūyāmahaṁ nottaramanyadatra || 116
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 7 I having experienced the fear of old age and death fly to this path of religion in my desire for liberation leaving behind my dear kindred with tears in their faces — still more then those pleasures which are the causes of evil,ahaṁ jarāmṛtyubhayaṁ viditvā mumukṣayā dharmamimaṁ prapannaḥ |baṁdhūnpriyānaśrumukhān vihāya prāgeva kāmānaśubhasya hetūn || 117
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 8 I am not so afraid even of serpents nor of thunderbolts falling from heaven nor of flames blown together by the wind as I am afraid of these worldly objects,nāśīviṣebhyo pi tathā bibhemi naivāśanibhyo gaganāccyutebhyaḥ |na pāvakebhyo nilasaṁhitebhyo yathā bhayaṁ me viṣayebhya ebhyaḥ || 118
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 9 These transient pleasures — the robbers of our happiness and our wealth and which float empty and like illusions through the world — infatuate men’s minds even when they are only hoped for — still more when they take up their abode in the soul,kāmā hyanityāḥ kuśalārthacaurā riktāśca māyāsadṛśāśca loke |āśāsyamānā api mohayaṁti cittaṁ nṛṇāṁ kiṁ punarātmasaṁsthāḥ || 119
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 10 The victims of pleasure attain not to happiness even in the heaven of the gods still less in the world of mortals he who is athirst is never satisfied with pleasures as the fire the friend of the wind with fuel,kāmābhibhūtā hi na yāṁti śarma tripiṣṭape kiṁ vata martyaloke |kāmaiḥ satṛṣṇasya hi nāsti tṛptiryatheṁdhanairvātasakhasya vahneḥ || 1110
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 11 There is no calamity in the world like pleasures — people are devoted to them through delusion when he once knows the truth and so fears evil what wise man would of his own choice desire evil,jagatyanartho na samo sti kāmairmohācca teṣveva janaḥ prasaktaḥ |tattvaṁ viditvaivamanarthabhīruḥ prājñaḥ svayaṁ ko bhilaṣedanartham || 1111
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 12 When they have obtained all the earth girdled by the sea kings wish to conquer the other side of the great ocean mankind are never satiated with pleasures as the ocean with the waters that fall into it,samudravastrāmapi gāmavāpya pāraṁ jigīṣaṁti mahārṇavasya |lokasya kāmairna vitṛptirasti patadbhiraṁbhobhirivārṇavasya || 1112
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 13 When it had rained a golden shower from heaven and when he had conquered the continents and the four oceans and had even obtained the half of Śakra’s throne 03 Māndhātṛ was still unsatisfied with worldly objects,devena vṛṣṭe pi hiraṇyavarṣe dvīpānsamudrāṁścaturo pi jitvā |śakrasya cārdhāsanamapyavāpya māṁdhāturāsīdviṣayeṣvatṛptiḥ || 1113
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 14 Though he had enjoyed the kingdom of the gods in heaven when Indra had concealed himself through fear of Vṛtra and though in his pride he had made the great Ṛṣis bear his litter 04 Nahuṣa fell unsatisfied with pleasures,bhuktvāpi rājyaṁ divi devatānāṁ śatakratau vṛtrabhayātpranaṣṭe |darpānmahārṣīnapi vāhayitvā kāmeṣvatṛpto nahuṣaḥ papāta || 1114
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 15 King (Purūravas) the son of Iḍā having penetrated into the furthest heaven and brought the goddess Urvaśī into his power — when he wished in his greed to take away gold from the Ṛṣis 05 — being unsatisfied with pleasures fell into destruction,aiḍaśca rājā tridivaṁ vigāhya nītvāpi devīṁ vaśamurvaśīṁ tām |lobhādṛṣibhyaḥ kanakaṁ jihīrṣurjagāma nāśaṁ viṣayeṣvatṛptaḥ || 1115
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 16 Who would put his trust in these worldly objects whether in heaven or in earth unsettled as to lot or family — which passed from Bali to Indra and from Indra to Nahuṣa and then again from Nahuṣa back to Indra,balermaheṁdraṁ nahuṣaṁ maheṁdrādiṁdraṁ punarye nahuṣādupeyuḥ |svarge kṣitau vā viṣayeṣu teṣu ko viśvasedbhāgyakulākuleṣu || 1116
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 17 Who would seek these enemies bearing the name of pleasures by whom even those sages have been overcome who were devoted to other pursuits whose only clothes were rags whose food was roots fruits and water and who wore their twisted locks as long as snakes,cīrāṁbarā mūlaphalāṁbubhakṣā jaṭā vahaṁto pi bhujaṁgadīrghāḥ |yairanyakāryā munayo pi bhagnāḥ kaḥ kāmasaṁjñān mṛgayeta śatrūn || 1117
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 18 Those pleasures for whose sake even Ugrāyudha 06 armed terribly as he was with his weapon found death at Bhiṣma’s hands — is not the mere thought of them unlucky and fatal — still more the thought of the irreligious whose lives are spent in their service,ugrāyudhaścaugradhṛtāyudho pi yeṣāṁ kṛte mṛtyumavāpa bhīṣmāt |ciṁtāpi teṣāmaśivā vadhāya tadvṛttināṁ kiṁ punaravratānām || 1118
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 19 Who that considers the paltry flavour of worldly objects — the very height of union being only insatiety — the blame of the virtuous and the certain sin — has ever drawn near this poison which is called pleasure,āsvādamalpaṁ viṣayeṣu matvā saṁyojanotkarṣamatṛptimeva |sadbhyaśca garhāṁ niyataṁ ca pāpaṁ kaḥ kāmasaṁjñaṁ viṣamāsasāda || 1119
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 20 When they hear of the miseries of those who are intent on pleasure and are devoted to worldly pursuits 07 such as agriculture and the rest and the self-content of those who are careless of pleasure — it well befits the self-controlled to fling it away 08,kṛṣyādibhirdharmabhiranvitānāṁ kāmātmakānāṁ ca niśamya duḥkham |svāsthyaṁ ca kāmeṣvakutūhalānāṁ kāmān vihātuṁ kṣamamātmavadbhiḥ || 1120
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 21 Success in pleasure is to be considered a misery in the man of pleasure for he becomes intoxicated when his desired pleasures are attained through intoxication he does what should not be done not what should be done and being wounded thereby he falls into a miserable end,jñeyā vipatkāmini kāmasaṁpatsiddheṣu kāmeṣu madaṁ hyupaiti |madādakāryaṁ kurute na kāryaṁ yena kṣato durgatimabhyupaiti || 1121
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 22 These pleasures which are gained and kept by toil — which after deceiving leave you and return whence they came — these pleasures which are but borrowed for a time 09 what man of self-control if he is wise would delight in them,yatnena labdhāḥ parirakṣitāśca ye vipralabhya pratiyāṁti bhūyaḥ |teṣvātmavān yācitakopameṣu kāmeṣu vidvāniha ko rameta || 1122
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 23 What man of self-control could find satisfaction in these pleasures which are like a torch of hay — which excite thirst when you seek them and when you grasp them and which they who abandon not keep only as misery 10,anviṣya cādāya ca jātatarṣā yānatyajaṁtaḥ pariyāṁti duḥkham |loke tṛṇolkāsadṛśeṣu teṣu kāmeṣu kasyātmavato ratiḥ syāt || 1123
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 24 Those men of no self-control who are bitten by them in their hearts fall into ruin and attain not bliss — what man of self-control could find satisfaction in these pleasures which are like an angry cruel serpent,anātmavaṁto hṛdi yairvidaṣṭā vināśamarchaṁti na yāṁti śarma |kruddhaugrasarpapratimeṣu teṣu kāmeṣu kasyātmavato ratiḥ syāt || 1124
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 25 Even if they enjoy them men are not satisfied like dogs famishing with hunger over a bone — what man of self-control could find satisfaction in these pleasures which are like a skeleton composed of dry bones,asthi kṣudhārttā iva sārameyā bhuktvāpi yānnaiva bhavaṁti tṛptāḥ |jīrṇāsthikaṁkālasameṣu teṣu kāmeṣu kasyātmavato ratiḥ syāt || 1125
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 26 What man of self-control could find satisfaction in these pleasures which are like flesh that has been flung away and which produce misery by their being held only in common with kings thieves water and fire 11,ye rājacaurodakapāvakebhyaḥ sādhāraṇatvājjanayaṁti duḥkham |teṣu praviddhāmiṣasaṁnibheṣu kāmeṣu kasyātmavato ratiḥ syāt || 1126
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 27 What man of self-control could find satisfaction in these pleasures which like the senses 12 are destructive and which bring calamity on every hand to those who abide in them from the side of friends even more than from open enemies,yatra sthitānāmabhito vipattiḥ śatroḥ sakāśādapi bāṁdhavebhyaḥ |hiṁsreṣu teṣvāyatanopameṣu kāmeṣu kasyātmavato ratiḥ syāt || 1127
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 28 What man of self-control could find satisfaction in those pleasures which are like the fruit that grows on the top of a tree — which those who would leap up to reach fall down upon a mountain or into a forest waters or the ocean,girau vane cāpsu ca sāgare ca yadbhraṁśamarchaṁtyabhilaṁghamānāḥ |teṣu drumaprāgraphalopameṣu kāmeṣu kasyātmavato ratiḥ syāt || 1128
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 29 What man of self-control could find satisfaction in those pleasures which are like snatching up a hot coal — men never attain happiness however they pursue them increase them or guard them,tīrthaiḥ prayatnairvividhairavāptāḥ kṣaṇena ye nāśamiha prayāṁti | 1129svapnopabhogapratimeṣu teṣu kāmeṣu kasyātmavato ratiḥ syāt |
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 30 What man of self-control could find satisfaction in those pleasures which are like the enjoyments in a dream — which are gained by their recipients after manifold pilgrimages and labours and then perish in a moment,yānarcayitvāpi na yāṁti śarma vivardhayitvā paripālayitvā |aṁgārakarṣapratimeṣu teṣu kāmeṣu kasyātmavato ratiḥ syāt || 1130
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 31 What man of self-control could find satisfaction in those pleasures which are like a spear 13 sword or club — for the sake of which the Kurus the Vṛṣṇis and the Andhakas the Maithilas and the Daṇḍakas suffered destruction,vināśamīyuḥ kuravo yadarthaṁ vṛṣṇyaṁdhakā maithiladaṁḍakāśca |śūlāsikāṣṭhapratimeṣu teṣu kāmeṣu kasyātmavato ratiḥ syāt || 1131
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 32 What man of self-control could find satisfaction in those pleasures which dissolve friendships and for the sake of which the two Asuras Sunda and Upasunda perished victims engaged in mutual enmity,suṁdopasuṁdāvasurau yadarthamanyonyavairaprasṛtau vinaṣṭau |sauhārdaviśleṣakareṣu teṣu kāmeṣu kasyātmavato ratiḥ syāt || 1132
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 33 None however their intellect is blinded with pleasure give themselves up as in compassion to ravenous beasts 14 so what man of self-control could find satisfaction in those pleasures which are disastrous and constant enemies,kāmāṁdhasaṁjñāḥ kṛpayā va ke ca kravyātsu nātmānamihotsṛjaṁti |sapatnabhūteṣvaśiveṣu teṣu kāmeṣu kasyātmavato ratiḥ syāt || 1133
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 34 He whose intellect is blinded with pleasure does pitiable things he incurs calamities such as death bonds and the like the wretch who is the miserable slave of hope for the sake of pleasure well deserves the pain of death even in the world of the living,kāmāṁdhasaṁjñaḥ kṛpaṇaṁ karoti prāpnoti duḥkhaṁ vadhabaṁdhanādi |kāmārthamāśākṛpaṇastapasvī mṛtyuśramaṁ cārhati jīvaloke || 1134
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 35 Deer are lured to their destruction by songs 15 insects for the sake of the brightness fly into the fire the fish greedy for the flesh swallows the iron hook — therefore worldly objects produce misery as their end,gītairhriyaṁte hi mṛgā vadhāya rūpārthamagnau śalabhāḥ pataṁti |matsyo giratyāyasamāmiṣārthī tasmādanarthaṁ viṣayāḥ phalaṁti || 1135
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 36 As for the common opinion pleasures are enjoyments none of them when examined are worthy of being enjoyed fine garments and the rest are only the accessories of things — they are to be regarded as merely the remedies for pain,kāmāstu bhogā iti yanmataṁ syādbhogyā na kecitparigaṇyamānāḥ |vastrādayo dravyaguṇā hi loke duḥkhapratīkāra iti pradhāryāḥ || 1136
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 37 Water is desired for allaying thirst food in the same way for removing hunger a house for keeping off the wind the heat of the sun and the rain and dress for keeping off the cold and to cover one’s nakedness,iṣṭaṁ hi tarṣapraśamāya toyaṁ kṣunnāśahetoraśanaṁ tathaiva |vātātapāṁbvāvaraṇāya veśma kaupīnaśītāvaraṇāya vāsaḥ || 1137
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 38 So too a bed is for removing drowsiness a carriage for remedying the fatigue of a journey a seat for alleviating the pain of standing so bathing as a means for washing health and strength,nidrāvighātāya tathaiva śayyā yānaṁ tathādhvaśramanāśanāya |tathāsanaṁ sthānavinodanāya snānaṁ mṛjārogyabalāśrayāya || 1138
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 39 External objects therefore are to human beings means for remedying pain not in themselves sources of enjoyment what wise man would allow that he enjoys those delights which are only used as remedial,duḥkhapratīkāranimittabhūtāstasmātprajānāṁ viṣayā na bhogyāḥ |aśnāmi bhogāniti ko bhyupeyātprājñaḥ pratīkāravidhau pravṛttān || 1139
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 40 He who when burned with the heat of bilious fever maintains that cold appliances are an enjoyment when he is only engaged in alleviating pain — he indeed might give the name of enjoyment to pleasures,yaḥ pittadāhena vidahyamānaḥ śītakriyāṁ bhoga iti vyavasyet |duḥkhapratīkāravidhau pravṛttaḥ kāmeṣu kuryātsa hi bhogasaṁjñām || 1140
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 41 Since variableness is found in all pleasures I cannot apply to them the name of enjoyment the very conditions which mark pleasure bring also in its turn pain,kāmeṣvanaikāṁtikatā ca yasmādato pi me teṣu na bhogasaṁjñā |ya eva bhāvā hi sukhaṁ diśaṁti ta eva duḥkhaṁ punarāvahaṁti || 1141
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 42 Heavy garments and fragrant aloe-wood are pleasant in the cold but an annoyance in the heat 16 and the moonbeams and sandal-wood are pleasant in the heat but a pain in the cold,gurūṇi vāsāṁsyagurūṇi caiva sukhāya śīte hyasukhāya gharme |caṁdrāṁśavaścaṁdanameva coṣṇe sukhāya duḥkhāya bhavaṁti śīte || 1142
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 43 Since the well-known opposite pairs 17 such as gain and loss and the rest are inseparably connected with everything in this world — therefore no man is invariably happy on the earth nor invariably wretched,dvaṁdvāni sarvasya yataḥ prasaktānyalābhalābhaprabhṛtīni loke |ato pi naikāṁtasukho sti kaścinnaikāṁtaduḥkhaḥ puruṣaḥ prṭhivyām || 1143
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 44 When I see how the nature of pleasure and pain are mixed I consider royalty and slavery as the same a king does not always smile nor is a slave always in pain,dṛṣṭvā ca miśrāṁ sukhaduḥkatāṁ me rājyaṁ ca dāsyaṁ ca mataṁ samānam |nityaṁ hasatyeva hi naiva rājā na cāpi saṁtapyata eva dāsaḥ || 1144
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 45 Since to be a king involves a wider range of command therefore the pains of a king are great for a king is like a peg 18 — he endures trouble for the sake of the world,ājñā nṛpatve bhyadhiketi yasmātmahāṁti duḥkhānyata eva rājñaḥ |āsaṁgakāṣṭhapratimo hi rājā lokasya hetoḥ parikhedameti || 1145
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 46 A king is unfortunate if he places his trust in his royalty which is apt to desert and loves crooked turns 19 and on the other hand if he does not trust in it then what can be the happiness of a timid king,rājye nṛpastyāgini vaṁkamitre viśvāsamāgacchati cedvipannaḥ |athāpi viśraṁbhamupaiti neha kiṁ nāma saukhyaṁ cakitasya rājñaḥ || 1146
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 47 And since after even conquering the whole earth one city only can serve as a dwelling-place and even there only one house can be inhabited is not royalty mere labour for others,yadā ca jitvāpi mahīṁ samagrāṁ vāsāya dṛṣṭaṁ puramekameva |tatrāpi caikaṁ bhavanaṁ niṣevyaṁ śramaḥ parārthe nanu rājabhāvaḥ || 1147
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 48 And even in royal clothing one pair of garments is all he needs and just enough food to keep off hunger so only one bed and only one seat all a king’s other distinctions are only for pride,rājyo pi vāse yugamekameva kṣutsaṁnirodhāya tathānnamātrā |śayyā tathaikāsanamekameva śeṣā viśeṣā nṛpatermadāya || 1148
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 49 And if all these fruits are desired for the sake of satisfaction I can be satisfied without a kingdom and if a man is once satisfied in this world are not all distinctions indistinguishable,tuṣṭyarthametacca phalaṁ yadīṣṭamṛte pi rājyānmama tuṣṭirasti |tuṣṭau ca satyāṁ puruṣasya loke sarve viśeṣā nanu nirviśeṣāḥ || 1149
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 50 He then who has attained the auspicious road to happiness is not to be deceived in regard to pleasures remembering thy professed friendship tell me again and again do they keep their promise,tannāsti kāmān prati saṁpratāryaḥ kṣeme śivaṁ mārgamanuprapannaḥ |smṛtvā suhṛttvaṁ tu punaḥ punarmāṁ brūhi pratijñāṁ khalu pālayaṁti || 1150
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 51 I have not repaired to the forest through anger nor because my diadem has been dashed down by an enemy’s arrows nor have I set my desires on loftier objects 20 that I thus refuse thy proposal,na hyasmyamarṣeṇa vanapraviṣṭo na śatrubāṇairavadhūtamauliḥ |kṛtaspṛho nāpi phalādhikebhyo gṛhṇāmi naitadvacanaṁ yataste || 1151
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 52 Only he who having once let go a malignant incensed serpent or a blazing hay-torch all on fire would strive again to seize it would ever seek pleasures again after having once abandoned them,yo daṁdaśūkaṁ kupitaṁ bhujaṁgaṁ muktvā vyavasyeddhi punargrahītum |dāhātmikāṁ vā jvalitāṁ tṛṇaulkāṁ saṁtyajya kāmānsa punarbhajeta || 1152
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 53 Only he who though seeing would envy the blind though free the bound though wealthy the destitute though sound in his reason the maniac — only he I say would envy one who is devoted to worldly objects,aṁdhāya yaśca spṛhayedanaṁdho baddhāya mukto vidhanāya vāḍhyaḥ |unmattacittāya ca kalyacittaḥ spṛhāṁ sa kuryādviṣayātmakāya || 1153
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 54 He who lives on alms my good friend is not to be pitied having gained his end and being set on escaping the fear of old age and death he has here the best happiness perfect calm and hereafter all pains are for him abolished,bhikṣopabhogī vara nānukaṁpyaḥ kṛtī jarāmṛtyubhayaṁ titīrṣuḥ |ihottamaṁ śāṁtisukhaṁ ca yasya paratra duḥkhāni ca saṁvṛtāni || 1154
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 55 But he is to be pitied who is overpowered by thirst though set in the midst of great wealth — who attains not the happiness of calm here while pain has to be experienced hereafter,lakṣmyāṁ mahatyāmapi vartamānastṛṣṇābhibhūtastvanukaṁpitavyaḥ |prāpnoti yaḥ śāṁtisukhaṁ na ceha paratra duḥkhaṁ pratigṛhyate ca || 1155
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 56 Thus to speak to me is well worthy of thy character thy mode of life and thy family and to carry out my resolve is also befitting my character my mode of life and my family,evaṁ tu vaktuṁ bhavato nurūpaṁ sattvasya vṛttasya kulasya caiva |mamāpi voḍhuṁ sadṛśaṁ pratijñāṁ sattvasya vṛttasya kulasya caiva || 1156
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 57 I have been wounded by the enjoyment of the world and I have come out longing to obtain peace I would not accept an empire free from all ill even in the third heaven how much less amongst men,ahaṁ hi saṁsārarasena viddho viniḥsṛtaḥ śāṁtamavāptukāmaḥ |neccheyamāptuṁ tridive pi rājyaṁ nirāmayaṁ kiṁ vata mānuṣeṣu || 1157
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 58 But as for what thou saidst to me O king that the universal pursuit of the three objects is the supreme end of man — and 21 thou saidst that what I regard as the desirable is misery — thy three objects are perishable and also unsatisfying,trivargasevāṁ nṛpa yattu kṛtsnataḥ paro manuṣyārtha iti tvamāttha mām |anartha ityāttha mamārthadarśanaṁ kṣayī trivargo hi na cāpi tarpakaḥ || 1158
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 59 But that world in which there is no old age nor fear no birth nor death nor anxieties 22 that alone I consider the highest end of man where there is no ever-renewed action,pade tu yasminna jarā na bhīrutā na janma naivoparamo na vādhayaḥ |tameva manye puruṣārthamuttamaṁ na vidyate yatra punaḥ punaḥ kriyā || 1159
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 60 And as for what thou saidst wait till old age comes for youth is ever subject to change — this want of decision is itself uncertain for age too can be irresolute and youth can be firm,yadapyavocaḥ paripālyatāṁ jarā navaṁ vayo gacchati vikriyāmiti |aniścayo yaṁ capalaṁ hi dṛśyate jarāpyadhīrā dhṛtimacca yauvanam || 1160
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 61 But since Fate 23 is so well skilled in its art as to draw the world in all its various ages into its power — how shall the wise man who desires tranquillity wait for old age when he knows not when the time of death will be,svakarmadakṣaśca yadā tu ko jagadvayaḥsu sarveṣu ca saṁvikarṣati |vināśakāle kathamavyavasthite jarā pratīkṣyā viduṣā śamepsunā || 1161
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 62 When death stands ready like a hunter with old age as his weapon and diseases scattered about as his arrows smiting down living creatures who fly like deer to the forest of destiny what desire can there be in any one for length of life,jarāyudho vyādhivikīrṇasāyako yadāṁtako vyādha ivāśritaḥ sthitaḥ |prajāmṛgān bhāgyavanāśritāṁstudan vayaḥprakarṣaṁ prati ko manorathaḥ || 1162
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 63 It well befits the youthful son or the old man or the child so to act with all promptitude that they may choose the action of the religious man whose soul is all mercy — nay better still his inactivity,suto yuvā vā sthaviro thavā śiśustathā tvarāvāniha kartumarhati |yathā bhaveddharmavataḥ kṛpātmanaḥ pravṛttiriṣṭā vinivṛttireva vā || 1163
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 64 And as for what thou saidst be diligent in sacrifices for religion such as are worthy of thy race and bring a glorious fruit — honour to such sacrifices I desire not that fruit which is sought by causing pain to others 24,yadāttha vā dīptaphalāṁ kulocitāṁ kuruṣva dharmāya makhakriyāmiti |namo makhebhyo na hi kāmaye sukhaṁ parasya duḥkhakriyayāpadiśyate || 1164
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 65 To kill a helpless victim through a wish for future reward — it would be an unseemly action for a merciful-hearted good man even if the reward of the sacrifice were eternal but what if after all it is subject to decay,paraṁ hi haṁtuṁ vivaśaṁ phalepsayā na yuktarūpaṁ karuṇātmanaḥ sataḥ |kratoḥ phalaṁ yadyapi śāśvataṁ bhavet tathāpi kṛtvā kimupakṣayātmakam || 1165
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 66 And even if true religion did not consist in quite another rule of conduct by self-restraint moral practice and a total absence of passion — still it would not be seemly to follow the rule of sacrifice where the highest reward is described as attained only by slaughter,bhavecca dharmo yadi nāparo vidhirvratena śīlena manaḥśamena vā |tathāpi naivārhati sevituṁ kratuṁ viśasya yasmin paramucyate phalam || 1166
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 67 Even that happiness which comes to a man while he stays in this world through the injury of another is hateful to the wise compassionate heart how much more if it be something beyond our sight in another life,ihāpi tāvatpuruṣasya tiṣṭhataḥ pravartate yatparahiṁsayā sukham |tadapyaniṣṭaṁ saghṛṇasya dhīmato bhavāṁtare kiṁ vata yanna dṛśyate || 1167
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 68 I am not to be lured into a course of action for future reward — my mind does not delight O king in future births these actions are uncertain and wavering in their direction like plants beaten by the rain from a cloud,na ca pratāryo smi phalapravṛttaye bhaveṣu rājan ramate na me manaḥ |latā ivāṁbhodharavṛṣṭitāḍitāḥ pravṛttayaḥ sarvagatā hi caṁcalā || 1168
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 69 I have come here with a wish to see next the seer Arāḍa who proclaims liberation I start this very day — happiness be to thee O king forgive my words which may seem harsh through their absolute freedom from passion 25,ihāgataścāhamito didṛkṣayā munerarāḍasya vimokṣavādinaḥ |prayāmi cādyaiva nṛpāstu te śivaṁ vacaḥ kṣamethāḥ śamatattvaniṣṭhuram || 1169
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 70 26Now therefore do thou guard (the world) like Indra in heaven guard it continually like the sun by thy excellencies guard its best happiness here guard the earth guard life by the noble 27 guard the sons of the good guard thy royal powers O king and guard thine own religion,atheṁdravaddivyava śaśvadarkavadguṇairava śreya ihāva gāmava |avāyurāryairava satsutān ava śriyaśca rājannava dharmamātmanaḥ || 1170
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 71 As in the midst of a sudden catastrophe arising from the flame of (fire) the enemy of cold a bird to deliver its body betakes itself to the enemy of fire (water) — so do thou when occasion calls betake thyself to deliver thy mind to those who will destroy the enemies of thy home’ 28,himāriketūdbhavasaṁplavāṁtare yathā dvijo yāti vimokṣayaṁstanum |himāriśatruṁ kṣayaśatrughātinastathāṁtare yāhi vimocayanmanaḥ || 1171
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 72 The king himself folding his hands with a sudden longing come upon him replied Thou art obtaining thy desire without hindrance when thou hast at last accomplished all that thou hast to do thou shalt show hereafter thy favour towards me’,nṛpo bravītsāṁjalirāgataspṛho yatheṣṭamāpnoti bhavānavighnataḥ |avāpya kāle kṛtakṛtyatāmimāṁ mamāpi kāryo bhavatā tvanugrahaḥ || 1172
https//bitly/2iisXd4, 73 Having given his firm promise to the monarch he proceeded to the Vaiśvantara hermitage and after watching him with astonishment as he wandered on in his course the king and 29 his courtiers returned to the mountain (of Rājagiri),sthiraṁ pratijñāya tatheti pārthive tataḥ sa vaiśvaṁtaramāśramaṁ yayau |parivrajaṁtaṁ samudīkṣya vismito nṛpo pi ca prāpurimaṁ giriṁ vrajan || 1173
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 1 Then the moon of the Ikṣvāku race turned towards the hermitage of the sage Arāḍa 01 of tranquil life — as it were doing honour to it by his beauty,tataḥ śamavihārasya munerikṣvākucaṁdramāḥ |arāḍasyāśramaṁ bheje vapuṣā pūrayanniva || 121
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 2 He drew near on being addressed in a loud voice Welcome’ by the kinsman of Kālāma as he saw him from afar,sa kālāmasagotreṇa tenālokyaiva dūrataḥ |uccaiḥ svāgatamityuktaḥ samīpamupajagmivān || 122
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 3 They having mutually asked after each other’s health as was fitting sat down in a clean place on two pure wooden seats,tāvubhau nyāyataḥ pṛṣṭvā dhātusāmyaṁ parasparam |dāravyormedhyayorvṛṣyoḥ śucau deśe niṣīdatuḥ || 123
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 4 The best of sages having seen the prince seated and as it were drinking in the sight of him with eyes opened wide in reverence thus addressed him,tamāsīnaṁ nṛpasutaṁ so bravīnmunisattamaḥ |bahumānaviśālābhyāṁ darśanābhyāṁ pibanniva 02 || 124
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 5 I know gentle youth how thou hast come forth from thy home having severed the bond of affection as a wild elephant its cord,viditaṁ me yathā saumya niṣkrāṁto bhavanādasi |chittvā snehamayaṁ pāśaṁ pāśaṁ dṛpta iva dvipaḥ || 125
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 6 In every way thy mind is stedfast and wise who hast come here after abandoning royal luxury like a creeper-plant with poisonous fruit,sarvathā dhṛtimaccaiva prājñaṁ caiva manastava |yastvaṁ prāptaḥ śriyaṁ tyaktvā latāṁ viṣaphalāmiva || 126
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 7 It is no marvel that kings have retired to the forest who have grown old in years having given up their glory to their children like a garland left behind after being used,nāścaryaṁ jīrṇavayaso yajjagmuḥ pārthivā vanam |apatyebhyaḥ śriyaṁ dattvā bhuktocchiṣṭāmiva srajam || 127
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 8 But this is to me indeed a marvel that thou art come hither in life’s fresh prime set in the open field of the world’s enjoyments ere thou hast as yet tasted of their happiness,idaṁ me matamāścaryaṁ nave vayasi yadbhavān |abhuktveva śriyaṁ prāptaḥ sthito viṣayagocare || 128
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 9 Verily thou art a worthy vessel to receive this highest religion having mastered it with full knowledge cross at once over the sea of misery,tadvijñātumimaṁ dharmaṁ paramaṁ bhājanaṁ bhavān |jñānapūrvamadhiṣṭhāya śīghraṁ duḥkhārṇavaṁ tara || 129
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 10 Though the doctrine is generally efficient only after a time when the student has been thoroughly tested thou art easy for me to examine from thy depth of character and determination’,śiṣye yadyapi vijñāte śāstraṁ kālena vartate |gāṁbhīryādvyavasāyācca suparīkṣyo bhavān mama || 1210
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 11 The prince having heard these words of Arāḍa was filled with great pleasure and thus made reply,iti vākyamarāḍasya vijñāya sa narādhipaḥ |babhūva paramaprītaḥ provācottarameva ca || 1211
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 12 This extreme kindliness which thou showest to me calmly passionless as thou art makes me imperfect as I am seem even already to have attained perfection,viraktasyāpi yadidaṁ saumukhyaṁ bhavataḥ param |akṛtārtho pyanenāsmi kṛtārtha iva saṁprati || 1212
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 13 I feel at the sight of thee like one longing to see who finds a light — like one wishing to journey a guide — or like one wishing to cross a boat,didṛkṣuriva hi jyotiryiyāsuriva daiśikam |tvaddarśanādahaṁ manye titīrṣuriva ca plavam || 1213
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 14 Wilt thou therefore deign to tell me that secret if thou thinkest it should be told whereby thy servant may be delivered from old age death and disease’,tasmādarhasi tadvaktuṁ vaktavyaṁ yadi manyase |jarāmaraṇarogebhyo yathāyaṁ parimucyate || 1214
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 15 Arāḍa thus impelled by the noble nature of the prince declared in a concise form the tenets of his doctrine,ityarāḍaḥ kumārasya māhātmyādeva coditaḥ |saṁkṣiptaṁ kathayāṁ cakre svasya śāstrasya niścayam || 1215
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 16 O best of hearers hear this our firmly-settled theory how our mortal existence arises and how it revolves,śrūyatāmayamasmākaṁ siddhāṁtaḥ śṛṇvatāṁ vara |yathā bhavati saṁsāro yathā vai parivartate || 1216
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 17 “The evolvent and the evolute birth old age and death — know that this has been called the reality by us do thou receive our words O thou who art stedfast in thy nature,prakṛtiśca vikāraśca janma mṛtyurjaraiva ca |tattāvatsattvamityuktaṁ sthirasattva parehi naḥ || 1217
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 18 But know O thou who art deep in the search into the nature of things that the five elements 03 egoism intellect and the unmanifested are the evolvents,tatra tu prakṛtirnāma viddhi prakṛtikovida |paṁca bhūtānyahaṁkāraṁ buddhimavyaktameva ca || 1218
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 19 But know that the evolutes consist of intellect external objects 04 the senses and the hands feet voice anus and generative organ and also the mind,vikāra iti buddhiṁ tu viṣayāniṁdriyāṇi ca |pāṇipādaṁ ca vādaṁ ca pāyūpasthaṁ tathā manaḥ || 1219
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 20 There is also a something which bears the name kṣetrajña from its knowledge of this field (kṣetra or the body) and those who investigate the soul call the soul kṣetrajña,asya kṣetrasya vijñānāt kṣetrajña iti saṁjñi ca |kṣetrajña iti cātmānaṁ kathayaṁtyātmaciṁtakāḥ || 1220
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 21 Kapila with his disciple became the illuminated — such is the tradition and he as the illuminated with his son is now called here Prajāpati,saśiṣyaḥ kapilaśceha pratibuddha iti smṛtiḥ |saputraḥ pratibuddhaśca prajāpatirihocyate || 1221
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 22 That which is born and grows old and is bound and dies — is to be known as the manifested and the unmanifested is to be distinguished by its contrariety,jāyate jīryate caiva budhyate mriyate ca yat |tadvyaktamiti vijñeyamavyaktaṁ tu viparyayāt || 1222
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 23 Ignorance the merit or demerit of former actions and desire are to be known as the causes of mundane existence he who abides in the midst of this triad does not attain to the truth of things —,ajñānaṁ karma tṛṣṇā ca jñeyāḥ saṁsārahetavaḥ |sthito smiṁstritaye yastu tatsattvaṁ nābhivartate || 1223
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 24 From mistake 05 egoism confusion fluctuation indiscrimination false means inordinate attachment and gravitation,vipratyayādahaṁkārātsaṁdehādabhisaṁplavāt |aviśeṣānupāyābhyāṁ saṁgādabhyavapātataḥ || 1224
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 25 Now mistake acts in a contrary manner it does wrongly what it should do and what it should think it thinks wrongly,tatra vipratyayo nāma viparītaṁ pravartate |anyathā kurute kāryaṁ maṁtavyaṁ manyate nyathā || 1225
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 26 “I say I know I go I am firmly fixed it is thus that egoism shows itself here O thou who art free from all egoism,bravīmyahamahaṁ vedmi gacchāmyahamahaṁ sthitaḥ |itīhaivamahaṁkārastvanahaṁkāra vartate || 1226
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 27 That state of mind is called confusion O thou who art all unconfused which views under one nature massed like a lump of clay objects that thus become confused in their nature,yastu bhāvena saṁdigdhānekībhāvena paśyati |mṛtpiṁḍavadasaṁdeha saṁdehaḥ sa ihocyate || 1227
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 28 That state of mind which says that this mind intellect and these actions are the same as I and that which says that all this aggregate is the same as I — is called fluctuation,ya evāhaṁ sa evedaṁ mano buddhiśca karma ca |yaścaivaṁ sa gaṇaḥ so hamiti yaḥ so bhisaṁplavaḥ || 1228
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 29 That state of mind is called indiscrimination O thou who art discriminating which thinks there is no difference between the illuminated and the unwise and between the different evolvents,aviśeṣaṁ viśeṣajña pratibuddhāprabuddhayoḥ |prakṛtīnāṁ ca yo veda so viśeṣa iti smṛtaḥ || 1229
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 30 Uttering namas and vaṣaṭ sprinkling water upon sacrifices &c with or without the recital of Vedic hymns and such like rites — these are declared by the wise to be false means O thou who art well skilled in true means,namaskāravaṣaṭkārau prokṣaṇābhyukṣaṇādayaḥ |anupāya iti prājñairupāyajña praveditaḥ || 1230
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 31 That is called inordinate attachment by which the fool is entangled in external objects through his mind speech actions and thoughts O thou who hast shaken thyself free from all attachments,sajjate yena durmedhā manovākkarmabuddhibhiḥ |viṣayeṣvanabhiṣvaṁga so bhiṣvaṁga iti smṛtaḥ || 1231
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 32 The misery which a man imagines by the ideas This is mine I am connected with this is to be recognised as gravitation — by this a man is borne downwards into new births,mamedamahamasyeti yadduḥkhamabhimanyate |vijñeyo bhyavapātaḥ sa saṁsāre yena pātyate || 1232
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 33 Thus Ignorance O ye wise being fivefold in its character energises towards torpor delusion the great delusion and the two kinds of darkness 06,ityavidyā hi vidvāṁsaḥ paṁcaparvā samīhate |tamo mohaṁ mahāmohaṁ tāmisradvayameva ca || 1233
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 34 Know that among these indolence is torpor death and birth are delusion and be it clearly understood O undeluded one that desire is the great delusion,tatrālasyaṁ tamo viddhi mohaṁ mṛtyuṁ ca janma ca |mahāmohastvasaṁmoha kāma ityavagamyatām || 1234
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 35 Since by it even the higher beings are deluded therefore O hero is this called the great delusion,yasmādatra ca bhūtāni pramuhyaṁti mahāṁtyapi |tasmādeṣa mahābāho mahāmoha iti smṛtaḥ || 1235
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 36 They define anger O thou angerless one as darkness and despondency O undesponding they pronounce to be the blind darkness,tāmisramiti cākrodha krodhamevādhikurvate |viṣādaṁ cāṁdhatāmisramaviṣāda pracakṣate || 1236
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 37 The child entangled in this fivefold ignorance is effused in his different births in a world abounding with misery,anayāvidyayā bālaḥ saṁyuktaḥ paṁcaparvayā |saṁsāre duḥkhabhūyiṣṭhe janmasvabhiniṣicyate || 1237
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 38 He wanders about in the world of embodied existence thinking that I am the seer and the hearer and the thinker — the effect and the cause,draṣṭā śrotā ca maṁtā ca kāryaṁ karaṇameva ca |ahamityevamāgamya saṁsāre parivartate || 1238
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 39 Through these causes 07 O wise prince the stream of torpor is set in motion be pleased to consider that in the absence of the cause there is the absence of the effect,ityebhirhetubhirdhīman tamaḥsrotaḥ pravartate |hetvabhāve phalābhāva iti vijñātumarhasi || 1239
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 40 Let the wise man who has right views know these four things O thou who desirest liberation — the illuminated and the unilluminated the manifested and the unmanifested,tatra samyagmatirvidyānmokṣakāma catuṣṭayam |pratibuddhāprabuddhau ca vyaktamavyaktameva ca || 1240
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 41 The soul having once learned to distinguish these four properly having abandoned all (ideas of) straightness or quickness 08 attains to the immortal sphere,yathāvadetadvijñāya kṣetrajño hi catuṣṭayam |ārjavaṁ javatāṁ hitvā prāpnoti padamakṣaram || 1241
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 42 For this reason the Brāhmans in the world discoursing on the supreme Brahman practise here a rigorous course of sacred study and let other Brāhmans live with them to follow it also’,ityarthaṁ brāhmaṇā loke paramabrahmavādinaḥ |brahmacaryaṁ caraṁtīha brāhmaṇān vāsayaṁti ca || 1242
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 43 The prince having heard this discourse from the seer asked concerning the means and the final state,iti vākyamidaṁ śrutvā munestasya nṛpātmajaḥ |abhyupāyaṁ ca papraccha padameva ca naiṣṭhikam || 1243
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 44 Wilt thou please to explain to me how how far and where this life of sacred study is to be led and the limit of this course of life’ 09,brahmacaryamidaṁ caryaṁ yathā yāvacca yatra ca |dharmasyāsya ca paryaṁtaṁ bhavān vyākhyātumarhati || 1244
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 45 Then Arāḍa according to his doctrine declared to him in another way that course of life clearly and succinctly,ityarāḍo yathāśāstraṁ vispaṣṭārthaṁ samāsataḥ |tamevānyena kalpena dharmamasmai vyabhāṣata || 1245
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 46 The devotee in the beginning having left his house and assumed the signs of the mendicant goes on following a rule of conduct which extends to the whole life,ayamādau gṛhānmuktvā bhaikṣākaṁ liṁgamāśritaḥ |samudācāravistīrṇaṁ śīlamādāya vartate || 1246
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 47 Cultivating absolute content with any alms from any person he carries out his lonely life indifferent to all feelings meditating on the holy books and satisfied in himself,saṁtoṣaṁ paramāsthāya yena tena yatastataḥ |viviktaṁ sevate vāsaṁ nirdvaṁdvaḥ śāstravitkṛtī || 1247
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 48 Then having seen how fear arises from passion and the highest happiness from the absence of passion he strives by restraining all the senses to attain to tranquillity of mind,tato rāgādbhayaṁ dṛṣṭvā vairāgyācca paraṁ śivam |nigṛhṇanniṁdriyagrāmaṁ yatate manasaḥ śrame || 1248
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 49 Then he reaches the first stage of contemplation which is separated from desires evil intentions and the like and arises from discrimination and which involves reasoning 10,atho viviktaṁ kāmebhyo vyāpādādibhya eva ca |vivekajamavāpnoti pūrvadhyānaṁ vitarkavat || 1249
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 50 And having obtained this ecstatic contemplation and reasoning on various objects the childish mind is carried away by the possession of the new unknown ecstasy,tacca dhyānaṁ sukhaṁ prāpya tattadeva vitarkayan |apūrvasukhalābhena hriyate bāliśo janaḥ || 1250
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 51 With a tranquillity of this kind which disdains desire or dislike he reaches the world of Brahman deceived by the delight,śamenaivaṁvidhenāyaṁ kāmadveṣavigarhiṇā |brahmalokamavāpnoti paritoṣeṇa vaṁcitaḥ || 1251
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 52 But the wise man knowing that these reasonings bewilder the mind reaches a (second) stage of contemplation separate from this which has its own pleasure and ecstasy,jñātvā vidvān vitarkāṁstu manaḥsaṁkṣobhakārakān |tadviyuktamavāpnoti dhyānaṁ prītisukhānvitam || 1252
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 53 And he who carried away by this pleasure sees no further distinction obtains a dwelling full of light even amongst the Ābhāsura deities,hriyamāṇastayā prītyā yo viśeṣaṁ na paśyati |sthānaṁ bhāsvaramāpnoti deveṣvābhāsureṣvapi || 1253
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 54 But he who separates his mind from this pleasure and ecstasy reaches the third stage of contemplation ecstatic but without pleasure,yastu prītisukhāttasmādvivecayati mānasam |tṛtīyaṁ labhate dhyānaṁ sukhaṁ prītivivarjitam || 1254
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 55 Upon this stage some teachers make their stand thinking that it is indeed liberation since pleasure and pain have been left behind and there is no exercise of the intellect,tatra kecidvyavasyaṁti mokṣa ityapi māninaḥ |sukhaduḥkhaparityāgādavyāpārācca cetasaḥ || 1255 (57)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 56 But he who immersed in this ecstasy strives not for a further distinction obtains an ecstasy in common with the Śubhakṛtsna deities,yastu tasminsukhe magno na viśeṣāya yatnavān |śubhakṛtsnaiḥ sa sāmānyaṁ sukhaṁ prāpnoti daivataiḥ || 1256 (55)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 57 But he who having attained such a bliss desires it not but despises it obtains the fourth stage of contemplation which is separate from all pleasure or pain,tādṛśaṁ sukhamāsādya yo na rajyannupekṣate |caturthaṁ dhyānamāpnoti sukhaduḥkhavivarjitam || 1257 (56)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 58 The fruit of this contemplation which is on an equality with the Vṛhatphala deities those who investigate the great wisdom call the Vṛhatphala 11,asya dhyānasya tu phalaṁ samaṁ devairvṛhatphalaiḥ |kathayaṁti vṛhatphalaṁ vṛhatprajñāparīkṣakāḥ || 1258
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 59 But rising beyond this contemplation having seen the imperfections of all embodied souls the wise man climbs to a yet higher wisdom in order to abolish all body,samādhervyutthitastasmāddṛṣṭvā doṣāṁścharīriṇām |jñānamārohati prājñaḥ śarīravinivṛttaye || 1259
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 60 Then having abandoned this contemplation being resolved to find a further distinction he becomes as disgusted with form itself as he who knows the real is with pleasures,tatastaddhyānamutsṛjya viśeṣe kṛtaniścayaḥ |kāmebhya iva satprājño rūpādapi virajyate || 1260
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 61 First he makes use of all the apertures of his body and next he exerts his will to experience a feeling of void space even in the solid parts 12,śarīre khāni yānyasya tānyādau parikalpayan |ghaneṣvapi tato dravyeṣvākāśamadhimucyate || 1261
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 62 But another wise man having contracted his soul which is by nature extended everywhere like the ether 13 — as he gazes ever further on detects a yet higher distinction,ākāśasamamātmānaṁ saṁkṣipya tvaparo budhaḥ |tadaivānaṁtataḥ paśyan viśeṣamadhigacchati || 1262
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 63 Another one of those who are profoundly versed in the supreme Self having abolished himself by himself sees that nothing exists and is called a Nihilist 14,adhyātmakuśaleṣvanyo nivartyātmānamātmanā |kiṁcinnāstīti saṁpaśyannākiṁcanya iti smṛtaḥ || 1263
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 64 Then like the Muñja-reed’s stalk 15 from its sheath or the bird from its cage the soul escaped from the body is declared to be liberated,tato muṁjādiṣīkeva śakuniḥ paṁjarādiva |kṣetrajño niḥsṛto dehānmukta ityabhidhīyate || 1264
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 65 This is that supreme Brahman constant eternal and without distinctive signs which the wise who know reality declare to be liberation,etattatparamaṁ brahma nirliṁgaṁ dhruvamakṣaram |yanmokṣa iti tattvajñāḥ kathayaṁti manīṣiṇaḥ || 1265
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 66 Thus have I shown to thee the means and liberation if thou hast understood and approved it then act accordingly,ityupāyaśca mokṣaśca mayā saṁdarśitastava |yadi jñātaṁ yadi ruci yathāvatpratipadyatām || 1266
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 67 Jaigīṣavya 16 and Janaka and the aged Parāsara by following this path were liberated and so were others who sought liberation’,jaigīṣavyo tha janako vṛddhaścaiva parāśaraḥ |imaṁ paṁthānamāsādya muktā hyanye ca mokṣiṇaḥ || 1267
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 68 The prince having not accepted his words but having pondered them filled with the force of his former arguments thus made answer,iti tasya sa tadvākyaṁ gṛhītvā na vicārya ca |pūrvahetubalaprāptaḥ pratyuttaramuvāca saḥ || 1268
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 69 I have heard this thy doctrine subtil and pre-eminently auspicious but I hold that it cannot be final because it does not teach us how to abandon this soul itself in the various bodies,śrutaṁ jñānamidaṁ sūkṣmaṁ parataḥ parataḥ śivam |kṣetreṣvasyāparityāgādavaimyetadanaiṣṭhikam || 1269
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 70 For I consider that the embodied soul though freed from the evolutes and the evolvents is still subject to the condition of birth and has the condition of a seed 17,vikāraprakṛtibhyo hi kṣetrajñaṁ muktamapyaham |manye prasavadharmāṇaṁ vījadharmāṇameva ca || 1270
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 71 Even though the pure soul is declared to be liberated yet as long as the soul remains there can be no absolute abandonment of it,viśuddho yadyapi hyātmā nirmukta iti kalpyate | 18a 18b (ab = 1271ab)atyaṁtastatparityāgaḥ satyātmani na vidyate || 1271 (cd = 1273cd)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 72 If we abandon successively all this triad yet distinction is still perceived as long as the soul itself continues there this triad continues in a subtil form,hitvā hitvā trayamidaṁ viśeṣastūpalabhyate |ātmanastu sthitiryatra tatra sūkṣmamidaṁ trayam || 12 72 (1274)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 73 It is held (by some) that this is liberation because the imperfections are so attenuated and the thinking power is inactive and the term of existence is so prolonged,sūkṣmatvāccaiva doṣāṇāmavyāpārācca cetasaḥ |dīrghatvādāyuṣaścaiva mokṣastu parikalpyate || 1273 (1275)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 74 But as for this supposed abandonment of the principle of egoism — as long as the soul continues there is no real abandonment of egoism,ahaṁkāraparityāgo yaścaiṣa parikalpyate |satyātmani parityāgo nāhaṁkārasya vidyate || 1274 (1276)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 75 The soul does not become free from qualities as long as it is not released from number and the rest therefore as long as there is no freedom from qualities there is no liberation declared for it,saṁkhyādibhiramuktaśca nirguṇo na bhavatyayam |tasmādasati nairguṇye nāsya mokṣo bhidhīyate || 1275 (1277)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 76 There is no real separation of the qualities and their subject for fire cannot be conceived apart from its form and heat,guṇino hi guṇānāṁ ca vyatireko na vidyate |rūpoṣṇābhyāṁ virahito na hyagnirupalabhyate || 1276 (1278)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 77 Before the body there will be nothing embodied so before the qualities there will be no subject how if it was originally free could the soul ever become bound 19,prāgdehānna bhaveddehī prāgguṇebhyastathā guṇī |kasmādādau vimuktaḥ sañśarīrī badhyate punaḥ || 1277 (1279)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 78 The body-knower (the soul) which is unembodied must be either knowing or unknowing if it is knowing there must be some object to be known and if there is this object it is not liberated,kṣetrajño viśarīraśca jño vā syādajña eva vā |yadi jño jñeyamasyāsti jñeye sati na mucyate || 1278 (1280)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 79 Or if the soul is declared to be unknowing then of what use to you is this imagined soul Even without such a soul the existence of the absence of knowledge is notorious as for instance in a log of wood or a wall,athājña iti siddho vaḥ kalpitena kimātmanā |vināpi hyātmanājñānaṁ prasiddhaṁ kāṣṭhakuḍyavat || 1279 (1281)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 80 And since each successive abandonment is held to be still accompanied by qualities I maintain that the absolute attainment of our end can only be found in the abandonment of everything’,parataḥ paratastyāgo yasmāttu guṇavān smṛtaḥ |tasmātsarvaparityāgānmanye kṛtsnāṁ kṛtārthatām || 1280 (1282)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 81 Thus did he remain unsatisfied after he had heard the doctrine of Arāḍa then having decided it to be incomplete he turned away,iti dharmamarāḍasya viditvā na tutoṣa saḥ |akṛtsnamiti vijñāya tataḥ pratijagāma ha || 1281 (1283)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 82 Seeking to know the true distinction he went to the hermitage of Udraka 20 but he gained no clear understanding from his treatment of the soul,viśeṣamatha śuśrūṣurudrakasyāśramaṁ yayau |ātmagrāhācca tasyāpi jagṛhe na sa darśanam || 1282 (1284)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 83 For the sage Udraka having learned the inherent imperfections of the name and the thing named took refuge in a theory beyond Nihilism which maintained a name and a non-name,saṁjñāsaṁjñitvayordoṣaṁ jñātvā hi munirudrakaḥ |ākiṁcinyātparaṁ lebhe saṁjñāsaṁjñātmikāṁ gatim || 1283 (1285)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 84 And since even a name and a non-name were substrata however subtil he went even further still and found his restlessness set at rest in the idea that there is no named and no un-named,yasmāccālaṁbane sūkṣme saṁjñāsaṁjñe tataḥ param |nāsaṁjñī naiva saṁjñīti tasmāttatra gataspṛhaḥ || 1284 (1286)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 85 And because the intellect rested there not proceeding any further — it became very subtil and there was no such thing as un-named nor as named,yataśca buddhistatraiva sthitānyatrāpracāriṇī |sūkṣmāpādi tatastatra nāsaṁjñitvaṁ na saṁjñitā || 1285 (1287)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 86 But because even when it has reached this goal it yet returns again to the world therefore the Bodhisattva seeking something beyond left Udraka,yasmācca tamapi prāpya punarāvartate jagat |bodhisattvaḥ paraṁ prepsustasmādudrakamatyajat || 1286 (1288)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 87 Having quitted his hermitage fully resolved in his purpose and seeking final bliss he next visited the hermitage called a city of the royal sage Gaya,tato hitvāśramaṁ tasya śreyo rthī kṛtaniścayaḥ |bheje gayasya rājarṣernagarīsaṁjñamāśramam || 1287 (1289)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 88 Then on the pure bank of the Nairañjanā the saint whose every effort was pure fixed his dwelling bent as he was on a lonely habitation,atha nairaṁjanātīre śucau śuciparākramaḥ |cakāra vāsamekāṁtavihārābhivratī muniḥ || 1288 (12 90)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, (Then he saw five mendicants who had come there before him they had taken vows on themselves and practised austerities vaunting themselves of control of the five senses),21<,> tatpūrvaṁ paṁceṁdriyavaśoddhatān |tapaḥ <xx> vratino bhikṣūn paṁca niraikṣata || (1291)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 89 Five mendicants desiring liberation came up to him when they beheld him there just as the objects of the senses come up to a percipient who has gained wealth and health by his previous merit,paṁcopatasthurdṛṣṭvātra bhikṣavastaṁ mumukṣavaḥ |puṇyārjitadhanārogyamiṁdriyārthā iveśvaram || 1289 (1292)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 90 Being honoured by these disciples who were dwelling in that family as they bowed reverently with their bodies bent low in humility as the mind is honoured by the restless senses,saṁpūjyamānastaiḥ prahvairvinayānatamūrtibhiḥ |tadvaṁśasthāyibhiḥ śiṣyairlolairmana iveṁdriyaiḥ || 1290 (1293)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 91 And thinking this may be the means of abolishing birth and death’ he at once commenced a series of difficult austerities by fasting,mṛtyujanmāṁtakaraṇe syādupāyo yamityatha |duṣkarāṇi samārebhe tapāṁsyanaśanena saḥ || 1291 (1294)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 92 For six years vainly trying to attain merit 22 he practised self-mortification performing many rules of abstinence hard for a man to carry out,upavāsavidhīn nekān kurvan naradurācarān |varṣāṇi ṣaṭkarmaprepsurakarotkārśyamātmanaḥ || 1292 (1295)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 93 At the hours for eating he longing to cross the world whose farther shore is so difficult to reach broke his vow with single jujube fruits sesame seeds and rice,annakāleṣu caikaikaiḥ sakolatilataṁḍulaiḥ |apārapārasaṁsārapāraṁ prepsurapārayat || 1293 (1296)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 94 But the emaciation which was produced in his body by that asceticism became positive fatness through the splendour which invested him,dehādapacayastena tapasā tasya yaḥ kṛtaḥ |sa evopacayo bhūyastejasāsya kṛto bhavat || 1294 (1297)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 95 Though thin yet with his glory and his beauty unimpaired he caused gladness to other eyes as the autumnal moon in the beginning of her bright fortnight gladdens the lotuses,kṛśo pyakṛśakīrtiśrīrhlādaṁ cakre nyacakṣuṣam |kumudānāmiva śaracchuklapakṣādicaṁdramāḥ || 1295 (1298)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 96 Having only skin and bone remaining with his fat flesh and blood entirely wasted yet though diminished he still shone with undiminished grandeur like the ocean,tvagasthiśeṣo niḥśeṣairmedaḥpiśitaśoṇitaiḥ |kṣīṇo pyakṣīṇagāṁbhīryaḥ samudra iva sa vyabhāt || 1296 (1299)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 97 Then the seer having his body evidently emaciated to no purpose in a cruel self-mortification — dreading continued existence thus reflected in his longing to become a Buddha,atha kaṣṭatapaḥspaṣṭavyarthakliṣṭatanurmuniḥ |bhavabhīrurimāṁ cakre buddhiṁ buddhatvakāṁkṣayā || 1297 (12100)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 98 This is not the way to passionlessness nor to perfect knowledge nor to liberation that was certainly the true way which I found at the root of the Jambu 23 tree,nāyaṁ dharmo virāgāya na bodhāya na muktaye |jaṁbumūle mayā prāpto yastadā sa vidhirdhruvaḥ || 1298 (12101)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 99 But that cannot be attained by one who has lost his strength’ — so resuming his care for his body he next pondered thus how best to increase his bodily vigour,na cāsau durbalenāptuṁ śakyamityāgatādaraḥ |śarīrabalavṛddhyarthamidaṁ bhūyo nvaciṁtayat || 1299 (12102)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 100 Wearied with hunger thirst and fatigue with his mind no longer self-possessed through fatigue how should one who is not absolutely calm reach the end which is to be attained by his mind,kṣutpipāsāśramaklāṁtaḥ śramādasvasthamānasaḥ |prāpnuyānmanasāvāpyaṁ phalaṁ kathamanirvṛtaḥ || 12100 (12103)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 101 True calm is properly obtained by the constant satisfaction of the senses the mind’s self-possession is only obtained by the senses being perfectly satisfied,nirvṛtiḥ prāpyate samyaksatateṁdriyatarpaṇāt |saṁtarpiteṁdriyatayā manaḥsvāsthyamavāpyate || 12101 (12104)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 102 True meditation is produced in him whose mind is self-possessed and at rest — to him whose thoughts are engaged in meditation the exercise of perfect contemplation begins at once,svasthaprasannamanasaḥ samādhirupapadyate |samādhiyuktacittasya dhyānayogaḥ pravartate || 12102 (12105)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 103 By contemplation are obtained those conditions 24 through which is eventually gained that supreme calm undecaying immortal state which is so hard to be reached’,dhyānapravartanāddharmāḥ prāpyaṁte yairavāpyate |durlabhaṁ śāṁtamajaraṁ paraṁ tadamṛtaṁ padam || 12103 (12106)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 104 Having thus resolved this means is based upon eating food’ the wise seer of unbounded wisdom having made up his mind to accept the continuance of life,tasmādāhāramūlo yamupāya itiniścayaḥ |asūrikaraṇe dhīraḥ kṛtvāmitamatirmatim || 12104 (12107)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 105 And having bathed thin as he was slowly came up the bank of the Nairañjanā supported as by a hand by the trees on the shore which bent down the ends of their branches in adoration,snāto nairaṁjanātīrāduttatāra śanaiḥ kṛśaḥ |bhaktyāvanataśākhāgrairdattahastastaṭadrumaiḥ || 12105 (12108)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 106 Now at that time Nandabalā the daughter of the leader of the herdsmen impelled by the gods with a sudden joy risen in her heart had just come near,atha gopādhipasutā daivatairabhicoditā |udbhūtahṛdayānaṁdā tatra naṁdabalāgamat || 12106 (12109)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 107 Her arm gay with a white shell and wearing a dark blue woollen cloth like the river Yamunā with its dark blue water and its wreath of foam,sitaśaṁkhojjvalabhujā nīlakaṁbalavāsinī |sapheṇamālānīlāṁburyamuneva saridvarā || 12107 (12110)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 108 She having her joy increased by her faith with her lotus-like eyes opened wide bowed down before him and persuaded him to take some milk,sā śraddhāvardhitaprītirvikasallocanotpalā |śirasā praṇipatyainaṁ grāhayāmāsa pāyasam || 12108 (12111)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 109 By partaking that food having made her obtain the full reward of her birth he himself became capable of gaining the highest knowledge all his six senses being now satisfied,kṛtvā tadupabhogena prāptajanmaphalāṁ sa tām |bodhiprāptau samartho bhūtsaṁtarpitaṣaḍiṁdriyaḥ || 12109 (12112)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 110 The seer having his body now fully robust together with his glorious fame one beauty and one majesty being equally spread in both shone like the ocean and the moon 25,paryāptāpyānamūrtaśca sārdhaṁ suyaśasā muniḥ |kāṁtidhairyaikabhāraikaḥ śaśāṁkārṇavavalbabhau || 12110 (12113)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 111 Thinking that he had returned to the world the five mendicants left him as the five elements leave the wise soul when it is liberated,āvṛtta iti vijñāya taṁ jahuḥ paṁcabhikṣavaḥ |manīṣiṇamivātmānaṁ nirmuktaṁ paṁcadhātavaḥ || 12111 (12114)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 112 Accompanied only by his own resolve having fixed his mind on the attainment of perfect knowledge he went to the root of an Aśvattha tree 26 where the surface of the ground was covered with young grass,vyavasāyadvitīyo tha śādvalāstīrṇabhūtalam |so śvatthamūlaṁ prayayau bodhāya kṛtaniścayaḥ || 12112 (12115)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 113 Then Kāla 27 the best of serpents whose majesty was like the lord of elephants having been awakened by the unparalleled sound of his feet uttered this praise of the great sage being sure that he was on the point of attaining perfect knowledge,tatastadānīṁ gajarājavikramaḥ padasvanenānupamena bodhitaḥ |mahāmunerāgatabodhiniścayo jagāda kālo bhujagottamaḥ stutim || 12113 (12116)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 114 Inasmuch as the earth pressed down by thy feet O sage resounds repeatedly and inasmuch as thy splendour shines forth like the sun thou shalt assuredly to-day enjoy the desired fruit,yathā mune tvaccaraṇāvapīḍitā muhurmuhurniṣṭanatīva medinī |yathā ca te rājati sūryavatprabhā dhruvaṁ tvamiṣṭaṁ phalamadya bhokṣyase || 12114 (12117)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 115 Inasmuch as lines of birds fluttering in the sky offer thee reverential salutation O lotus-eyed one and inasmuch as gentle breezes blow in the sky thou shalt certainly to-day become the Buddha’,yathā bhramaṁtyo divi vāyapaṁktayaḥ pradakṣiṇaṁ tvāṁ kamalākṣa kurvate |yathā ca saumyā divi vāṁti vāyavastvamadya buddho niyataṁ bhaviṣyasi || 12115 (12118)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 116 Being thus praised by the best of serpents and having taken some pure grass from a grasscutter he having made his resolution sat down to obtain perfect knowledge at the foot of the great holy tree,tato bhujaṁgapravareṇa saṁstutastṛṇānyupādāya śucīni lāvakāt |kṛtapratijño niṣasāda bodhaye mahātarormūlamupāśritaḥ śuceḥ || 12116 (12119)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 117 Then he sat down on his hams in a posture immovably firm and with his limbs gathered into a mass like a sleeping serpent’s hood exclaiming I will not rise from this position on the earth until 28 I have obtained my utmost aim’,tataḥ sa paryaṁkamakaṁpyamuttamaṁ babaṁdha suptoragabhogapiṁḍitam |bhinadmi tāvadbhuvi naitadāsanaṁ na yāmi tāvatkṛtakṛtyatāmiti || 12117 (12120)
https//bitly/2vAtD1Z, 118 Then the dwellers in heaven burst into unequalled joy the herds of beasts and the birds uttered no cry the trees moved by the wind made no sound when the holy one took his seat firm in his resolve,tato yayurmudamatulāṁ divaukaso vavāsire na mṛgaganā na pakṣiṇaḥ |na sasvanurvanataravo nilāhatāḥ kṛtāsane bhagavati niścalātmani || 12118 (12121)
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 1 When the great sage sprung from a line of royal sages sat down there with his soul fully resolved to obtain the highest knowledge the whole world rejoiced but Māra the enemy of the good law was afraid,tasminśca bodhāya kṛtapratijñe rājarṣivaṁśaprabhave mahārṣau |tatropaviṣṭe prajaharṣa lokastatrāsa saddharmaripustu māraḥ || 131
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 2 He whom they call in the world Kāmadeva the owner of the various weapons the flower-arrowed the lord of the course of desire — it is he whom they also style Māra the enemy of liberation,yaṁ kāmadevaṁ pravadaṁti loke citrāyudhaṁ puṣpaśaraṁ tathaiva |kāmapracārādhipatiṁ tameva mokṣadviṣaṁ māramudāharaṁti || 132
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 3 His three sons Confusion Gaiety and Pride and his three daughters Lust Delight and Thirst 01 asked of him the reason of his despondency and he thus made answer unto them,tasyātmajā vibhramaharṣadarpāstisro ratiprītitṛṣaśca kanyāḥ |papracchurenaṁ manaso vikāraṁ sa tāṁśca tāścaiva vaco babhāṣe || 133
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 4 This sage wearing the armour of resolution and having drawn the arrow of wisdom with the barb of truth sits yonder intending to conquer my realms — hence is this despondency of my mind,asau munirniścayavarma bibhrat sattvāyudhaṁ buddhiśaraṁ vikṛṣya |jigīṣurāste viṣayānmadīyān tasmādayaṁ me manaso viṣādaḥ || 134
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 5 If he succeeds in overcoming me and proclaims to the world the path of final bliss all this my realm will to-day become empty as did that of the disembodied lord when he violated the rules of his station 02,yadi hyasau māmabhibhūya yāti lokāya cākhyātyapavargamārgam |śūnyastato yaṁ viṣayo mamādya vṛttāccyutasyeva videhabhartuḥ || 135
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 6 While therefore he stands within my reach and while his spiritual eyesight is not yet attained I will assail him to break his vow as the swollen might of a river assails a dam’,tadyāvadevaiṣa na labdhacakṣurmadgocare tiṣṭhati yāvadeva |yāsyāmi tāvadvratamasya bhettuṁ setuṁ nadīvega ivābhivṛddhaḥ || 136
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 7 Then having seized his flower-made bow and his five infatuating arrows he drew near to the root of the Aśvattha tree with his children he the great disturber of the minds of living beings,tato dhanuḥ puṣpamayaṁ gṛhītvā śarāṁstathā mohakarāṁśca paṁca |so śvatthamūlaṁ sasuto bhyagacchadasvāsthyakārī manasaḥ prajānām || 137
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 8 Having fixed his left hand on the end of the barb and playing with the arrow Māra thus addressed the calm seer as he sat on his seat preparing to cross to the further side of the ocean of existence,atha praśāṁtaṁ munimāsanasthaṁ pāraṁ titīrṣuṁ bhavasāgarasya |viṣajya savyaṁ karamāyudhāgre krīḍañśareṇedamuvāca māraḥ || 138
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 9 Up up O thou Kṣatriya afraid of death follow thine own duty and abandon this law of liberation and having conquered the lower worlds by thy arrows  proceed to gain the higher worlds of Indra,uttiṣṭha bhoḥ kṣatriya mṛtyubhīta varasva dharmaṁ tyaja mokṣadharmam |vāṇaiśca  03 vinīya lokān lokān parān prāpnuhi vāsavasya || 139
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 10 That is a glorious path to travel which has been followed by former leaders of men this mendicant life is ill-suited for one born in the noble family of a royal sage to follow,paṁthā hi niryātumayaṁ yaśasyo yo vāhitaḥ pūrvatamairnareṁdraiḥ |jātasya rājarṣikule viśāle bhaikṣākamaślāghyamidaṁ prapattum || 1310
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 11 But if thou wilt not rise strong in thy purpose — then be firm if thou wilt and quit not thy resolve — this arrow is uplifted by me — it is the very one which was shot against Sūryaka 04 the enemy of the fish,athādya nottiṣṭhasi niścitātmā bhava sthiro mā vimucaḥ pratijñām |mayodyato hyeṣa śaraḥ sa eva yaḥ sūryake mīnaripau vimuktaḥ || 1311
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 12 So too I think when somewhat probed by this weapon even the son of Iḍā 05 the grandson of the moon became mad and Sāntanu 06 also lost his self-control — how much more then one of feebler powers now that the age has grown degenerate,pṛṣṭaḥ sa cānena kathaṁcidaiḍaḥ somasya naptāpyabhavadvicittaḥ |sa cābhavacchāṁtanurasvataṁtraḥ kṣīṇe yuge kiṁ vata durbalo nyaḥ || 1312
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 13 Therefore quickly rise up and come to thyself - for this arrow is ready darting out its tongue which I do not launch even against the cakravāka birds tenderly attached as they are and well deserving the name of lovers’,tatkṣipramuttiṣṭha labhasva saṁjñāṁ vāṇo hyayaṁ tiṣṭhati lelihānaḥ |priyābhidheyeṣu ratipriyeṣu yaṁ cakravākeṣvapi notsṛjāmi || 1313
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 14 But when even though thus addressed the Śākya saint unheeding did not change his posture then Māra discharged his arrow at him setting in front of him his daughters and his sons 07,ityevamukto pi yadā nirāstho naivāsanaṁ śākyamunirbibheda |śaraṁ tato smai visasarja māraḥ kanyāśca kṛtvā purataḥ sutāṁśca || 1314
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 15 But even when that arrow was shot he gave no heed and swerved not from his firmness and Māra beholding him thus sank down and slowly thus spoke full of thought,tasmiṁstu vāṇe pi sa vipramukte cakāra nāsthāṁ na dhṛteścacāla |dṛṣṭvā tathainaṁ viṣasāda māraściṁtāparītaśca śanairjagāda || 1315
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 16 He does not even notice that arrow by which the god Śambhu was pierced with love for the daughter of the mountain 08 and shaken in his vow can he be destitute of all feeling is not this that very arrow,śaileṁdraputrīṁ prati yena viddho devo pi śaṁbhuścalito babhūva |na ciṁtayatyeṣa tameva vāṇaṁ kiṁ syādacitto na śaraḥ sa eṣaḥ || 1316
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 17 He is not worthy of my flower-shaft nor my arrow gladdener nor the sending of my daughter Rati (to tempt him) he deserves the alarms and rebukes and blows from all the gathered hosts of the demons’,tasmādayaṁ nārhati puṣpavāṇaṁ na harṣaṇaṁ nāpi raterniyogam |arhatyayaṁ bhūtagaṇairaśeṣaiḥ saṁtrāsanātarjanatāḍanāni || 1317
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 18 Then Māra called to mind his own army wishing to work the overthrow of the Śākya saint and his followers swarmed round wearing different forms and carrying arrows trees darts clubs and swords in their hands,sasmāra māraśca tataḥ svasainyaṁ vidhvaṁsanaṁ śākyamuneścikīrṣan |nānāśrayāścānucarāḥ parīyuḥ śaradrumaprāsagadāsihastāḥ || 1318
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 19 Having the faces of boars fishes horses asses and camels of tigers bears lions and elephants — one-eyed many-faced three-headed — with protuberant bellies and speckled bellies,varāhamīnāśvakharoṣṭravaktrā vyāghrarkṣasiṁhadviradānanāśca |ekekṣaṇā naikamukhāstriśīrṣā laṁbodarāścaiva pṛṣodarāśca || 1319
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 20 Blended with goats with knees swollen like pots armed with tusks and with claws carrying headless trunks in their hands and assuming many forms with half-mutilated faces and with monstrous mouths,ajāsu saktā ghaṭajānavaśca daṁṣṭrāyudhāścaiva nakhāyudhāśca |kabaṁdhahastā bahumūrtayaśca bhagnārdhavaktrāśca mahāmukhāśca || 1320
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 21 Copper-red covered with red spots bearing clubs in their hands with yellow or smoke-coloured hair with wreaths dangling down with long pendulous ears like elephants clothed in leather or wearing no clothes at all,tāmrāruṇā lohitaviṁducitrāḥ khaṭvāṁgahastā haridhūmrakeśāḥ |laṁbasrajo vāraṇalaṁbakarṇāścarmāṁbarāścaiva niraṁbarāśca || 1321
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 22 Having half their faces white or half their bodies green — red and smoke-coloured yellow and black — with arms reaching out longer than a serpent and with girdles jingling with rattling bells,śvetārdhavaktrā haritārdhakāyāstāmrāśca dhūmrā harayo sitāśca |vyāḍottarāsaṁgabhujāstathaiva praghuṣṭaghaṁṭākulamekhalāśca || 1322
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 23 Some were as tall as palm-trees carrying spears — others were of the size of children with projecting teeth others birds with the faces of rams others with men’s bodies and cats’ faces,tālapramāṇāśca gṛhītaśūlā daṁṣṭrākarālāśca śiśupramāṇāḥ |urabhravaktrāśca vihaṁgamāśca mārjāravaktrāśca manuṣyakāyāḥ || 1323
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 24 With dishevelled hair or with topknots or half-bald with rope-garments or with head-dress all in confusion — with triumphant faces or frowning faces — wasting the strength or fascinating the mind,prakīrṇakeśāḥ śikhino rdhamuṁḍā rajjvaṁbarā vyākulaveṣṭanāśca |prahṛṣṭavaktrā bhṛkuṭīmukhāśca tejoharāścaiva manoharāśca || 1324
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 25 Some as they went leaped about wildly others danced upon one another some sported about in the sky others went along on the tops of the trees,kecidvrajaṁto bhṛśamāvavalguranyo nyamāpupluvire tathānye |cikrīḍurākāśagatāśca kecitkecicca cerustarumastakeṣu || 1325
