https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 26 One danced shaking a trident another made a crash dragging a club another bounded for joy like a bull another blazed out flames from every hair,nanarta kaścidbhramayaṁstriśūlaṁ kaściddha pusphūrja gadāṁ vikarṣan |harṣeṇa kaścidvṛṣavannanarta kaścitprajajvāla tanūruhebhyaḥ || 1326
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 27 Such were the troops of demons who encircled the root of the Bodhi tree on every side eager to seize it and to destroy it awaiting the command of their lord,evaṁvidhā bhūtagaṇāḥ samaṁtāttadbodhimūlaṁ parivārya tasthuḥ |jighṛkṣavaścaiva jighāṁsavaśca bharturniyogaṁ paripālayaṁtaḥ || 1327
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 28 Beholding in the first half of the night that battle of Māra and the bull of the Śākya race the heavens did not shine and the earth shook and the (ten) regions of space flashed flame and roared,taṁ prekṣya mārasya ca pūrvarātre śākyarṣabhasyaiva ca yuddhakālam |na dyauścakāśe pṛthivī cakaṁpe prajajvaluścaiva diśaḥ saśabdāḥ || 1328
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 29 A wind of intense violence blew in all directions 09 the stars did not shine the moon gave no light and a deeper darkness of night spread around and all the oceans were agitated,viṣvagvavau vāyurudīrṇavegastārā na rejurna babhau śaśāṁkaḥ |tamaśca bhūyo vitatāra rātreḥ sarve ca saṁcukṣubhire samudrāḥ || 1329
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 30 The mountain deities 10 and the Nāgas who honoured the Law indignant at the attack on the saint rolling their eyes in anger against Māra heaved deep sighs and opened their mouths wide,mahībhṛto dharmaparāśca nāgā mahāmunervighnamamṛṣyamāṇāḥ |māraṁ prati krodhavivṛttanetrā niḥśaśvasuścaiva jajṛṁbhire ca || 1330
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 31 But the god-sages the Śuddhādhivāsas 11 being as it were absorbed in the perfect accomplishment of the good Law felt only a pity for Māra in their minds and through their absolute passionlessness were unruffled by anger,śuddhādhivāsā vibudharṣayastu saddharmasiddhyarthamiva pravṛttāḥ |māre nukaṁpāṁ manasā pracakrurvirāgabhāvāttu na roṣamīyuḥ || 1331
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 32 When they saw the foot of the Bodhi tree crowded with that host of Māra intent on doing harm — the sky was filled with the cry raised by all the virtuous beings who desired the world’s liberation,tadbodhimūlaṁ samavekṣya kīrṇaṁ hiṁsātmanā mārabalena tena |dharmātmabhirlokavimokṣakāmairbabhūva hāhākṛtamaṁtarīkṣam || 1332
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 33 But the great sage 12 having beheld that army of Māra thus engaged in an attack on the knower of the Law 13 remained untroubled and suffered no perturbation like a lion seated in the midst of oxen,upaplutaṁ dharmavidastu tasya dṛṣṭvā sthitaṁ mārabalaṁ mahārṣiḥ |na cukṣubhe nāpi yayau vikāraṁ madhye gavāṁ siṁha ivopaviṣṭaḥ || 1333
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 34 Then Māra commanded his excited army of demons to terrify him and forthwith that host resolved to break down his determination with their various powers,mārastato bhūtacamūmudīrṇāmājñāpayāmāsa bhayāya tasya |svaiḥ svaiḥ prabhāvairatha sāsya senā taddhairyabhedāya matiṁ cakāra || 1334
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 35 Some with many tongues hanging out and shaking with sharp-pointed savage teeth and eyes like the disk of the sun with wide-yawning mouths and upright ears like spikes — they stood round trying to frighten him,keciccalannaikavilaṁbijihvāstīkṣṇogradaṁṣṭrā harimaṁḍalākṣāḥ |vidāritāsyāḥ sthiraśaṁkukarṇāḥ saṁtrāsayaṁtaḥ kila nāma tasthuḥ || 1335
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 36 Before these monsters standing there so dreadful in form and disposition the great sage remained unalarmed and untroubled sporting with them as if they had been only rude children 14,tebhyaḥ sthitebhyaḥ sa tathāvidhebhyaḥ rūpeṇa bhāvena ca dāruṇebhyaḥ |na vivyathe nodvivije mahārṣiḥ krīḍan subālebhya ivoddhatebhyaḥ || 1336
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 37 Then one of them with his eyes rolling wildly lifted up a club against him but his arm with the club was instantly paralysed as was Indra’s of old with its thunderbolt 15,kaścittato raudravivṛttadṛṣṭistasmai gadāmudyamayāṁcakāra |tastaṁbha bāhuḥ sagadastato sya puraṁdarasyeva purā savajraḥ || 1337
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 38 Some having lifted up stones and trees found themselves unable to throw them against the sage down they fell with their trees and their stones like the roots of the Vindhya shattered by the thunderbolt,kecitsamudyamya śilāstarūṁśca viṣehire naiva munau vimoktum |petuḥ savṛkṣāḥ saśilāstathaiva vajrāvabhagnā iva viṁdhyapādāḥ || 1338
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 39 Others leaping up into the sky flung rocks trees and axes these remained in the sky and did not fall down like the many-coloured rays of the evening clouds,kaiścitsamutpatya nabho vimuktāḥ śilāśca vṛkṣāśca paraśvadhāśca |tasthurnabhasyeva na cāvapetuḥ saṁdhyābhrapādā iva naikavarṇāḥ || 1339
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 40 Another hurled upon him a mass of blazing straw as big as a mountain-peak which as soon as it was thrown while it hung poised in the sky was shattered into a hundred fragments by the sage’s power,cikṣepa tasyopari dīptamanyaḥ kaḍaṁgaraṁ parvataśṛṁgamātram |yanmuktamātraṁ gaganasthameva tasyānubhāvācchatadhā babhūva || 1340
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 41 One rising up like the sun in full splendour rained down from the sky a great shower of live embers as at the end of an aeon blazing Meru showers down the pulverised scoriae of the golden valleys,kaścijjvalannarka ivoditaḥ khādaṁgāravarṣaṁ mahadutsasarja |cūrnāni cāmīkarakaṁdarāṇāṁ kalpātyaye meruriva pradīptaḥ || 1341
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 42 But that shower of embers full of sparks when scattered at the foot of the Bodhi tree became a shower of red lotus-petals through the operation of the great saint’s boundless charity,tadbodhimūle pravikīryamāṇamaṁgāravarṣaṁ tu savisphuliṁgam |maitrīvihārādṛṣisattamasya babhūva raktotpalapatravarṣaḥ || 1342
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 43 But with all these various scorching assaults on his body and his mind and all these missiles showered down upon him the Śākya saint did not in the least degree move from his posture clasping firmly his resolution as a kinsman,śarīracittavyasanātapaistairevaṁvidhaistaiśca nipātyamānaiḥ |naivāsanācchākyamuniścacāla svaṁ niścayaṁ baṁdhumivopaguhya || 1343
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 44 Then others spat out serpents from their mouths as from old decayed trunks of trees but as if held fast by a charm near him they neither breathed nor discharged venom nor moved,athāpare nirjagalurmukhebhyaḥ sarpānvijīrṇebhya iva drumebhyaḥ |te maṁtrabaddhā iva tatsamīpe na śaśvasurnotsasṛjurna celuḥ || 1344
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 45 Others having become great clouds emitting lightning and uttering the fierce roar of thunderbolts poured a shower of stones upon that tree — but it turned to a pleasant shower of flowers,bhūtvāpare vāridharā vṛhaṁtaḥ savidyutaḥ sāśanicaṁḍaghoṣāḥ |tasmin drume tatyajuraśmavarṣaṁ tatpuṣpavarṣaṁ ruciraṁ babhūva || 1345
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 46 Another set an arrow in his bow — there it gleamed but it did not issue forth like the anger which falls slack 16 in the soul of an ill-tempered impotent man,cāpe tha vāṇo nihito pareṇa jajvāla tatraiva na niṣpapāta |anīśvarasyātmani dhūryamāṇo durmarṣaṇasyeva narasya manyuḥ || 1346
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 47 But five arrows shot by another stood motionless and fell not through the saint’s ruling guidance — like the five senses of him who is well experienced in the course of worldly objects and is afraid of embodied existence,paṁceṣavo nyena tu vipramuktāstasthurnayatyeva munau na petuḥ |saṁsārabhīrorviṣayapravṛttau paṁceṁdriyāṇīva parīkṣakasya || 1347
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 48 Another full of anger rushed towards the great saint having seized a club with a desire to smite him but he fell powerless without finding an opportunity like mankind in the presence of faults which cause failure 17,jighāṁsayānyaḥ prasasāra ruṣṭo gadāṁ gṛhītvābhimukho mahārṣeḥ |so prāptakālo vivaśaḥ papāta doṣeṣvivānarthakareṣu lokaḥ || 1348
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 49 But a woman named Meghakālī bearing a skull in her hand in order to infatuate the mind of the sage flitted about unsettled and stayed not in one spot like the mind of the fickle student over the sacred texts,strī meghakālī tu kapālahastā kartuṁ mahārṣeḥ kila mohacittam |babhrāma tatrāniyataṁ na tasthau calātmano buddhirivāgameṣu || 1349
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 50 Another fixing a kindling eye wished to burn him with the fire of his glance like a poisonous serpent but he saw the sage and lo he was not there like the votary of pleasure when true happiness is pointed out to him 18,kaścitpradīptaṁ praṇidhāya cakṣurnetrāgnināśīviṣavaddidhakṣuḥ |tatraiva nāsīttamṛṣiṁ dadarśa kāmātmakaḥ śreya ivopadiṣṭam || 1350
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 51 Another lifting up a heavy rock wearied himself to no purpose having his efforts baffled like one who wishes to obtain by bodily fatigue that condition of supreme happiness which is only to be reached by meditation and knowledge,gurvīṁ śilāmudyamayaṁstathānyaḥ śaśrāma moghaṁ vihataprayatnaḥ |niḥśreyasaṁ jñānasamādhigamyaṁ kāyaklamairdharmamivāptukāmaḥ || 1351
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 52 Others wearing the forms of hyenas and lions uttered loudly fierce howls which caused all beings round to quail with terror as thinking that the heavens were smitten with a thunderbolt and were bursting,tarakṣusiṁhākṛtayastathānye praṇeduruccairmahataḥ praṇādān |sattvāni yaiḥ saṁcukucuḥ samaṁtādvajrāhatā dyauḥ phalatīti matvā || 1352
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 53 Deer and elephants uttering cries of pain ran about or lay down — in that night as if it were day screaming birds flew around disturbed in all directions,mṛgā gajāścārttaravān sṛjaṁto vidudruvuścaiva nililyire ca |rātrau ca tasyāmahanīva digbhyaḥ khagā ruvaṁtaḥ paripeturārttāḥ || 1353
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 54 But amidst all these various sounds which they made although all living creatures were shaken the saint trembled not nor quailed like Garuḍa at the noise of crows,teṣāṁ praṇādaistu tathāvidhaistaiḥ sarveṣu bhūteṣvapi kaṁpiteṣu |munirna tatrāsa na saṁcukoca ravairgarutmāniva vāyasānām || 1354
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 55 The less the saint feared the frightful hosts of that multitude the more did Māra the enemy of the righteous continue his attacks in grief and anger,bhayāvahebhyaḥ pariṣadgaṇebhyo yathā yathā naiva munirbibhāya |tathā tathā dharmabhṛtāṁ sapatnaḥ śokācca roṣācca sasāra māraḥ || 1355
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 56 Then some being of invisible shape but of pre-eminent glory standing in the heavens — beholding Māra thus malevolent against the seer — addressed him in a loud voice unruffled by enmity,bhūtaṁ tataḥ kiṁcidadṛśyarūpaṁ viśiṣṭarūpaṁ gaganasthameva |dṛṣṭvārṣaye drugdhamavairaruṣṭaṁ māraṁ babhāṣe mahatā svareṇa || 1356
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 57 Take not on thyself O Māra this vain fatigue — throw aside thy malevolence and retire to peace 19 this sage cannot be shaken by thee any more than the mighty mountain Meru by the wind,moghaṁ śramaṁ nārhasi māra kartuṁ hiṁsrātmatāmutsṛja gaccha śarma |naiṣa tvayā kaṁpayituṁ hi śakyo mahāgirirmerurivānilena || 1357
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 58 Even fire might lose its hot nature water its fluidity earth its steadiness but never will he abandon his resolution who has acquired his merit by a long course of actions through unnumbered aeons,apyuṣṇabhāvaṁ jvalanaḥ prajahyādāpo dravatvaṁ pṛthivī sthiratvam |anekakalpācitapuṇyakarmā na tveva jahyādvyavasāyameṣaḥ || 1358
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 59 Such is that purpose of his that heroic effort that glorious strength that compassion for all beings — until he attains the highest wisdom he will never rise from his seat just as the sun does not rise without dispelling the darkness,yo niścayo hyasya parākramaśca tejaśca yadyā ca dayā prajāsu |aprāpya notthāsyati tattvameṣa tamāṁsyahatveva sahasraraśmiḥ || 1359
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 60 One who rubs the two pieces of wood obtains the fire one who digs the earth finds at last the water — and to him in his perseverance there is nothing unattainable — all things to him are reasonable and possible,kāṣṭhaṁ hi mathnan labhate hutāśaṁ bhūmiṁ khanan viṁdati cāpi toyam |nirbaṁdhinaḥ kiṁca na nāsya sādhyaṁ nyāyena yuktaṁ ca kṛtaṁ ca sarvam || 1360
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 61 Pitying the world lying distressed amidst diseases and passions he the great physician ought not to be hindered who undergoes all his labours for the sake of the remedy knowledge,tallokamārttaṁ karuṇāyamāno rogeṣu rāgādiṣu vartamānam |mahābhiṣagnārhati vighnameṣa jñānauṣadhārthaṁ parikhidyamānaḥ || 1361
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 62 He who toilsomely pursues the one good path when all the world is carried away in devious tracks — he the guide should not be disturbed like a right informant when the caravan has lost its way,hṛte ca loke bahubhiḥ kumārgaiḥ sanmārgamanvicchati yaḥ śrameṇa |sa daiśikaḥ kṣobhayituṁ na yuktaṁ sudeśikaḥ sārtha iva pranaṣṭe || 1362
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 63 He who is made a lamp of knowledge when all beings are lost in the great darkness — it is not for a right-minded soul to try to quench him — like a lamp kindled in the gloom of night,sattveṣu naṣṭeṣu mahāṁdhakārairjñānapradīpaḥ kriyamāṇa eṣaḥ |āryasya nirvāpayituṁ na sādhu prajvālyamānastamasīva dīpaḥ || 1363
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 64 He who when he beholds the world drowned in the great flood of existence and unable to reach the further shore strives to bring them safely across — would any right-minded soul offer him wrong,dṛṣṭvā ca saṁsāramaye mahaughe magnaṁ jagatpāramaviṁdamānam |yaścedamuttārayituṁ pravṛttaḥ kaścinnayettasya tu pāpamāryaḥ || 1364
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 65 The tree of knowledge whose roots go deep in firmness and whose fibres are patience — whose flowers are moral actions and whose branches are memory and thought — and which gives out the law as its fruit — surely when it is growing it should not be cut down,kṣamāśipho dhairyavigāḍhamūlaścāritrapuṣpaḥ smṛtibuddhiśākhaḥ |jñānadrumo dharmaphalapradātā notpāṭanaṁ hyarhati vardhamānaḥ || 1365
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 66 Him whose one desire is to deliver mankind bound in soul by the fast snares of illusion — thy wish to overthrow him is not worthy wearied as he is for the sake of unloosing the bonds of the world,baddhāṁ dṛḍhaiścetasi mohapāśairyasya prajāṁ mokṣayituṁ manīṣā |tasmin jighāṁsā tava nopapannā śrāṁte jagadbaṁdhanamokṣahetoḥ || 1366
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 67 To-day is the appointed period of all those actions which have been performed by him for the sake of knowledge — he is now seated on this seat just as all the previous saints have sat,bodhāya karmāṇi hi yānyanena kṛtāni teṣāṁ niyato dya kālaḥ |sthāne tathāsminnupaviṣṭa eṣa yathaiva pūrve munayastathaiva || 1367
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 68 This is the navel of the earth’s surface endued with all the highest glory there is no other spot of the earth than this — the home of contemplation the realm of well-being,eṣā hi nābhirvasudhātalasya kṛtsnena yuktā parameṇa dhāmnā |bhūmerato nyo sti hi na pradeśo veśaṁ samādherviṣayo hitasya || 1368
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 69 Give not way then to grief but put on calm let not thy greatness O Māra be mixed with pride it is not well to be confident — fortune is unstable — why dost thou accept a position on a tottering base’,tanmā kṛthāḥ śokamupehi śāṁtiṁ mā bhūnmahimnā tava māra mānaḥ |viśraṁbhituṁ na kṣamamadhruvā śrīścale pade kiṁ padamabhyupaiṣi || 1369
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 70 Having listened to his words and having seen the unshaken firmness of the great saint Māra departed dispirited and broken in purpose 20 with those very arrows by which O world thou art smitten in thy heart,tataḥ sa saṁśrutya ca tasya tadvaco mahāmuneḥ prekṣya ca niṣprakaṁpatām |jagāma māro vimanā hatodyamaḥ śarairjagaccetasi yairvihanyase || 1370
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 71 With their triumph at an end their labour all fruitless and all their stones straw and trees thrown away that host of his fled in all directions like some hostile army when its camp has been destroyed by the enemy,gatapraharṣā viphalīkṛtaśramā praviddhapāṣāṇakaḍaṁgaradrumā |diśaḥ pradudrāva tato sya sā camūrhatāśrayeva dviṣatā dviṣaccamūḥ || 1371
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, surabhi ca jalagarbhaṁ puṣpavarṣaṁ papāta || 1372,dravati saparapakṣe nirjite puṣpaketaujayati jitatamaske nīrajaske mahārṣau |
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 72 When the flower-armed god 21 thus fled away vanquished with his hostile forces and the passionless sage remained victorious having conquered all the power of darkness the heavens shone out with the moon like a maiden with a smile and a sweet-smelling shower of flowers fell down wet with dew,yuvatiriva sahāsā dyauścakāśe sacaṁdrāsurabhi ca jalagarbhaṁ puṣpavarṣaṁ papāta || 1372
https//bitly/2wZqxm8, 73 22When the wicked one thus fled vanquished the different regions of the sky grew clear the moon shone forth showers of flowers fell down from the sky upon the earth and the night gleamed out like a spotless maiden 23a 23b,tathāpi pāpīyasi nirjite gate diśaḥ praseduḥ prababhau niśākaraḥ |divo nipeturbhuvi puṣpavṛṣṭayo rarāja yoṣeva vikalmaṣā niśā | 1373*
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 1 Then having conquered the hosts of Māra by his firmness and calmness he the great master of meditation set himself to meditate longing to know the supreme end,tato mārabalaṁ jitvā dhairyeṇa ca śamena ca |paramārthaṁ vijijñāsuḥ sa dadhyau dhyānakovidaḥ || 141
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 2 And having attained the highest mastery in all kinds of meditation he remembered in the first watch the continuous series of all his former births,sarveṣu dhyānavidhiṣu prāpya caiśvaryamuttamam |sasmāra prathame yāme pūrvajanmaparaṁparām || 142
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 3 In such a place I was so and so by name and from thence I passed and came hither’ thus he remembered his thousands of births experiencing each as it were over again,amutrāhamayaṁ nāma cyutastasmādihāgataḥ |iti janmasahasrāṇi sasmārānubhavanniva || 143
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 4 And having remembered each birth and each death in all those various transmigrations the compassionate one then felt compassion for all living beings,smṛtvā janma ca mṛtyuṁ ca tāsu tāsūpapattiṣu |tataḥ sattveṣu kāruṇyaṁ cakāra karuṇātmakaḥ || 144
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 5 Having wilfully rejected the good guides in this life and done all kinds of actions in various lives this world of living beings rolls on helplessly like a wheel,kṛtveha svajanotsargaṁ punaranyatra ca kriyāḥ |atrāṇaḥ khalu loko yaṁ paribhramati cakravat || 145
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 6 As he thus remembered to him in his strong self-control came the conviction All existence is insubstantial like the fruit of a plantain’,ityevaṁ smaratastasya babhūva niyatātmanaḥ |kadalīgarbhaniḥsāraḥ saṁsāra iti niścayaḥ || 146
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 7 When the second watch came he possessed of unequalled energy received a pre-eminent divine sight like the highest of all sight-gifted beings,dvitīye tvāgate yāme so dvitīyaparākramaḥ |divyaṁ cakṣuḥ paraṁ lebhe sarvacakṣuṣmatāṁ varaḥ || 147
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 8 Then by that divine perfectly pure sight he beheld the whole world as in a spotless mirror,tatastena sa divyena pariśuddhena cakṣuṣā |dadarśa nikhilaṁ lokamādarśa iva nirmale || 148
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 9 As he saw the various transmigrations and rebirths of the various beings with their several lower or higher merits from their actions compassion grew up more within him,sattvānāṁ paśyatastasya nikṛṣṭotkṛṣṭakarmaṇām |pracyutiṁ copapattiṁ ca vavṛdhe karuṇātmatā || 149
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 10 These living beings under the influence of evil actions pass into wretched worlds — these others under the influence of good actions go forward in heaven,ime duṣkṛtakarmāṇaḥ prāṇino yāṁti durgatim |ime nye śubhakarmāṇaḥ pratiṣṭhaṁte tripiṣṭape || 1410
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 11 The one being born in a dreadful hell full of terrors are miserably tortured alas by many kinds of suffering,upapannāḥ pratibhaye narake bhṛśadāruṇe |amī duḥkhairbahuvidhaiḥ pīḍyaṁte kṛpaṇaṁ vata || 1411
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 12 Some are made to drink molten iron of the colour of fire others are lifted aloft screaming on a red-hot iron pillar,pāyyaṁte kvathitaṁ kecidagnivarṇamayorasam |āropyaṁte ruvaṁto nye niṣṭaptastaṁbhamāyasam || 1412
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 13 Others are baked like flour thrown with their heads downwards into iron jars others are miserably burned in heaps of heated charcoal,pacyaṁte piṣṭavatkecidayaskuṁbhīṣvavāṅmukhāḥ |dahyaṁte karuṇaṁ keciddīpteṣvaṁgārarāśiṣu || 1413
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 14 Some are devoured by fierce dreadful dogs with iron teeth others by gloating crows with iron beaks and all made as it were of iron,kecittīkṣṇairayodaṁṣṭrairbhakṣyaṁte dāruṇaiḥ śvabhiḥ |keciddhṛṣṭairayastuṁḍairvāyasairāyasairiva || 1414
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 15 Some wearied of being burned long for cold shade these enter like bound captives into a dark blue wood with swords for leaves,keciddāhapariśrāṁtāḥ śītacchāyābhikāṁkṣiṇaḥ |asipatraṁ vanaṁ nīlaṁ baddhā iva viśaṁtyamī || 1415
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 16 Others having many arms are split like timber with axes but even in that agony they do not die being supported in their vital powers by their previous actions,pāṭyaṁte dāruvat kecitkuṭhārairbahubāhavaḥ |duḥkhe pi na vipadyaṁte karmabhirdhāritāsavaḥ || 1416
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 17 Whatever deed was done only to hinder pain with the hope that it might bring pleasure its result is now experienced by these helpless victims as simple pain,sukhaṁ syāditi yatkarma kṛtaṁ duḥkhanivṛttaye |phalaṁ tasyedamavaśairduḥkhamevopabhujyate || 1417
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 18 These who did something evil for the sake of pleasure and are now grievously pained — does that old taste produce even an atom of pleasure to them now,sukhārthamaśubhaṁ kṛtvā ya ete bhṛśaduḥkhitāḥ |āsvādaḥ sa kimeteṣāṁ karoti sukhamaṇvapi || 1418
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 19 The wicked deed which was done by the wicked-hearted in glee — its consequences are reaped by them in the fulness of time with cries,hasadbhiryatkṛtaṁ karma kaluṣaṁ kaluṣātmabhiḥ |etatpariṇate kāle krośadbhiranubhūyate || 1419
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 20 If only evil doers could see the fruits of their actions they would vomit hot blood as if they were smitten in a vital part,yadyeva pāpakarmāṇaḥ paśyeyuḥ karmaṇāṁ phalam |vameyuruṣṇarudhiraṁ marmasvabhihatā iva || 1420
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 21 And worse still than all these bodily tortures in hell seems to me the association of an intelligent man with the base,śārīrebhyo pi duḥkhebhyo nārakebhyo manasvinaḥ |anāryaiḥ saha saṁvāso mama kṛcchratamo mataḥ || | 1421*
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 22 Others also through various actions arising from the spasmodic violence of their minds are born miserable in the wombs of various beasts,ime nye karmabhiścitraiścittavispaṁdasaṁbhavaiḥ |tiryagyonau vicitrāyāmupapannāstapasvinaḥ || 1422 (1421)
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 23 There the poor wretches are killed even in the sight of their kindred for the sake of their flesh their skin their hair or their teeth or through hatred or for mere pleasure,māṁsatvagbāladaṁtārthaṁ vairādapi madādapi |hanyaṁte kṛpaṇā yatra baṁdhūnāṁ paśyatāmapi || 1423 (1422)
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 24 Even though powerless and helpless oppressed by hunger thirst and fatigue they are driven along as oxen and horses their bodies wounded with goads,aśaknuvaṁto pyavaśāḥ kṣuttarṣaśramapīḍitāḥ |go śvabhūtāśca vāhyaṁte pratodakṣatamūrtayaḥ || 1424 (1423)
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 25 They are driven along when born as elephants by weaker creatures than themselves for all their strength — their heads tormented by the hook and their bodies kicked by foot and heel,vāhyaṁte gajabhūtāśca balīyāṁso pi durbalaiḥ |aṁkuśakliṣṭamūrdhānastāḍitāḥ pādapārṣṇibhiḥ || 1425 (1424)
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 26 And with all these other miseries there is an especial misery arising from mutual enmity and from subjection to a master,satsvapyanyeṣu duḥkheṣu duḥkhaṁ yatra viśeṣataḥ |parasparavirodhācca parādhīnatayaiva ca || 1426 (1425)
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 27 Air-dwellers are oppressed by air-dwellers the denizens of water by the denizens of water those that dwell on dry land are made to suffer by the dwellers on dry land in mutual hostility,khasthāḥ khasthairhi bādhyaṁte jalasthā jalacāribhiḥ |sthalasthāḥ sthalasaṁsthaistu prāpyaṁte cetaretaraiḥ || 1427 (1426)
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 28 And others there are who when born again with their minds filled with envy reap the miserable fruit of their actions in a world of the Pitṛs destitute of all light,upapannāstathā ceme mātsaryākrāṁtacetasaḥ |pitṛloke nirāloke kṛpaṇaṁ bhuṁjate phalam || 1428 (1427)
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 29 Having mouths as small as the eye of a needle and bellies as big as a mountain these miserable wretches are tortured with the pains of hunger and thirst,sūcīchidropamamukhāḥ parvatopamakukṣayaḥ |kṣuttarṣajanitairduḥkhaiḥ pīḍyaṁte duḥkhabhāginaḥ || 1429 (1428)
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 30 If a man only knew that such was the consequence of selfishness he would always give to others even pieces of his own body like Śibi,puruṣo yadi jānīta mātsaryasyedṛśaṁ phalam |sarvathā śivivaddadyāccharīrāvayavānapi || 1430 (1430)
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 31 Rushing up filled with hope but held back by their former deeds they try in vain to eat anything large however impure,āśayā samabhikrāṁtā ghāryamāṇāḥ svakarmabhiḥ |labhaṁte na hyamī bhoktuṁ pravṛddhānyaśucīnyapi || 1431 (1429)
https//bitly/2vJMCXN, 32 Others having found a hell in an impure lake called the womb are born amongst men and there suffer anguish,ime nye narakaṁ prāpya garbhasaṁjñe śucihrade |upapannā manuṣyeṣu duḥkhamarchaṁti jaṁtavaḥ || 1432 (1431)
